# AD INTERIM COMMITTEE TO STUDY THE NUMBER OF OFFICERS OF THE CHURCH (2-29)

"The Rev. Harold Borchert, Chairman of the Ad-Interim Committee to Study the Question of Ruling Elders Administering the Sacraments, who presented the Majority Report of the Committee (See pp. 176-179). Mr. Borchert in turn yielded the floor to the Rev. Basil Albert, who presented the Minority Report. The whole matter was referred to an Ad Interim Committee to Study the Question of the Number of Officers of the Church, and bring final recommendations on this issue to the General Assembly." (2-29).

"Overture 11 from the 1973 Assembly was committed to the Ad-Interim Committee to Study the Question of the Number of Officers of the Church (2-69). "The Ad Interim Committee to Study the Question of the Number of Officers of the Church was instructed to include the study of the office of assistant minister in its assignment" (2-70).

PART II JOURNAL
MINUTES FIRST DAY
TUESDAY

September 17, 1974
2-1 The Assembly Called to Order
The Second General Assembly of the National Presbyterian Church
meeting at the First Presbyterian Church, Macon, Georgia, was called
to order at 9:00 A.M. on Septmber 17, 1974, by the Moderator, Ruling
Elder W. Jack Williamson, who led the Assembly in an opening prayer.
2-2 Opening Worship
The retiring Moderator led the Assembly in a service of the worship of God, in which he preached the retiring Mocterator'·s sermon.
Following the sermon the Assembly observed the Lord's Supper, which
was conducted by the Rev. James E. Moore and the Rev. Sidney Anderson, assisted by the following Ruling Elders:
Ruling Elder Church Presbytery
Knox Fraley Eau Claire Calvary
Millard Tate Northside Carolina
Tom Alexander Vinevi!le Central Georgia
Earl Jaggers Johnson Memorial Covenant
J. E. Botsford First Presbyterian, Gadsden Evangel
C. G. Stokes, Jr. First NPC Mobile Gulf Coast
James H . Campbell Ref. Presb. Ch. of Tidewater Mid Atlantic
Harry B. McNeel First Ch., Louisville Mississippi Valley
Donald Redman Hixson Tennessee Valley
A.H. Burton Paris Texas
Ralph Bollinger Grace Covenant, Hampton Vanguard
John Fowler Greensboro Warrior
J. H. Bell York Warrior
Frank Clark Asbury Westminster

2-3 Report on Enrollment and Determination of a Quorum
The Stated Clerk announced the enrollment, which was then 213
Teaching Elders and 202 Ruling Elders.
The final enrollment of Commissioners is recorded as follows:
1. CALVARY PRESBYTERY

## 2-5 Election of the Moderator

The following rules of procedure for the election of a moderator were adopted:

1. The first order of business shall be the election of a Moderator. There shall be only one nominating speech not to exceed five minutes for each nominee. No seconding speeches shall be permitted.

2. If more than one Commissioner is nominated, election shall be by ballot, on ballots provided by the Stated Clerk. Tellers appointed by the Stated Clerk shall gather and count the ballots, and report the tabulation to the Stated Clerk. If no nominee receives a majority of the votes cast, a second ballot shall be called on the two nominees who receive the highest number of votes on the

<a id="ga02-p23"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=23 printed_page=null -->

first ballot. The Moderator shall declare an election when a nominee receives a majority of the votes cast by the commissioners present and voting.

3. As soon as a Moderator shall have been declared elected he shall assume his constitutional duties as Moderator.

Teaching Elder Erskine L. Jackson, pastor of the First Presbyterian Church of Kosciusko, Mississippi, was elected by acclamation, and he assumed the Chair.

## 2-6 Special Presentation to the Retiring Moderator

The Stated Clerk presented on behalf of the Assembly a beautifully framed copy of the “Message to all Churches of Jesus Christ Throughout the World from the General Assembly of the National Presbyterian Church,” which had been prepared by Ruling Elder Ligon Duncan of Greenville, South Carolina.

## 2-7 Election of Recording Clerks

Ruling Elder John E. Spencer of the Briarwood Presbyterian Church of Birmingham, Alabama, and Ruling Elder James W. Kemper of the Reformed Presbyterian Church (NPC) of Manassas, Virginia, were elected as Recording Clerks.

## 2-9 Welcome from the Host Church

The Rev. James M. Baird, Jr., pastor of the First Presbyterian Church of Macon welcomed the General Assembly to Macon. He sketched briefly the history of the Church, noting the fact that two previous General Assembly meetings had been held in the sanctuary.

## 2-10 Report of the Retiring Moderator

The retiring Moderator gave a brief report of the progress of the National Presbyterian Church since its First General Assembly. He presented the problem which has arisen during that time regarding the name “National Presbyterian Church.”

## 2-11 Resolution on the Change of Name

The following resolution was adopted by the Assembly, after being presented by Ruling Elders Jack Williamson, and Kenneth L. Ryskamp, legal counsel for the Church in this matter, to whom the privilege of the floor was granted:

<a id="ga02-p24"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=24 printed_page=null -->

Whereas, the First General Assembly of the National Presbyterian Church did in good faith adopt the name “National Presbyterian Church,” and

Whereas, since the First General Assembly, it has come to the attention of the Board of Directors of the National Presbyterian Church that there is a congregation of the United Presbyterian Church in the United States of America in the nation’s capital called by the name “National Presbyterian Church,” which congregation derives a portion of its support from across the nation and claims a nationwide ministry, and thus fears that our use of the same name will cause confusion in their support base, and

Whereas, representatives of the Washington congregation feel so strongly about this matter that they indicate they would resort to the civil courts, if necessary, to settle this issue, and

Whereas, our Lord teaches that “If any man will sue thee at the law, and take away thy cost, let him have thy cloak also. And whosoever shall compel thee to go a mile, go with him twain. Give to him that asketh thee, and from him that would borrow of thee turn not away” (Mt. 5:40-42),

Therefore, be it Resolved, by the Second General Assembly of the National Presbyterian Church that it change the name of the Church, in obedience to her Lord, and in love for our brethren in Christ of the National Presbyterian Church and Center of Washington, D. C.

## 2-12 Procedure for Name Change Approved

The Assembly adopted the following procedure for implementing the change of name: That the proposal of names for this denomination be the first order of business this afternoon, allowing one two minute speech with each name suggested. The vote and selection of the name to be finally made as the first order of business at the evening session tonight, requesting the afternoon hours to find us all in a deeply prayerful mood that this important issue be settled to the glory of God and the Honor of His Church. (See 2-24, 25, 45, 46, 49)

## 2-13 Rules for Assembly Operation Presented

Ruling Elder W. Jack Williamson, Chairman of the Special Committee on a Manual for Operation of the General Assembly presented the “Proposed Rules for Assembly Operations” as found in the Commissioners Handbook, pp. 6-11. (See Appendix A, pp. 89-94) (See 2-16)

## 2-18 Overtures Resolutions and Communications Referred

The Stated Clerk presented the following resolutions, communications and overtures, which were referred as indicated:

## OVERTURES TO THE 1974 GENERAL ASSEMBLY

### To the Committee of Commissioners on Bills and Overtures

##### Overture 1. From Rev. William Rose

FATHERS AND BRETHREN: To the General Assembly meeting in Macon, Ga. September 17, 1974

Whereas: One of the greatest needs facing the National Presbyterian Church is the need for laborers for the great white harvest field of over 3 billion people in the world: THE majority of whom do not know CHRIST, and multitudes have never heard HIS name:

Whereas: One of the greatest needs in the “National Presbyterian Church” is for laborers for the whitened harvest field.

Whereas: CHRIST said in Luke 10:2 THEREFORE SAID HE UNTO THEM. THE HARVEST TRULY IS GREAT. BUT THE LABOURERS ARE FEW: PRAY YE THEREFORE THE LORD OF THE HARVEST THAT HE WOULD SEND FORTH LABOURERS INTO HIS HARVEST.

Clearly letting us know that the way for believers to secure the necessary laborers is to PRAY TO THE LORD OF THE HARVEST TO SEND FORTH LABOURERS INTO HIS HARVEST.

Therefore: The General Assembly is overtured to:

1. Call to the attention of every session this great need of our fellowship.
2. Set aside a day, when the Sessions can bring Luke 10:2 before their people in any way that HE should lead them, the end result being that our people would begin to pray for Labourers, and GOD would call out labourers to work for CHRIST in the harvest field of the world.

William H. Rose, Jr.

##### Overture 3. From Rev. Eurie Hayes Smith, III et al

FATHERS AND BRETHREN: To the Reverend General Assembly, First Presbyterian Church, Macon, Georgia

Whereas certain branches of the Christian Church have limited or implied a limit to the free exercise of the conscience of its office bearers and membership by restricting them from secret associations and fraternities such as the Masonic order.

Now therefore, we respectfully overture the Second General Assembly of the National Presbyterian Church to affirm the right of its office bearers and constituency to hold such membership in accordance with the Westminster Confession of Faith chapters 20:II, and 22:I, II, VIIa.

Rev. Eurie Hayes Smith III
Rev. Edwin P. Elliott, Jr.
Junius W. Brown
H. H. Stillions

<a id="ga02-p26"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=26 printed_page=null -->

##### Overture 6. From First Presbyterian Church, Belzoni, Mississippi

**FATHERS AND BRETHREN**: The Reverend General Assembly, First Presbyterian Church, Macon, Georgia

The Session of the First Presbyterian Church respectfully overtures the Second General Assembly of the National Presbyterian Church meeting at Macon, Georgia on September 11, 1974, to cause to be prepared, in addition to those items in communication 4, Minutes of The First General Assembly, National Presbyterian Church (1973) p. 19, a Service Book of liturgical forms for the two higher courts. Such book shall provide for such matters as court communion, candidacy, licensure, ordination and installation, commissions, burial of ministers, dedications, chartering of congregations and so forth.

Rev. Eurie H. Smith III, Moderator

##### Overture 13. From Westminster Presbytery Adopted at its Meeting, July 20, 1974

We, the members of Westminster Presbytery, overture General Assembly to encourage the Theological Committee to consider the following adopted resolution:

### RESOLUTION ON THE BAPTISM OF THE HOLY SPIRIT

**Whereas** Matthew (3:11), Mark (1:8), Luke (3:16), and John (1:33) prophesy that Christ will baptize His Church with the Holy Spirit, and;

**Whereas** Acts 1:5 definitely says that the outpouring of the Holy Spirit at the Day of Pentecost fulfills this prophecy, and;

**Whereas** in Acts 11:16 Peter identifies Cornelius’ Holy Spirit baptism with that of the Day of Pentecost, and;

**Whereas** I Corinthians 12:13 (cf Galatians 3:27) categorically states that all Christians have been baptized with the Holy Spirit;

(These seven references being the only occurrences of the phrase, ‘baptized with the Spirit’, in the Scriptures.)

Therefore, be it concluded that:

1. To be baptized by the Spirit is to be joined to the body of Christ by His Spirit and therefore is experienced by all believers upon conversion.

2. Neo-Pentecostalism is in error in teaching that all Christians have not been baptized with the Spirit at conversion.

3. Neo-Pentecostalism is in error in teaching that tongue-speaking is the evidence of the baptism of the Holy Spirit.

4. It is unscriptural to pray for another Pentecost in the same sense in which it is unscriptural to pray for another Calvary.

5. We urge our brethren to be on guard against the teaching that a Christian should seek the baptism of the Holy Spirit to obtain a deeper Christian experience.

6. Further, we recommend the following bibliography:

- **a.** Anthony A. Hoekema, Holy Scripture Baptism
- **b.** Anthony A. Hoekema, What About Tongue-Speaking?
- **c.** Frederick Bruner, A Theology of the Holy Spirit

7. This is not intended to be a complete doctrinal statement on the Charismatic Movement. We are not saying anything about the validity of the “gifts of the Spirit” or “filling of the Holy Spirit” in this resolution.

### To the Committee of Commissioners on Judicial Business

##### Overture 4. From First Presbyterian Church, Belzoni, Mississippi

**FATHERS AND BRETHREN**: The Reverend General Assembly, First Presbyterian Church, Macon, Georgia

**Whereas** the nature of ordination and its several facets is not clear in the Book of Church Order,

Now, therefore, the Session of the First Presbyterian Church overtures the Second General Assembly to raise a competent committee of scholars and churchmen to study and to:

<a id="ga02-p27"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=27 printed_page=null -->

1. Affirm and declare the nature of ordination in the National Presbyterian Church to be functionary and strictly biblical,

2. Describe the limits to which Scripture permits ordination to be used
apart from the pastorate,

3. Review and clarify the concept of parity if Teaching Elders other than
full time pastors are to be permitted to serve on the committees of the higher
courts and have the franchise in those courts,

4. Clarify the matter of unordained personnel, their proper examination
and certification, the regulation of their work and the limits of women’s participation.

Rev. Eurie Hayes Smith, III, Moderator

##### Overture 5. From First Presbyterian Church, Belzoni, Mississippi

FATHERS AND BRETHREN: The Reverend General Assembly, First Presterian Church, Macon, Georgia

Whereas, the Book of Church Order provides for the examination and certification of every officer and member in our denomination, and

Whereas, the Book of Church Order also constitutes an examining committee
of the General Assembly which contradicts the above mentioned practice and
violates Presbyterian polity principles.

Now, therefore, the Session of the First Presbyterian Church respectfully overtures the Second General Assembly to remove that Section (lines 22-29) on page
23 of the Book of Church Order and thereby return these duties to the appropriate lower court.

Rev. Eurie Hayes Smith III, Moderator

##### Overture 7. Adopted by Warrior Presbytery at its Stated Meeting of May 21,

1974

Out of sincere concern for the well being of the National Presbyterian
Church and a desire to promote the peace and tranquility of the Church; Warrior Presbytery respectfully overtures the Second General Assembly of the National Presbyterian Church that:

Whereas: There are issues which have not been decided which directly affect
basic elements of the Book of Church Order such as:

1. Paragraph 7-1 of the form of Government.

2. The dropping of the inactive roll.

3. The question of rotation of officers.

4. The concept of total and complete parity of ruling and teaching elders
to include ruling elders as moderators of the sessions and to officiate at the
sacrament of Holy Communion.

5. The vital concern that the Book of Worship reflect Reformed Worship
more thoroughly.

__ 6. The consideration of the denomination’s whole attitude on church discipiine.

7. The controversy about evangelism.

Whereas: There are many who hold contrary opinions on these matters.

Whereas: There are many items of personal concern with differing elements
in the Book of Church Order which should be heard and considered fully by
the General Assembly.

Whereas: This section 27-2 of the form of Government if enacted would severely
limit the active discussion of these vital areas and apply pressure on the individuals and groups concerned to receive a hearing on their suggestions and recommendations at this assembly.

Be It Resolved: That section 27-2 of the form of Government of the Book of Church Order be suspended for a period of not less than five years.

## To the Committee of Commissioners on Mission to the World

##### Overture 9. From the Presbytery of Mississippi Valley adopted at its adjourned Meeting, June 20, 1974

Whereas, the National Presbyterian Church is committed to the Reformed Faith as set forth in the Westminster Standards, and

Whereas, the National Presbyterian Church is committed to carrying out the Great Commission as the chief mission of the Church, and

Whereas, the National Presbyterian Church as a denomination carries out its program activities through Permanent Committees of the Assembly, immediately responsible to the Assembly, and

Whereas, it is important that the National Presbyterian Church as it embarks on this world wide phase of sending the Gospel forth should do so by preaching the whole counsel of God as set forth in the Reformed Faith,

Now therefore, the Presbytery of Mississippi Valley overtures the Second General Assembly of the National Presbyterian Church to direct its Committee on Mission to the World to use care to see that all missionaries sent by the Assembly’s Committee be involved in propagating the Reformed Faith, either by working with already established Presbyterian and Reformed Churches, or, if no Reformed Church exists in the land to which they are sent, to seek to establish a Reformed witness there.

##### Overture 10. Adopted by the Presbytery of Mississippi Valley at its Adjourned Meeting, June 20, 1974

Whereas the Book of Church Order of the N.P.C. calls for the ordination and commissioning of some to be evangelists in foreign countries (#8-3,6) and

Whereas Presbyteries alone have the authority to examine and ordain those called into the ministry (#14-5,7), and

Whereas the General Assembly is responsible to encourage and promote the fulfilment of this mission by the various courts (#15-1), and

Whereas the Assembly’s committees are to serve and not to direct any church judicatories and are to serve the church (#15-1,7,8),

Be it resolved that Presbyteries are to examine, ordain, and appoint those who are to serve as evangelists on the foreign field and through licensure approve all lay personnel who are to go to the field; and

That the responsibility for the support of such evangelists and their work, ordained or lay, is the responsibility of the Presbytery which ordains them and commissions them to this task; and

That the missionary evangelist so commissioned is directly responsible to, and is to give full account of his work to his Presbytery; and

That the special oversight of the missionary evangelist’s work shall rest in the hands of the Mission to the World Committee of the Presbytery which shall have as its duties to promote the mission of the church to the world, challenge men and women to give their lives in service to this work, raise support for those called and commissioned by the Presbytery and continue to be in correspondence with them throughout their term of service; and

That missionary evangelists must strive to adjust to the language and culture of the land where they are to serve beginning as soon after their call to this work as is possible; and

That missionary evangelists ought to do their work in the foreign field within the framework of the existing national church insofar as that church’s doctrine is compatible with the doctrine of the NPC and ought not to estab-

<a id="ga02-p29"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=29 printed_page=null -->

lish an extra-church organization on the foreign field where such churches exist; and

That the NPC Mission to the World committee ought to exist to serve the Presbyteries in their carrying out of the Great Commission by aiding in the equipping of missionaries for their task, arranging for and informing of passage to the field, informing of needs in various parts of the world, receiving and distributing to the Presbyteries funds received for the proclamation of the gospel in foreign fields, carrying out of general promotion of the church's task in foreign missions and so forth; and

That the Assembly's Committee on the Mission to the World is to be composed of the chairmen of the Presbyteries' Committees on the Mission to the World in order that the work between the various Presbyteries and the National Committee be properly coordinated.

##### Overture 11. From Westminster Presbytery, Adopted at its Meeting July 20, 1974

We, the members of Westminster Presbytery, solemnly overture General Assembly to encourage the Mission to the World Committee to be carefully Biblical in its use of women on the mission field, particularly as regards evangelism, preaching, and church development; remembering Paul's admonition to Timothy (I Timothy 2:12):

&gt; "But I do not allow a woman to teach or exercise authority over a man, but to remain quiet." NASB

##### Overture 12. From Westminster Presbytery Adopted at its Meeting, July 20, 1974

We, the members of Westminster Presbytery, overture General Assembly to exhort the Committee of Mission to the World to discontinue, in the immediate future, all ties and cooperation with any agency or arm of the World Council of Churches, or with any affiliation thereof.

**Overture No. 15. From Warrior Presbytery**

Whereas, the National Presbyterian Church has repeatedly stated in publications and pronouncements that it does not belong to nor support the National and/or World Councils of Churches, and,

Whereas, the First General Assembly of the National Presbyterian Church did instruct the denomination's Committee on Mission to the United States not to conduct any joint work with any denomination which is a member of the National and/or World Councils of Churches,

Therefore, be it resolved that Warrior Presbytery respectfully overtures the Second General Assembly of the National Presbyterian Church to instruct the denomination's Committee on Mission to the World not to send any missionaries to work with denominations in foreign countries if that denomination is a member of the World Council of Churches.

Therefore, be it resolved that Warrior Presbytery respectfully overtures the Second General Assembly of the National Presbyterian Church to instruct the denomination's Committee on Mission to the World not to send any missionaries to work with denominations in foreign countries if that denomination is a member of the World Council of Churches.

Whereas, the National Presbyterian Church has repeatedly stated in publications and pronouncements that it does not belong to nor support the National and/or World Councils of Churches,

<a id="ga02-p30"></a>

denominations Committee on Mission to the World not to give financial support to any native minister or church in a foreign country where the minister and/or church are members of a denomination which belongs to the World Council of Churches.

## Overture No. 18. From Warrior Presbytery

Whereas, the National Presbyterian Church has repeatedly stated in publications and pronouncements that it does not belong to nor support the National and/or World Council of Churches,

Therefore, be it resolved that Warrior Presbytery respectfully overtures the Second General Assembly of the National Presbyterian Church to instruct the denomination's Committee on Mission to the World to instruct all National Presbyterian Church missionaries not to affiliate through any kind of membership with any Presbytery of a national church which is a part of a denomination that belongs to the World Council of Churches and to instruct any missionaries who may presently be affiliated with Presbyteries of native denominations which belong to the World Council of Churches to immediately terminate their affiliation.

## Overture No. 19. From Warrior Presbytery

Whereas, the National Presbyterian Church from its inception has stated its purpose to glorify God by being a denomination truly Reformed in its doctrine, worship, and work, and

Whereas, the National Association of Evangelicals is not nor does it claim to be Reformed in its doctrine and practice,

Therefore, be it resolved that Warrior Presbytery respectfully overtures the Second General Assembly of the National Presbyterian Church to instruct its Committee on Mission to the World to terminate its membership in the National Association of Evangelicals before the meeting of the Third General Assembly.

## Overture No. 20. From Warrior Presbytery

Whereas, the National Presbyterian Church from its inception has stated its purpose to glorify God by being a denomination truly Reformed in its doctrine, worship, and work, and,

Whereas, the Committee on Mission to the World of the National Presbyterian Church has expressed its desire to send personnel and funds to said personnel through organizations which are not Reformed and in many instances which are not a part of the Church as such, but are at best extra-Church organizations,

Therefore, be it resolved that Warrior Presbytery respectfully overtures the Second General Assembly of the National Presbyterian Church to instruct its Committee on Mission to the World to formulate a program of world missions for the National Presbyterian Church which is truly Reformed and present a strategy for implementing a Reformed program of world missions to the Third General Assembly of the National Presbyterian Church.

## Overture No. 21. From Warrior Presbytery

Whereas, the National Presbyterian Church from its inception has stated its purpose to glorify God by being a denomination truly Reformed in its doctrine, worship, and work, and,

Whereas, the Committee on Mission to the World of the National Presbyterian Church has expressed its intention to send National Presbyterian Church missionary personnel to foreign fields under the auspices of extra-Church organizations and to fund such personnel through these organizations,

Therefore, be it resolved that Warrior Presbytery overtures the Second General Assembly of the National Presbyterian Church to instruct the denomination's Committee on Mission to the World to send all missionary personnel directly on the field under the auspices of the National Presbyterian Church and/or any other Reformed Church.

# To the Ad-Interim Committee on Constitutional Documents

##### Overture 2. From the McIlwain Memorial Church, Pensacola

The Session of McIlwain Memorial Presbyterian Church submits the following overture to the 2nd General Assembly of the National Presbyterian Church for their consideration and adoption.

RE: Part III of the BCO, THE DIRECTORY FOR THE WORSHIP OF GOD.

Page 88 Ch 6, #6-7, Lines 17 and 18

Page 90 Ch. 9, #9-1, Lines 22 and 23

Whereas it is explicitly set forth in the Book of Church Order that the jurisdiction over a particular church is a joint power lodged in the hands of the church Session (Page 7, Ch 4, #4-3, Lines 1-3), and,

Whereas the Ruling Elders are to have the government and spiritual oversight of the church (Page 9, Ch 7, #7-2) and,

Whereas the Teaching Elder is, with the other elders, to exercise the joint power of government (Page 10, Ch 8, #8-4, Lines 28 and 29), and,

Whereas the Ruling Elders, in conjunction with the pastors or ministers, are to take the oversight of the spiritual interests of the particular church, and exercise government and discipline (Page 12, Ch 9, #9-4), and,

Whereas the Session is to have the power to establish rules for government, discipline, worship, and extension of the church (Page 15, Ch 12, #12-2, Lines 20-21) 23-27), and,

Whereas the church Session is to determine the best measures for promoting the spiritual interest of the church and congregation (Page 18, Ch 13., #13-6, lines and,

Whereas in the Directory for the Worship of God (page 88, Ch 6, #6-7) the statement that “No person should be invited to preach in any of the National Presbyterian Churches without the consent of the pastor or Session,” and a similar statement (Page 90, Ch. 9, #9-1, Lines 22 and 23) divests the Session of its assigned rights, prevents the Session in this most important area, from exercising its responsibility of the spiritual oversight of a particular church, and,

Whereas the government, discipline, and spiritual oversight of a church are inseparably tied together and are adversely affected by the fact that a Session cannot exercise any jurisdiction over who will be invited to preach.

Therefore, the Session of McIlwain Memorial Presbyterian Church respectfully requests the 2nd General Assembly of the National Presbyterian Church to amend Part III, Directory for the Worship of God of the Book of Church as follows:

Ch 6, #6-7, to read, “No person is to be invited to preach in any of the National Presbyterian Churches or occupy the time set aside for the preaching of the Word, without prior consent of the Session.” and, Ch 9, #9-1, Line 23, to read, “Any other person must be approved by the Session.”

John R. Massey
Clerk of Session

Attest:
Donald A. Dunberley
Moderator

## Overture No. 14. From the Presbytery of Mississippi Valley enacted at its regular meeting on September 10, 1974.

Whereas, the Book of Church Order of the National Presbyterian Church provides the use of licensure for both candidates for the ministry and for ruling elders, who desire to preach regularly in National Presbyterian Church congregations,

Whereas, no provision has been made regarding the possibility of students or others from outside the National Presbyterian Church being examined and permitted to preach either occasionally or on a regular basis in the National Presbyterian Church, and

Whereas, the Presbytery of Mississippi Valley has cases of ministers, students and others from outside the National Presbyterian Church desirous of such permission,

<a id="ga02-p32"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=32 printed_page=null -->

Therefore, the Presbytery of Mississippi Valley hereby overtures the General Assembly of the National Presbyterian Church to clarify the matter of licensure and permission to preach in National Presbyterian congregations by making the following changes in the Book of Church Order:

1. To restrict the use of licensure only to candidates for the Gospel Ministry in the National Presbyterian Church and Ruling Elders of the Presbytery.
2. To provide for the examination and/or consultation with non-National Presbyterian ministers, who desire to preach with regularity in the National Presbyterian Church, and that upon satisfying the Presbytery as to their doctrinal soundness, and their willingness to comply with the government of the National Presbyterian Church, they may be approved for such service for such periods of time that the Presbytery may deem wise.
3. To provide for the examination of non-National Presbyterian students and others who desire to preach regularly in the National Presbyterian congregations and that upon satisfying the Presbytery as to their doctrinal soundness and their willingness to comply with the government of the National Presbyterian Church, they may be approved for such service for such periods of time as the Presbytery may deem wise.

## RESOLUTIONS

### To the Committee of Commissioners on Bills and Overtures

**Resolution 1 Adopted by the Presbytery of Mississippi Valley at its Adjourned Meeting, June 20, 1974, and ordered sent to the General Assembly**

**Whereas** God's word teaches us that the church is not a loosely knit federation of independent churches but rather the body of Christ "fitly framed and knit together through that which every joint supplieth"; and

**Whereas** the Book of Church Order #1-5 describes the courts as sustaining "such mutual relations as to realize the idea of the unity of the Church"; and

**Whereas** the Book of Church Order #12-4 declares that "these courts are not separate and independent tribunals, but they have a mutual relation, and every act of jurisdiction is the act of the whole Church" and

**Whereas** the Presbytery consists of all the Teaching Elders and churches within its bounds (BCO #14-1); and

**Whereas** the courts "have no power to inflict temporal pains and penalties, but their authority is in all respects moral or spiritual" (BCO #12-1,2; #3-6); and

**Whereas** "this Scriptural doctrine of Presbytery is necessary to the perfection of the order of the visible church, but is not essential to its existence" (BCO #1-7);

### Be it therefore resolved

1. That the individual churches of this Presbytery are not independent nor are they a loosely bound federation but rather are committed together to serve Christ and to labor for the mutual good and peace of the whole body; and
2. That while not under threat of the loss of property or any other such temporal punishment, they are, however, in joining this Presbytery under commitment to Christ first and to one another second to labor for the continued unity and mutual good of the whole body; and
3. That no individual congregation or minister who is a member of this Presbytery should consider separation or withdrawal from the Presbytery as an easy solution when differences should arise but rather should pledge themselves to strive for continued unity and harmony in subjection to the brethren until such time as to do so would be in violation of God's Word; and
4. That all individual congregations and ministers who are members or shall become members of this Presbytery do pledge themselves, in harmony with the prayer of our Lord, to labor for the continued unity and harmony of this Presbytery and for the mutual blessing of all its members in accord with the will of God for our sanctification.

**Resolution 2 Adopted by the Trustees of the Annuity Fund, June 25, 1974**

**Whereas**, the General Assembly of the National Presbyterian Church has pro-

<a id="ga02-p33"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=33 printed_page=null -->

vided an excellent retirement program for its ministers which it considers to be,
overall, superior to any individually funded program; and

Whereas, the most efficient and most productive operation of that retirement
program requires the fullest participation on the part of the ministers and congregations of the National Presbyterian Church; and,

Whereas, the servants of Christ in the National Presbyterian Church should
have their financial security in their old age made sure by such a retirement
program; therefore,

Be it Resolved, that the General Assembly of the National Presbyterian Church
encourage and urge all of its ministers and congregations to participate in the
denominationally sponsored retirement program, and,

Be it Further Resolved, that the General Assembly urge all the presbyteries
of the national presbyterian church to establish a policy of requiring participation in the denominational ly sponsored retirement and medical insurance programs in the term sofa call to a minister.

Recommendatians of the Trustees of the Annuity Fund

1. That all participants in the Annuity Plan be participants in the Social Security program.

2. That the beneficiaries of death benefits and of the long term disability insurance policies be changed to the Trustees for the Insurance and Annuity Fund
of the National Presbyterian Church.

To the Committee of Commissioners on the Board of Directors

Resolution 3 From Rev. Thomas A. Cook, First Presbyterian Church, Louisville,
Mississippi

Whereas, The National Presbyterian Church has come into being because of the
desire of her members to return to a more Biblical form of Church governance.

Whereas, the Minutes of the First General Assembly indicate that there is now
at the Assembly level a duplication of structure, with an “ecclesiastical” and a
“corporate” structure,

Whereas the Corporation structure of the National Presbyterian Church provides for a Board of Directors, which is, in effect, a ruling body between General
Assemblies, for which there is no Scriptural warrant,

Whereas, The National Presbyterian Church is yet in its formative stages, and
it would be better to have some of her Committees making mistakes, instead of
creating a faulty structure that could ultimately be destructive to the very aims
for which the Church was formed.

Now Therefore Be It Resolved, that the present Corporation By Laws be suspended, and that a special Committee of non-Asembly personnel be appointed
to study the whole matter of the Assembly operation and structures,

Be It Further Resolved, that the Second General Assembly assign to the Committee on Administration all of the business affairs of the General Assembly,
and that the Board of Directors be named a Board of Trustees to hold title to
properties belonging to the Assembly, with powers similar to those assigned
congregational Trustees in the Book of Church Order 26-7.

Be It Further Resolved, that the Second General Assembly directs that there
be at least three meetings of the following persons between Assembly meetings
for the purpose of coordination of the Church’s work at the Assembly level:
the Chairmen of the Permanent Committees, two representatives (one ruling
and one teaching elder) of each of the Permanent Committees as elected by
the Committees, the Coordinators of each Committee, the Business Administrator, the Stated Clerk and the Moderator of the Assembly. Such meetings will
be for the purpose of exchange of information, the discussion of ways and
means of handling particular matters, but without power to act, other than to
recommend action to the Permanent Committees or directly to the General Assembly. The Stated Clerk shall keep a record of the minutes of these meetings,
which shall be reported to the General Assembly.

Rev. Thomas A. Cook
Louisville, Mississippi

<a id="ga02-p34"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=34 printed_page=null -->

### Resolution 5 From the Session and Congregation of the Monte Sano Presbyterian Church, Baton Rouge, Louisiana

The Session and Congregation of the Monte Sano Presbyterian Church of Baton Rouge, Louisiana respectfully request the Ad Interim Committee — To Recommend Presbytery Boundaries, to include the Monte Sano Presbyterian Church within the boundaries of the “Louisiana Presbytery”.

## COMMUNICATIONS TO THE 1974 GENERAL ASSEMBLY

### Referred to the Committee of Commissioners on Administration

**Communication No. 3** From the Second Presbyterian Church of Greenville, South Carolina, to the General Assembly of the National Presbyterian Church, dated September 9, 1974.

**Fathers and Brethren:**

The Session of the Second Presbyterian Church extends an invitation to the General Assembly of the National Presbyterian Church to hold its Fourth Stated Meeting in 1976 in Greenville, South Carolina.

We hereby commit ourselves to renting the Memorial Auditorium for this purpose at no expense to the General Assembly. This facility is well suited to a General Assembly meeting and will seat upwards to 2,000 commissioners on the main floor with balcony space for additional 4,500 observers and visitors. There is also ample room for committees and Presbyteries to hold their meetings and for a noon meal to be catered. The parking is more than adequate for the meeting.

Greenville is known as a convention center in the southeast and has more than adequate motel and hotel accommodations. The airport is served by two major airlines and Interstate Highway 85 is easy access for surface traveling.

A large number of our constituent churches are within easy traveling distance from Greenville, which is within the bounds of Calvary Presbytery, one of the larger Presbyteries of the National Church. We pledge ourselves to make every effort for a successful, smoothly run General Assembly meeting, and we sincerely hope that you will accept our offer.

Sincerely,

SESSION, SECOND PRESBYTERIAN CHURCH
By: John I. Smith, Clerk
By: Gordon K. Reed, Moderator

Dr. Morton Smith, Stated Clerk

The First General Assembly of the National Presbyterian Church directed the Assembly's Committee on Mission to the United States to “provide strategy papers” for the direction of those desiring to begin National Presbyterian Churches. In response to that directive the Committee on Mission to the United States has prayerfully prepared a modest booklet entitled “... I Will Build My Church ...” the booklets are free and available at the M US display. Additional copies may be obtained from the M US office in Jackson, Mississippi.

## Communication 6. From Presbyterians Church of Australia, 8 Park Road, Cheltenham 3192

To: Clerk of the Assembly, National Presbyterian Church.

The General Assembly of the Presbyterian Church of Australia continuing in session following a decision of the majority on the first day of May, 1974 anent corporate union —

Greetings: Grace, mercy and peace be multiplied unto you. It may be known to you that upon the above mentioned date a resolution was adopted by the General Assembly of the Presbyterian Church of Australia to enter into union with the Methodist Church of Australia and such Congregational Churches as had agreed to unite.

As a result of the passing of this resolution the members of this Assembly withdrew from the majority and are continuing as the General Assembly of the Presbyterian Church of Australia provided for in the constitution of our Church. Otherwise we should have been in subjection to church courts themselves under the paramount obligation to facilitate the union on a basis we firmly believe to be inconsistent with the positions we are pledged to uphold as Presbyterians.

We regret our separation from our brethren brought about by this decision

<a id="ga02-p36"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=36 printed_page=null -->

to enter union and have no spirit of hostility to those who so resolved. Since we constitute no changed position from that which the constitution of the Presbyterian Church of Australia has required down the years to be maintained, and our right to the name “Presbyterian Church of Australia” is recognized by Acts of the Parliament of each of the six Australian States, we most sincerely hope for a continuance of those good relations we have hitherto enjoyed with the other Presbyterian Churches of the World.

Neil MacLeod, Moderator                                      E. R. Pearsons, Clerk
28th May, 1974

## To the Ad-Interim Committee on Constitutional Documents

### Communication 1. From First Presbyterian Church, Jackson, MS

To: Members of the Second General Assembly of the National Presbyterian Church at Macon, Georgia, September 16-20, 1974.

At a duly constituted regular monthly meeting of our Session at seven o’clock Monday evening, May 6, 1974, the following recommendations for changes in the National Presbyterian Church Book of Church Order as Adopted by the First General Assembly 1973 and Amended were approved.

The Moderator and Clerk were instructed to place the recommendations in the hands of the General Assembly’s State Clerk with a request that they be considered by the Second General Assembly and approved if deemed to be in order.

Donald B. Patterson, Moderator                                      Ralph L. Landrum, Clerk

| --- | --- | --- |
|  1. | Page 2 Line 18 | Change “beside it” to read “in addition to”.  |
|  2.a. | Page 3 Line 12 | “Truth is in order to goodness” is vague and obscure. Should be revised for clarity.  |
|  b. | Line 15 | Change after “represents” to read “that the opinions of man are of no consequences”.  |
|  3. | Page 4 Line 4 | Substitute “church courts” for “synods”.  |

## Communication 2. From Granada Presbyterian Church, Coral Gables, Fla.

The Session of Granada Presbyterian Church, Coral Gables, Florida, a member of the Presbytery of Southern Florida, makes the following recommendations with reference to Part III, The Directory for the Worship of God in the National Presbyterian Church, as contained in the Book of Church Order beginning on page 84A.

Page 88, line 6, paragraph 6-4, now reads: "Each minister should preach one sermon each week on the Confession of Faith or the Catechisms."

**Recommendation**: "Each minister should preach periodically on the Confession of Faith or the Catechisms."

Page 88, line 14, paragraph 6-6 now reads: "After the sermon, the minister should ordinarily offer a prayer to Almighty God, let a psalm or hymn be sung, then dismiss the congregation with the benediction."

**Recommendation**: "After the sermon, the minister should ordinarily offer a prayer to Almighty God, then dismiss the congregation with the benediction."

Page 88, line 17, paragraph 6-7 now reads: "No person should be invited to preach in any of the National Presbyterian churches without the consent of the pastor or Session."

**Recommendation**: No person should be invited to preach in any of the National Presbyterian churches without the consent of the Session."

Page 88, line 20, paragraph 7-1 now reads: "The holy Scriptures teach that God is the owner of all persons and all things and that we are but stewards of both life and possessions; that God's ownership and our stewardship should be acknowledged; that this acknowledgement should take the form, in part, of giving a worthy proportion of our income to the Church of Jesus Christ, thus worshipping the Lord with our possessions."

**Recommendation**: "The holy Scriptures teach that God is the owner of all persons and all things and that we are but stewards of both life and possession; that God's ownership and our stewardship should be acknowledged; that this acknowledgement should take the form, in part of giving at least a tithe of our income to the Church of Jesus Christ, thus worshipping the Lord with our possessions."

Page 88, line 26, paragraph 7-2 now reads: "It is both a privilege and a duty, plainly enjoined in the Bible, to make regular, weekly, systematic and

<a id="ga02-p41"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=41 printed_page=null -->

proportionate offerings for the support of religion and for the propagation of the Gospel in our own and foreign lands, and for the relief of the poor.”

**Recommendation:** “It is both a privilege and a duty, plainly enjoined in the Bible, to make regular, weekly, systematic and proportionate offerings for the support of Christianity and for the propagation of the Gospel in our own and foreign lands, and for the relief of the poor.”

Page 90, line 21, paragraph 9-1 (last sentence in paragraph) **now reads:** “They should be conducted by the pastor, or by some member of the Session, or by any duly qualified member of the church, or by any other person who has been invited by the pastor or Session.”

**Recommendation:** “They should be conducted by the pastor, or by some member of the Session, or by any duly qualified member of the church, or by any other person who has been invited by the Session.”

Page 91, line 10, paragraph 10-1 **now reads:** “It is the duty and privilege of parents to delicate their children to God in baptism, thereby claiming God’s covenant promises to parents and children.”

**Recommendation:** “It is the duty and privilege of Christian parents to dedicate their children to God in baptism, thereby claiming God’s covenant promises to parents and children.”

Page 91, line 20, paragraph 10-4 **now reads:** “After previous notice is given to the minister, the child to be baptized is to be presented, by one or both of the parents, or some other responsible person, signifying the desire that the child be baptized.”

**Recommendation:** “After previous notice is given to the minister, the child to be baptized is to be presented, by one or both of Christian parents, or some other responsible Christian person, signifying the desire that the child be baptized.”

Page 92, line 24, paragraph 10-6(3) **now reads:** “Do you unreservedly dedicate your child to God, and promise, in humble reliance upon divine grace, that you will endeavor to set before (him) a godly example, that you will pray with and for (him), that you will teach (him) the doctrines of our holy religion, and that you will strive, by all the means of God’s appointment, to bring (him) up in the nurture and admonition of the Lord?”

**Recommendation:** “Do you unreservedly dedicate your child to God, and promise, in humble reliance upon divine grace, that you will endeavor to set before (him) a godly example, that you will pray with and for (him), that you will teach (him) the doctrines of our holy religion, and that you will strive by all means of God’s appointment, to bring (him) up in the nurture and admonition of the Lord to the end that he may confess Christ as his Lord and Savior?”

Page 98, line 7, paragraph 13-4 **now reads:** “The parties should be of such years of discretion as to be capable of making their own choice; and if they be under age, or live with their parents, the consent of the parents or others under whose care they are should be previously obtained, and well certified to the minister before he proceeds to solemnize the marriage.”

**Recommendation:** “The parties should be of such years of discretion as to be capable of making their own choice; and if they be under age, the consent of the parents or others under whose care they are should be previously obtained, and well certified to the minister before he proceeds to solemnize the marriage.”

The above recommendations were unanimously adopted by the Session of Granda Presbyterian Church in meeting assembled on May 19, 1974.

Attested:
Robert J. Ostenson, Moderator
Charles A. Kimbrell, Clerk of Session

# ITEMS OF BUSINESS CARRIED OVER FROM THE FIRST GENERAL ASSEMBLY

## 1-79 Theological Committee

The Constitutional Documents Committee recommended that the Assembly establish a Theological Committee to study the matter of Scripture proofs for the Confession and Catechisms; that the Assembly authorize this Committee to consult with the Orthodox Presbyterian Church and other denominations who may be interested in such a study with us. The Constitutional Documents Committee does not envision that the Scripture proofs would become a part of the Constitution itself, but that they be approved, when agreed upon, to be printed with our Constitution. This would allow for the addition of new proof texts, without the complex procedure of having to amend the Constitution.

On recommendation of the Nominating Committee, the Constitutional Documents Committee was charged with this matter. The Committee is as follows: Rev. Charles Dunahoo, Chairman, Rev. Donald Patterson, Rev. Frank Barker, Rev. Morton Smith, Ruling Elder John Barnes.

## 1-80 Report of the Standing Theological Committee

3. Concerning Overture 9 (page 20.); that this overture be answered in the affirmative; that an Ad interim committee be appointed to study all aspects of Reformed Worship, considering with care communication 4; and that this committee work in conjunction with the Constitutional Documents Committee, reporting its findings to the Second General Assembly of the National Presbyterian Church.

##### Overture 9. From Covenant Presbytery

That an ad-interim committee be appointed to study aspects of Reformed Worship.

### Communication 4. From the Rev. Eurie Hayes Smith, III

To: The General Assembly

Fathers and Brethren:

The General Assembly of the Continuing Presbyterian Church meeting in Birmingham, Alabama, on December 4, 1973, is herewith respectfully overtured:

1. To investigate and publish to the Congregations of the Continuing Presbyterian Church the rich spirit filled, but neglected heritage of Reformed Worship and,
2. To contrast this with the many non-Reformed liturgies presently in use among us and,
3. To provide a Reformed Liturgy and a Reformed psalter (including hymns and other appropriate music) that clearly exists in our faith, and,
4. To recommend to the ministers what constitutes proper pulpit (liturgical) dress for Reformed pastors and,
5. To recommend to the congregations what constitutes proper architecture as exhibits the Reformed Christian faith truly, accurately and majestically and,
6. To demonstrate by its attention to those matters that for the Reformed Faith, faithful, true, biblical worship in the Church is as important as the Great Commission to the world.

Eurie Hayes Smith, III

## 1-81 Constitutional Documents Committee

2. That Overture 11 (page 21) be referred to the Constitutional Documents Committee for report to the Second General Assembly.

##### Overture 11. From McIlwain Memorial Presbyterian Church, Pensacola, Florida

Whereas, there is not to be any differentiation between the office of ruling elder

<a id="ga02-p43"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=43 printed_page=null -->

and teaching elder (minister of the Word), and each is given equal authority in church government according to the Scriptures *(Book of Church Order, III, page 20)*;

Whereas, the power of jurisdiction is to be equally exercised by ruling and teaching elders (ministers), but jointly in church courts (Book of Church Order, 1-4, 3-3, pages 22 and 23);

Whereas, the Minister of the Word and the ruling elder are to share equally in the governing of the church (Book of Church Order, 9-3 page 32);

Whereas, Christ has furnished others (ruling elders), besides the Minister of the Word, with gifts and commissions to govern when called and ordained thereto (Book of Church Order, 11-1, page 35);

Whereas, in all courts of the church the ruling elders possess the same authority and the same eligibility to office as the Minister of the Word (Book of Church Order, 11-2, page 35);

Whereas, the Session is the only court that is denied the right to elect its own moderator;

Whereas, the office of Moderator of Session is the only office in the entire Presbyterian Church system of government to which an elder cannot be elected: and that in his own particular church;

Whereas, the requirement that the Minister be the Moderator of Session (Book of Church Order, 13-2, page 38) denies the ruling elder (1) the exercise of his gifts and commission to rule; (2) to share equally in the governing of the church; (3) the same eligibility to office as the Minister of the Word and differentiates between the teaching and ruling elder in matters of church government — all contrary to the Book of Church Order. Furthermore, the principle implies ruling elders are not capable of moderating the Session (Book of Church Order, 15-4, page 42);

Whereas, the appointment of a moderator of a session by a presbytery when a church is without a pastor (Book of Church Order, 15-4, page 42) denies the session the exercise of its proper and efficient jurisdiction and governing of its church. It is subject to the convenience and/or whims of a moderator who is generally already overburdened with responsibilities. It permits a presbytery to name a moderator unacceptable to a session because of his theological position, personality or availability;

Whereas, the requirement that a Minister of the Word be the moderator of session under the Book of Church Order (13-2 and 15-4) places another unnecessary burden and additional responsibilities on a minister already encumbered so heavily that the minister of the Word is rendered less effective in his total ministry;

Whereas, the minister of the Word is so encumbered that he ought to have relief from the task and responsibility of moderator of session;

Whereas, the principal parity of the ruling and teaching elders is violated;

Whereas, there is no Spiritual grounds for the teaching elder to moderate the session, only the tradition of men;

Therefore, to rectify the inequities, to promote a more harmonious relationship in and between courts, to provide some relief to an encumbered ministry and to maintain the parity of teaching and ruling elders, the Session of McIlwain Memorial Presbyterian Church overtures the first General Assembly of the Continuing Presbyterian Church to amend the Book of Church Order so that a session may exercise its right to elect its moderator.

*References are the BOCO copyrighted by the PCUS in 1965, 12th printing 1969, paperback edition.

4. That the Resolution from Tom Cook having to do with requiring all Teaching Elders to serve as pastor (page 22) was referred to the Constitutional Documents Committee for report to the Second General Assembly.

Resolution from Teaching Elder Thomas Cook, Louisville, Mississippi.

No ordained member of any Presbytery in the Continuing Church may remain out of the Pastor-church relationship for more than six (6) years at one time except missionaries in the field and retirees. After six (6)

<a id="ga02-p44"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=44 printed_page=null -->

years of service, i.e., Board-Agency-Executive, Professor, etc., they shall be required to spend three (3) years in a Pastor-church relationship in a bona fide call. In extreme cases the local Presbytery, at a stated meeting, may by two-thirds vote, extend the six years to seven years.

5. The Constitutional Documents Committee was granted authority to work with corresponding committees of the Orthodox Presbyterian Church, the Reformed Presbyterian Church, Evangelical Synod, and the Reformed Presbyterian Church of North America on both an updating of the language of the Westminster Standards, and on Scripture proof texts of the same.

## 1-82 Theological Conferences

A motion of the General Assembly recommend to each Presbytery that it utilize one of its Committees or appoint a Committee to establish an annual theological conference to serve its own constituency, and that this matter be referred to the Committee on Christian Education and Publications, was referred to the Committee on Christian Education and Publications for study and report back to the Second General Assembly.

## 2-22 Recess

## EVENING SESSION

### 2-23 Assembly Reconvened

The Assembly reconvened at 7:00 P.M. with prayer by the Rev. Charles Dunahoo.

### 2-24 Procedural Motion on Selection of Church Name

It was moved that the Assembly proceed to the vote on the Name of the Church in the following manner: Without further discussion, the Assembly take a first vote on all seventeen names, with each commissioner voting on three of the seventeen. Then the floor be opened for discussion on the top three names, after which they be voted upon until one of them receives a majority of the Assembly's vote. (See 2-17.)

### 2-25 The Name Chosen

The top three names chosen were:

- National Reformed Presbyterian Church
- International Presbyterian Church
- American Presbyterian Church

The Assembly selected National Reformed Presbyterian Church as the new name of the Church. (See 2-34, 2-45 — 2-49)

### 2-26 Clearing of the Name

The Assembly instructed our Legal Counsel, Mr. Ken Ryskamp, to contact the National Presbyterian Church and Center of Washington, D. C. to determine their reaction to this choice of name.

### 2-27 Proposal for a Suit of Declaratory Judgment Tabled

A motion reading, “If the new name is not accepted, then the counsel will be instructed to file a suit in declaratory judgment,” was tabled. Teaching Elder William P. Buckner of the Presbytery of Texas requested that his negative vote on the motion to table be recorded.

### 2-28 Constitutional Documents Committee Report — Charismatic Gifts

The Rev. Charles Dunahoo, Chairman of the Constitutional Documents Committee began his report, and yielded the floor to the Rev. Jack B. Scott, Chairman of the Ad Interim Committee on Charismatic Gifts (See 1-71).

Paragraph 7-1 of the Book of Church Order was adopted as follows, as recommended by the Ad-Interim Committee:

“Under the New Testament, our Lord at first collected His people out of different nations, and united them to the household of faith by the ministry of extraordinary officers who received extraordinary gifts of the Spirit and who were agents by whom God completed His revelation to His church. Such officers and gifts related to new revelation have no successors since God completed His revelation at the conclusion of the Apostolic Age.”

The Pastoral Letter proposed by the Ad Interim Committee on Charismatic Gifts was adopted by the Assembly as a pastoral letter to

<a id="ga02-p46"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=46 printed_page=null -->

all Churches. The following Commissioners requested that their negative votes be recorded against this action:
Rev. John Clelland, Rev. Harry Miller.
(See Appendix D, pp. 126-129)

## 2-29 Constitutional Documents Committee Report — Ruling Elders Administering Sacraments

The Rev. Charles Dunahoo, Chairman of the Constitutional Documents Committee yielded the floor to the Rev. Harold Borchert, Chairman of the Ad-Interim Committee to Study the Question of Ruling Elders Administering the Sacraments, who presented the Majority Report of the Committee. Mr. Borchert in turn yielded the floor to the Rev. Basil Albert, who presented the Minority Report. (See Appendix pp. 177-179). The whole matter was referred to an Ad Interim Committee to Study the Question of the Number of Officers of the Church, and bring final recommendations on this issue to the General Assembly. (See 2-36.)

## 2-30 The Assembly was recessed for the evening with prayer by Dr. Allen Fleece, with special petitions for Mr. David Osborne, Pastor Elect of one of our Churches in Pulaski, Virginia, who had to be taken to the hospital.

## SECOND DAY
## WEDNESDAY MORNING SESSION

September 18, 1974

### 2-31 Worship

The Assembly reconvened at 8:30 A.M. and was led in worship by Ruling Elder Ken Keyes. The Rev. Todd Allen led in prayer. Mr. Keyes read the Scripture, and brought the message. The Rev. Kennedy Smartt led in the closing prayer.

### 2-32 Assembly Reconvened

The Assembly was convened by the Moderator at 9:00 A.M. being opened with prayer by Dr. William E. Hill, Jr.

### 2-33 Reading of the Minutes

The Minutes of Tuesday’s sessions were read and approved.

### 2-34 Reconsideration of the Name Proposed

The Rev. Kennedy Smartt made the following motion: As one who voted with the majority, I move that the Assembly reconsider the matter of the name of the denomination.

The matter was docketed as the first order of business at the afternoon session, with the instructions that all committees be present. (See 2-45 — 2-49.)

### 2-35 Mission to the World Committee Excused

The Committee of Commissioners on Mission to the World was excused from the sessions of the Assembly today to continue their work, except for the period in which the name is being considered.

# 2-36 Constitutional Documents Committee Report (Continued From 2-29.)

The Form of Government was amended as follows:

5-2. The following procedures shall be used in electing Ruling Elders in a newly organized congregation:

1. Not less than thirty days prior to the date of organization, petitioners shall submit, from among their body, nominations of male members for the office of Ruling Elder to the presbytery or its designated organizing commission or evangelist, keeping in mind the qualifications set forth in I Timothy 3 and Titus 1.

2. Nominees shall be instructed and examined concerning their Christian experience, their knowledge and acceptance of the constitutional standards of the Church and their willingness to assume the responsibilities of Ruling Elder.

3. The congregation will, at the organizational meeting, determine the number of Ruling Elders to be elected.

4. Report shall be made to the congregation of those eligible to be elected, from whom the Ruling Elders shall be chosen, following procedures outlined in Paragraphs 25-3 and 25-4 of the Book of Church Order.

5. Ordination and installation shall follow the procedure set forth in Paragraph 25-5 of the Book of Church Order.

6. Those elected, ordained and installed Ruling Elders should meet as soon as is practicable to elect a moderator and a clerk. The moderator may be one of their own number, or, any Teaching Elder of the Presbytery with Presbytery’s approval.

5-3. If Deacons are elected, follow the procedures of (1) through (5) above. If Deacons are not elected, the duties of the office shall devolve upon the Ruling Elders.

1-6 (p.5, line 6) to read, “The ordination of officers is by a court except in the case of ordination by presbytery’s evangelist. (See 8-6).”

Page 10 Insert new 8-5 to read “When a teaching elder is called to labor as an associate or assistant pastor (see Chapter 23, Pastoral Relations), he may be assigned special areas of responsibility.”

Add “#25-9. It is recommended to all Sessions that when a Ruling Elder or Deacon becomes infirm or reaches the age of 70, he may at his request be designated Elder or Deacon Emeritus, retaining full privileges of his office but being relieved of the obligations for regular attendance at Church Courts or the Diaconate and service on the committees.

The Rev. Erskine Jackson resumed the Chair.

The following motion was presented to add a new section 6-5.

“A member who for one year does not participate in the ordinances at his church or otherwise express interest in its work, when not Providentially hindered, may be placed on an Inactive Roll after the Session has made diligent effort to restore him to activity in the life and work of the congregation. This Inactive Roll is not to be reported to the Presbytery. If the member resumes active participation in the life of the church, the Session shall restore him to the Active Roll. An officer who is placed on the Inactive Roll shall have his office dissolved and may only be restored to that office by reelection by the congregation if and when he resumes activity in the life of the church.”

Action on this motion postponed until after the first order of business in the afternoon session. (See 2-64.)

The program presentation of the Permanent Committee on Mission to the United States was set for 11:30 A.M., Thursday, September 19.

## 2-43 Committees Excused

The Committee of Commissioners on Christian Education and Publications, the Committee of Commissioners on Mission to the World, and the Standing Committee on Extension Seminaries were excused from the afternoon sessions of the Assembly, after the matter of the name is settled.

## 2-44 Report of the Program Committee

The Stated Clerk presented the following docket for the afternoon to follow the decision on the name, the completion of the report of the Constitutional Documents Committee, the Report of the Ad Interim Committee on Presbytery Boundaries, and the Report of the Nominating Committee, the reports of the Committees of Commissioners are scheduled in the following order: Insurance and Annuities, the Board of Directors and Administration.

## 2-45 Reconsideration of the Name of the Church

The special order of dealing with the matter of reconsideration of the name of the Church having arrived, the motion to reconsider was passed by a vote of 326 to 94. (See 2-34 p. 44.)

## 2-46 Names Placed in Nomination

The following names were placed in nomination for consideration:

- Presbyterian Church in America
- The Presbyterian Church
- International Prebyserian Church
- Grace Presbyterian Church
- Mission Presbyterian Church
- National Reformed Presbyterian Church
- American Presbyterian Church
- Presbyterian Church of the Americas

## 2-47 Two thirds Vote Set

It was determined that no name should be adopted without a two thirds majority vote of the General Assembly.

## 2-48 Names with “America” to be Treated First

It was moved to deal with all of the names including some form of the word “America” separately, so that only one name appear on the final list. The name “Presbyterian Church in America” was chosen.

## 2-49 The Name Selected

On the vote on the remaining slate the name “Presbyterian Church in America” was chosen. The following is the tabulation of the votes:

<a id="ga02-p51"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=51 printed_page=null -->

|  Presbyterian Church in America | 302  |
| --- | --- |
|  The Presbyterian Church | 3  |
|  International Presbyterian Church | 27  |
|  Grace Presbyterian Church | 5  |
|  Mission Presbyterian Church | 6  |
|  National Reformed Presbyterian Church | 61  |

On a revote a total of 401 voted for Presbyterian Church in America.

## 2-50 The Moderator to Express the Sense of this Action

Regarding statements to the press, it was moved and passed that the Moderator issue a statement expressing the sense of the General Assembly as to why we changed our name.

## 2-51 Recess

A ten minute recess was taken.

## 2-52 Assembly Reconvened

The Moderator reconvened the Assembly at 4:40 with prayer.

## 2-53 Docket Amended

On motion from the Clerk the docket was amended to hear the Report of the Committee of Commissioners on Insurance and Annuities at this time.

## 2-54 Report of the Committee of Commissioners on Insurance and Annuities

The Rev. Robert Sweet, Chairman of the Committee of Commissioners on Insurance and Annuities presented the following report which was adopted:

### REPORT OF THE COMMITTEE OF COMMISSIONERS ON INSURANCE AND ANNUITIES

The meeting opened with a prayer by Commissioner Thos. E. Hoolsema.

I. The Committee of Commissioners on September 17, 1974 considered the following items:

Minutes

1. Minutes of meeting of the Sub-Committee on Insurance, of the Committee on Administration.
a. December 18, 1973
b. May 30, 1974
c. September 16, 1974

2. Minutes of Board of Trustees, Insurance and Annuity Fund.
a. March 29, 1974
b. May 31, 1974
c. June 25, 1974
d. July 3, 1974
e. September 16, 1974

3. Joint meeting of two above groups February 15, 1974.

The Committee of Commissioners designated the Secretary, Chairman, and member Parker Rhett to review all the Minutes of the above Committees by a vote of 15 to 0. These Minutes were reviewed and found to be in order.

The Commissioners reviewed the official plan of the Annuity Fund for Ministers and the report of the Sub-Committee on Insurance and resolution #2, page 89, of the Commissioners Handbook. (See pp. 135-145)

<a id="ga02-p52"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=52 printed_page=null -->

## II. YOUR COMMITTEE RECOMMENDS:

A. That the Minutes listed above be approved.

B. That the report of the Board of Trustees be approved, and the following recommendations be adopted

1. That the plan be adopted.

2. That Resolution No. 2 be adopted, as amended as follows:

**Resolution 2 Adopted by the Trustees of the Annuity Fund, June 25, 1974**

**Whereas**, the General Assembly of the National Presbyterian Church has provided an excellent retirement program for its ministers which it considers to be, overall, superior to any individually funded program; and

**Whereas**, the most efficient and most productive operation of that retirement program requires the fullest participation on the part of the ministers and congregations of the National Presbyterian Church; and,

**Whereas**, the servants of Christ in the National Presbyterian Church should have their financial security in their old age made sure by such a retirement program; therefore,

**Be it Resolved**, that the General Assembly of the National Presbyterian Church encourage and urge all of its ministers and congregations to participate in the denominationally sponsored retirement program, and,

**Be it Further Resolved**, that the General Assembly encourage all the presbyteries of the National Presbyterian Church to establish a policy of urging participation in the denominationally sponsored retirement and medical insurance programs in the terms of a call to a minister.

**Recommendation of the Trustee of the Annuity Fund**

That the beneficiaries of death benefits and of the long term disability insurance policies be changed if possible to the Trustees for the Insurance and Annuity Fund of the National Presbyterian Church.

3. That we again suggest that all ministers be participants in the Social Security Program.

4. That the Board of Trustees of the Annuity Fund for Ministers cause to be drafted the necessary trust indenture to implement the official plan.

5. That the Board of Directors of the National Presbyterian Church be authorized by the General Assembly to approve the trust indenture so drafted and to enter into the same with the Board of Trustees in the name of and on behalf of the General Assembly.

The following motion was also adopted, that the Trustees for the Insurance and Annuity Fund be directed to investigate the possibility of expanding the Annuity Fund for Ministers to include all full time Church employees, and to amend the plan to include them, if actuarially possible. (See also Minutes of the 1973 General Assembly, item 1-67, recommendation 12, page 49.)

(See 2-63 for the completion of this report.)

### 2-61 Report of the Joint Committee — Christian Education and Mission to the United States

The following report from the Joint Committee of Commissioners on Christian Education and Publications and on Mission to the United States (See 2-37, 2-41) was adopted:

This Committee determines that the Committee for Christian Education and Publications has responsibility for seminaries as set forth in the Minutes of our First General Assembly on page 57.

However, this Committee takes note of recommendation number 11 of the Report of the Committee on Mission to the United States concerning the shortage of ministers in the Presbyterian Church in America and recommends that the General Assembly charge the Committee for Christian Education and Publications, in consultation with the Committee on Mission to the United States, to formulate plans and programs for extension seminaries.

Respectfully submitted,
Emory M. Folmar, Chairman Joint Committee

This report was presented by Ruling Elder Thurston Futch, Jr., member of the Committee in the absence of the Chairman.

<a id="ga02-p54"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=54 printed_page=null -->

## 2-63 Report of the Committee of Commissioners on Insurance and Annuities (Continued from 2-54)

C. That the report of the Sub-Committee on Insurance be approved, and the following recommendations be adopted:

1. We recommend that ministers and others who need additional life insurance consider purchasing ordinary or whole life insurance through individual programs, and that the Sub-Committee on Insurance give further study to providing an additional amount of life insurance.

2. We recommend that an offering to be known as the Christmas Gift for Ministerial Relief be received to help supplement the retirement needs of ministers and their families of the National Presbyterian Church.

3. We recommend that 80% of the funds received in the Ministerial Relief Offering for the first five years of our church's life be set aside as a reserve fund against future needs for both retired ministers and their dependents.

4. We recommend that the Ministerial Relief Funds provide that the retired ministers of the National Presbyterian Church receive a minimum income of not less than $4,800 per year for couples and $3,300 per year for single persons, all regular income being considered.

5. We recommend that Ministerial Relief Funds be used to pay the premiums for the health insurance and to reimburse the cost of Medicare Part B for the retired ministers of the National Presbyterian Church, and their dependents.

D. That the Supplemental Report of the Insurance Committee of September 17, 1974, be approved (See Appendix G p. 143.), and that the following additional recommendations be adopted:

1. We recommend that the hospital room rate coverage be increased to $62.00 a day, effective November 1, 1974 at a cost increase of $1.00 a month for an employee and $3.00 a month for an employee and his family.
Total cost: $22.00 a month for employees
$48.00 a month for employee and his family.

2. We recommend to the General Assembly that we provide hospitalization insurance for persons age 65 and above by one of the following options:

1. Those enrolled in Medicare, Parts A and B, be provided for a monthly premium of $8.00 per person.

2. Those not enrolled in Medicare be covered for the same premium as those under age 65.

3. We recommend that the General Assembly authorize the Insurance Committee to continue to negotiate with insurance companies for the purpose of providing continuing hospitalization insurance equal to or better than the existing major medical insurance for the year 1975.

III. The Committee of Commissioners commends the Trustees and the Committee on Insurance on the very fine handling of their responsibilities and in their providing an outstanding Annuity and Insurance Program.

Respectfully submitted,
Robert C. Sweet, Chairman
R. K. Abele, Secretary

**COMMITTEE MEMBERS:**

## 2-64 Report of the Constitutional Documents Committee (Continued from 2-36)

The Rev. Charles Dunahoo continued to present the report of the Constitutional Documents Committee:

The discussion on the proposed amendment on inactive roles (See 2-36, p. 45.) was extended by ten minutes. The motion to adopt this amendment was lost.

The Rules of Discipline of the Book of Church were amended as follows:

Page 53A, line After “and necessary” add “In its proper usage discipline maintains (a) the glory of God; (b) the purity of His Church; (c) the preservation of the saints and restoration of disobedient sinners. Discipline is for the purpose of godliness (1 Timothy 4:7); therefore, it demands a self-examination under Scripture.”

Page 54, line 6 add:

“Discipline is systematic training under the authority of God’s Scripture. No communing or non-communing member of the Church should be allowed to stray from the Scripture’s discipline. Therefore, teaching elders must: (a) instruct the officers in discipline, (b) instruct the congregation in discipline, (c) jointly practice it in the context of the congregation and church courts.”

Add new section 1-5 (page 54)

1-5 Scripture law is the basis of all discipline; because it is the revelation of God’s Holy will.

Add new 1-6

1-6 Proper disciplinary principles are set forth in the Scriptures and must be followed. They are: (a) instruction in the Word, (b) the individual’s responsibility to admonish one another (Matthew 18:15-17; Galatians 6:1), (c) if the admonition is rejected, then the calling of one or more witnesses (Matthew 18:16), (d) if rejection persists, then the Church must act through her courts, first unto admonition, then to suspension, excommunication and deposition (See chapters three and four for further explanation.). Steps (a) through (d) must be followed in proper order for the exercise of discipline.

Page 54, line 11. After “in the home” add: “True discipleship involves learning the Word of God under the guidance of the Holy Spirit both at home and in the Church. Without learning there is no growth and without growth there is no discipline and without discipline there is sin and iniquity (I Timothy 4:7).”

Page 54, line 12 insert before “The Church” . . . “The home and”.

The time for the special order having arrived, this report was interrupted. (See 2-70.)

## 2-65 Report of the Judicial Business Committee on the Name

Ruling Elder Robert Cannada, Chairman of the Judicial Business Committee reported that he had reserved the name “Presbyterian Church in America” in the State of Delaware. He indicated that there was no guarantee that this name would not be challenged by others.
