Add the following:

5-2. The following procedures shall be used in electing Ruling Elders in a newly organized congregation:

(1) Not less than thirty days prior to the date of organization, petitioners shall submit, from among their body, nominations of male members for the office of Ruling Elder to the presbytery or its designated organizing commission or evangelist, keeping in mind the qualifications set forth in I Timothy 3 and Titus 1.

(2) Nominees shall be instructed and examined concerning their Christian experience, their knowledge and acceptance of the constitutional standards of the Church and their willingness to assume the responsibilities of the office of Ruling Elders.

(3) The congregation will, at the organizational meeting, determine the number of Ruling Elders to be elected.

(4) Report shall be made to the congregation of those eligible to be elected, from whom the Ruling Elders shall be chosen, following procedures outlined in Paragraphs 25-3 and 25-4 of the Book of Church Order.

(5) Ordination and installation shall follow the procedure set forth in Paragraph 2-5-5 of the Book of Church Order.

(6) Those elected, ordained and installed Ruling Elders should meet as soon as is practicable to elect a moderator and a clerk. The moderator may be one of their own number, or, any Teaching Elder of the Presbytery with Presbytery’s approval.

5-3. If deacons are elected, follow the procedures of (1) through (5) above. If deacons are not elected, the duties of the office shall devolve upon the Ruling Elders.

## 2-74 Report of the Presbytery Boundaries Committee

The Rev. Dan McCown, Chairman of the Ad Interim Committee on Presbytery Boundaries presented the report of the Committee, which was adopted as amended as follows:

## REPORT OF THE PRESBYTERY BOUNDARY COMMITTEE

At the First Meeting of the General Assembly held last December in Birmingham, Ala., a Special Ad-Interim Committee was appointed to recommend Presbytery Boundaries. The Committee was composed of one Teaching Elder and one Ruling Elder from each of the existing Presbyteries of the National Presbyterian Church, with Rev. Dan H. McCown of the Presbytery of Texas appointed as Convener.

The Committee met in Atlanta, Ga. on March 8-9 with most of the members present, and with some suggestions from those who had to be absent. The first item of business was the election of a Chairman and a Secretary. Those elected were the Convener, Dan H. McCown as Chairman and Rev. Tom Patete of Winona, Miss. as Secretary.

Communications from the absent members were read along with the Communication #3 from the Commissioner's Handbook of the First General Assembly and Overtures #1, 10, and 15, that were referred to this committee for its consideration.

We might mention here that Communication #3 stated: “1) after the initial formation of the Presbyteries the right of presbytery sovereignty be acknowledged so as to prevent the diminishing or enlarging of Presbyteries’ boundaries without the direct consent of those bodies and, 2) that it shall be recommended to these courts that a) their size shall be limited, generally, to a diameter of 150 miles in order to maintain Elder participation and, b) that their number shall be limited, generally, to 40 churches so that genuine fellowship may be had by all the constituting ministers and churches.”

Your Committee sought to adhere to the 150 mile guideline insofar as possible, but we felt that it would be best not to restrict presbyteries to only 40 churches. This will probably be the case in most instances — but again we sought to be flexible — plus the fact that at least one presbytery already has 40 or more churches.

The three overtures that were answered in the affirmative and referred to this Committee — #1, 10, and 15 were taken into consideration and were adhered to insofar as possible. #1, and 15 were almost the same as they requested that “the boundaries of the presbyteries be left fluid through 1974 and to consult with the presbyteries concerning their boundaries before any changes are planned.” #10 read “that the General Assembly seek to keep, both now and in the future, the size of our presbyteries — both geographically and numerically — small enough so that every church and minister may be represented at all meetings, and so that general fellowship among members may be fully realized.”

As your Committee discussed the best possible way to arrive at some solution concerning the boundaries, it was decided that the members of the Committee would be divided into four sub-committees (by geographical areas where they had mutual interest). These areas were: 1) Mississippi, Louisiana, Texas, and Arkansas; 2) Alabama and Gulf Coast (north Florida); 3) South Carolina, Georgia, and Southern Florida; 4) North Carolina, Tennessee, Kentucky, West Virginia, Virginia, and Maryland.

After each group met separately, their recommendations to the Committee for presbytery boundaries were these: (And may it be said that there was a common consent, a oneness among the entire Committee in regard to these recommendations.)

TEXAS — state of Texas

LOUISIANA — LOUISIANA PRESBYTERY (Louisiana west of Mississippi River plus West Feliciana, East Feliciana, St. Helena, East Baton Rouge, and Livingston parishes.

GRACE — Same as PCUS Presbytery of South Mississippi plus Louisiana west to LOUISIANA Presbytery border.

MISSISSIPPI VALLEY — same as PCUS Presbytery of Central Mississippi

<a id="ga02-p65"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=65 printed_page=null -->

COVENANT — same as PCUS Presbytery of St. Andrew plus state of Arkansas and Tennessee west of Tennessee River
EVANGEL — same as PCUS Presbyteries of North Alabama, Birmingham and East Alabama.
WARRIOR — same as PCUS Presbytery of Tuscaloosa plus Washington, Clarke, Monroe, and Conecuh counties
GULF COAST — northwest Florida east to and including Madison and Taylor counties plus Mobile, Baldwin, and Escambia counties in Alabama
SOUTHERN FLORIDA — southern Florida up to Tampa/Orlando area
CENTRAL GEORGIA — central and southern Georgia up to and including Harris, Talbot, Upson, Lamar, Butts, Jasper, Morgan, Greene, Taliaferro, Wilkes, and Lincoln counties
NORTH GEORGIA — northern Georgia down to CENTRAL GEORGIA border
CALVARY — state of South Carolina
WESTERN NORTH CAROLINA — western North Carolina east to and including Alleghany, Wilkes, Alexander, Caldwell, Burke, and Cleveland counties
CAROLINA — central and eastern North Carolina, west to WESTERN NORTH CAROLINA border
MID-ATLANTIC — state of Maryland and Virginia west to and including Loudon, Faquier, Rappahannock, Madison, Greene, Albemarle, Nelson, Amherst, Bedford, and Pittsylvania counties, and Morgan, Jefferson and Berkley counties in West Virginia.
NEW RIVER PRESBYTERY West Virginia except Morgan, Jefferson and Berkley counties and Virginia east to MID-ATLANTIC border and down to and including Giles, Montgomery, Floyd, and Patrick counties in Virginia.
TENNESSEE VALLEY — central and southeastern Tennessee up to and including Claiborne, Grainger, Hamblen, and Cocke counties and west to Tennessee River
WESTMINSTER — northeastern Tennessee down to TENNESSEE VALLEY border and southwestern Virginia up to NEW RIVER border
*VANGUARD — state of Kentucky

PACIFIC

[*Names marked by an asterisk are merely suggestions and/or geographical designations; names must be finally determined by each presbytery. Other names are as already determined by existing presbyteries.]

You will be able to see the exact presbytery boundaries better on the map enclosed for your convenience.

Because of the involvement of the Mission to the U. S. Committee with the various Churches and presbyteries, this report was sent to them for their study and response before being included in the Handbook.

We know that other presbyteries will possibly be formed — and there will be certain situations that will need to be handled as individual cases, but in seeking to fulfill the purpose for which this Committee was brought into being — to recommend Presbytery Boundaries — we recommend the following:

1) That the tentative boundaries proposed in the report be approved and the effective date be January 1, 1975 (being flexible or fluid until that time)
2) That the General Assembly recognize and insure the right of any individual church to petition its presbytery to alter presbytery lines to exclude that particular church from the boundaries proposed.
3) Recommend that any new work outside of present Presbytery boundaries begun after the close of the 2nd General Assembly seek the advice of the Mission to the U. S. Committee before uniting with a Presbytery.
4) That, if the General Assembly feels it necessary, this Committee continue to work with any problems that might arise in this area of boundaries, until January 1, 1975.

Commissioner’s Handbook.

Respectfully submitted,
Dan H. McCown, Chairman
Committee to Recommend
Presbytery Boundaries

2-82 Report Continued from 2-80

In consideration of Recommendation B-2 the following substitute was offered:

The Second General Assembly of the Presbyterian Church in America directs its Permanent Committee on Mission to the World to use care to see that all missionaries sent by the Assembly's Committee be involved in propagating the Reformed Faith, either by working with already established Presbyterian and Reformed Churches, or, if no Reformed Church exists in the land to which they are sent, to seek to establish a Reformed witness there.

2-88 Report of the Committee on Mission to the World (Continued From
2- 8 2 )
Recommendation B-8, which reads: “That lay missionaries be al
lowed to participate in the 12% annuity program ” was referred to the

The report as amended and adopted is as follows:
report of the committee of commissioners on
mission to the world
I. the committee of commissioners on mission to the world considered the
following items referred to it::
minutes of the permanent committee
report of the permanent committee
overtures numbered 9, 10, 11, 12, 15, 16, 17, 18, 19, 20, 21
resolution number 4
II. your committee recommend s:
A. that the minutes of the permanent committee on mission to the world
be approved .
B. that the report of the permanent committee on mission to the world
be approved , and the following recommendations be adopted :

<a id="ga02-p70"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=70 printed_page=null -->

1. That the Rev. John E. Kyle be called as Coordinator for the Committee on Mission to the World.

2. That the General Assembly authorize the Committee on Mission to the World to establish working relationships with other evangelical missionary agencies that welcome the services and teaching of missionaries holding the Reformed faith and polity, so as to enable it to send candidates to them, as it may seem best for the greatest effectiveness in proclaiming the Gospel, to work under their auspices while at the same time maintaining full relationship to the NPC; also to receive and forward to the agencies concerned financial support needed by them. Such missionaries shall be responsible to the Sessions or Presbyteries in matters of doctrine and moral conduct, but at the same time subject to the rules of the agencies under which they serve. Such missionaries shall be considered missionaries of the NPC, and as such will send news and reports of their work to the CMW, their Presbyteries and supporting churches and individuals in the NPC. Details as to itineration while on furlough, pensions and other matters needing definition or adjustment would be worked out with the agencies concerned, that careful evaluation be made at the 1975 General Assembly to be certain that our missionary efforts under the program provide full and free presentation of the Gospel as contained in and understood in the Reformed view (16 for, 1 against)

3. Budget for 1975. See report of the Committee on Administration.

4. That the General Assembly approve in principle the acceptance of Christ's College in Taiwan, and to authorize the Permanent Committee on Mission to the World to actively support Christ's College while working toward completion of the transfer, . . . and that a report on the college and the proposed transfer to the National Presbyterian Church be heard at this time. (See Appendix L for Agreement, pp. 164-167) (This authorizes the Committee to begin sending missionaries to the college.) (unanimous)

5. That the General Assembly support the Committee on Mission to the World as they seek to help the Presbyteries and Churches find reasonable, judicious, and Biblical ways for raising support for approved missionary efforts by the Presbyterian Church in America. (unanimous)

6. That the second Sunday of June, 1975, be designated as a day of prayer and fasting for the World Mission of the Church.

7. That Presbyteries and local Sessions have an orderly process of sending missionaries overseas and that the Committee on Mission to the World be advised and consulted in this orderly process, and that the Permanent Committee on Missions to the World be available to the Presbyteries to assist them in the establishing of this orderly process, and that the Permanent Committee on Missions to the World be available to the Presbyteries to assist them in the establishing of this orderly process. (unanimous)

8. That lay missionaries be allowed to participate in the 12% annuity program. (unanimous) The Assembly referred this recommendation to the Trustees of the Insurance Fund.

9. That the Second General Assembly direct the Permanent Committee on Mission to the World to prepare a policy manual to be presented for approval and adoption at the next General Assembly, and be authorized to hire an additional staff person, if necessary, to implement this action, and that the Permanent Committee be reminded of our consistent separation from the World Council and National Council of Churches. (unanimous)

C. That Overtures numbered 9, 10, 11, 12, 15, 16, 17, 18, 19, 20, 21 and Resolution number 4 be carried over to the next General Assembly when they can be acted on in relation to the General Assembly's approval of the policy manual.

D. Whereas the Permanent Committee on Mission to the World has, in the

<a id="ga02-p71"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=71 printed_page=null -->

short span of one year, succeeded in initiating a m1ss1onary enterprise
composed of 19 missionaries now working in or soon to be in 5 coun-
tries, and

Whereas they have developed a missionary program that envisions ex-
pansion throughout the world within the next few years, and

Whereas this has been accomplished at great expense of time and labor
while carrying on full time jobs and ministries.

Therefore be it resolved that the Permanent Committee on Mission to
the World of the Presbyterian Church in America be commended by the
Second General Assembly for the diligent and sacrificial manner with
which they have carried out their task since the first General Assembly.
Gene Hunt,
Chairman

## II. YOUR COMMITTEE RECOMMENDS:

### A. That the Minutes of the Board of Directors be approved.

The committee recommends that the Board of Directors by resolution require the 4 Permanent Committees to have two signatures on all checks written against Corporation and Committee bank accounts.

That the following policy of conditional gifts be adopted instead of Paragraph 1-23 of the Board of Director's Minutes.

It is resolved that the Board of Directors establish a matter of policy that before any conditional gifts are received in behalf of the National Presbyterian Church, the conditions shall be put into writing and submitted to the Board of Directors for approval. It is further resolved that as a matter of policy the Board of Directors does not favor receiving gifts that have any conditions attached thereto, unless after ten (10) years if the purposes of the contributor have not been accomplished, or cannot be accomplished the General Assembly may upon recommendation of the Board of Directors remove such conditions by a 2/3 vote of registered commissioners.

### B. Report of the Special Committee on By-Laws be approved as amended following change: Add “the immediate past Moderator” to the Committee on Administration, Article IV, Section 1.

The Rev. Richard Adelman, Chairman of the Committee of Commissioners on Judicial Business, presented the following report, which was adopted as amended:

<a id="ga02-p74"></a>

# REPORT OF THE COMMITTEE OF COMMISSIONERS ON JUDICIAL BUSINESS

|  Name | Presbytery  |
| --- | --- |

|  Millard Tate | Carolina  |
|  John Clelland | Evangel  |

|  Charles E. Champion | Tennessee Valley  |
|  James H. Campbell | Mid-Atlantic  |
|  Russell D. Toms | Southern Florida  |
|  Joe Morecraft, III | Westminster  |
|  Richard Adelman | Gulf Coast  |
|  Gerald G. Morgan | Mississippi Valley  |

The Committee met in the Elder Room on Tuesday afternoon, September 17. The meeting opened with prayer by the Convenor, Richard Adelman. Richard Adelman was elected Chairman. John Clelland was elected Secretary.

The Report of the Committee on Judicial Business was read. It was moved and carried that the report of the Permanent Committee be received as read.

It was moved and carried that Overture 4 be answered in the affirmative.

It was moved and carried that Overture 5 be answered in the negative.

It was moved and carried that Overture 7 be answered in the negative.

It was moved and carried that Overture 8 be referred to the Constitutional Documents Committee.

It was moved and carried that the Report of the Permanent Committee amended by the substitution of “The Committee on Judicial Business” for “The Board of Directors” in the paragraphs on Court Cases and Legal Defense Funds be received.

It was moved and carried that the Committee recommend to the General Assembly approval of the report of the Permanent Committee as printed in the Handbook. (See Appendix I, pp. 147-148)

It was moved and carried that the Commissioners Committee on Judicial Business recommend to General Assembly that it take action to establish a fund to assist needy churches involved in litigation over their property, as recommended by the presbytery in whose boundaries they are located; all subject to approval of the Committee on Administration. This fund is to be a voluntary fund, which is to be publicized.

Pending the adoption of Manuals of the Permanent Committees by the General Assembly, the duties of these Committees shall be the following, and such other duties as shall be assigned by the General Assembly:

## Administration

1. To nominate to the General Assembly a Stated Clerk and a Business Administrator.

2. The Stated Clerk may serve part time or full time as needed, to reside where he desires. The General Assembly shall provide office help for him. His duties are: a) handle records; b) maintain history; c) serve as parliamentarian; d) handle all correspondence; e) the Committee shall serve as a clearing house for vacant churches and available ministers.

3. The Business Administrator shall be a full time employee, preferably not a teaching elder. He shall maintain the denominational business office, administer all the business affairs of the Assembly, act as treasurer of this committee, handle annuity and insurance. He is to be answerable to the Committee on Administration of the General Assembly.

4. To review the budget requests of the three other committees; to consider

<a id="ga02-p75"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=75 printed_page=null -->

the requests of each committee as it relates to the budget requests of other committees, to needs and to opportunities, and to recommend a budget for each of the three committees to the General Assembly. Each committee shall be responsible to raise the financial support for its work and distribute its funds through its own treasurers elected by each committee. It shall be clearly understood that churches and individual donors shall be free to designate their gifts to the causes they desire to support and that there shall be no equalization of gifts so designated.

5. The suggested budget of the Committee on Administration shall be presented to the General Assembly. Upon adoption by the General Assembly, funds for the operation of the Committee on Administration shall be raised by this Committee and distributed through its own treasurer.

6. To operate the insurance and annuity program. It shall recommend salaries of personnel to the General Assembly. It shall supervise the work of the Business Administrator.

7. The office of Stated Clerk and of Business Administrator may not be held by the same individual.

8. Judicial Business Sub-Committee

- **a.** To advise the General Assembly on judicial matters.
- **b.** To assist the Stated Clerk on such matters between Assemblies.
- **c.** To be elected by the General Assembly.

**Christian Education and Publications**
1. To nominate a Coordinator to each General Assembly and recommend his salary to the Committee on Administration.
2. To publish official publications of the denomination.
3. To study and recommend Christian Education curricula programs to the denomination.
4. To study the possibility of developing curricula by the denomination itself.
5. To recommend plans for promoting: Sunday School, Christian Education Work, youth work, men's work, women's work, camp and conference programs, etc.
6. To maintain a liaison with other Christian publishers.
7. To continue to study and make recommendations to the denomination regarding our needs in schools, colleges, seminaries, and similar institutions.

**Mission to the United States**
1. To nominate a Coordinator to each General Assembly and recommend his salary to the Committee on Administration.
2. To study the mission needs in the nation, and inform the Assembly of these needs.
3. To promote mission work outside the boundaries of the Church until such work can be integrated into the regular Presbytery, and to assist in the coordination of such work by Presbyteries.
4. To cooperate with Presbyteries in their mission work.
5. To promote financial aid where needed and other mission support throughout the denomination.
6. To interpret the mission program to the denomination.
7. To maintain liaison with the Mission to the United States committees of all the judicatories.
8. To organize provisional Presbyteries.

**Mission to the World**
1. To nominate a coordinator to each General Assembly and recommend his salary to the Committee on Administration.
2. To advise the General Assembly of missionary needs abroad.
3. To recommend ways of meeting these needs abroad.
4. To assist Presbyteries and local churches to recruit missionaries.
5. To function as a sending agency for missionaries not otherwise accredited, and the support agency for missionaries not sustained.
6. To promote the missionary spirit across the denomination.
7. To interpret the missionary program to the denomination.
8. To assist missionaries in their visas and recognition by foreign countries.
9. To maintain liaison with the missionaries but not to function as adminis-

<a id="ga02-p76"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=76 printed_page=null -->

trator of the local program of the individual missionary, and to work with them in developing their work.

10. To coordinate the work of Presbyteries in the endorsement of military and institutional chaplains and to represent chaplains in relation to military and civil authorities.

11. To be a servant to the General Assembly. The General Assembly as servant to the churches shall establish and/or approve general guidelines and policies within which the committee shall implement the denomination's efforts to fulfill the Great Commission. The Committee shall have the responsibility for immediate supervision of the Committee staff, which the General Assembly shall elect.

The Rev. William J. Stanway, Chairman of the Committee of Commissioners on Bills and Overtures presented the following report of the Committee, which was adopted:

REPORT OF THE COMMITTEE OF COMMISSIONERS ON BILLS AND OVERTURES

I. The Committee of Commissioners on Bills and Overtures considered the following items referred to it:

Overtures 1, 3, and 6, pp. 23-24;

Overture 13; p. 24;

Resolutions 1 and 2, pp. 30-31.

II. Your Committee recommends:

That Overture 1, p. 23, requesting the General Assembly to call to the attention of Sessions the need of laborers for the Lord's harvest, and to set aside a day when Sessions can confront congregations with the challenge of Luke 10:2, be answered by reference to Recommendation 6 on page

2. That Overture 3, p. 23, requesting the General Assembly to affirm the right of office bearers and constituents to hold membership in secret associations and fraternities, be answered by declaring that inasmuch as membership in the Presbyterian Church in America is under the jurisdiction of Sessions and Presbyteries, this matter does not properly come under the jurisdiction of the General Assembly. (The Committee vote was 15 to 1.)

3. That Overture 6, p. 24, proposing preparation of a service book of liturgical forms, be answered as follows:

It is our understanding that this matter is under consideration by the Committee on Constitutional Documents, and we call attention also to the fact that optional forms for special worship occasions are available from such sources as The Book of Common Prayer.

4. That Overture 13, p. 24, concerning the Baptism of the Holy Spirit, be answered by reference to the action of the General Assembly in adopting the report of the Ad-Interim Committee to Study the Question of Spiritual Gifts (2-28)

5. That Resolution 1, p. 30, concerning the unity and harmony of respective congregations in the Body of Christ which is the Church, be received as information.

6. That Resolution 2, p. 30, concerning the Annuity Fund, be answered by calling to the attention of the General Assembly the fact that this resolution was improperly referred to the Committee of Commissioners on Insurance and Annuities adopted by this General Assembly p. 52)

W. J. Stanway, Chairman

2-100 Report of the Committee of Commissioners on Interchurch Relations

The Rev. John W. Stodghill, Chairman of the Committee of Commissioners on Interchurch Relations, presented the following report, which was adopted as amended:

<a id="ga02-p77"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=77 printed_page=null -->

# REPORT OF THE COMMITTEE OF COMMISSIONERS ON INTER-CHURCH RELATIONS

I. The Committee of Commissioners on Interchurch Relations considered the following items referred to it:

The Report of the Sub-Committee on Interchurch Relations of the Committee on Administration.

Communication from the Presbyterian Church of Australia.

Communication from the Associate Reformed Presbyterian Church.

Communications from three non church-related organizations; Concerned Presbyterians, National Presbyterian and Reformed Fellowship, and the Lord's Day Alliance.

## II. YOUR COMMITTEE RECOMMENDS:

### A. That the report of the Subcommittee on Interchurch Relations be approved (This includes everything up to the quote on page 146 in the Appendix), and that the following Recommendations be adopted:

1. That the following statement constitute the policy of the General Assembly in these two areas of Interchurch Relations:

(a) **CHURCHES IN CORRESPONDENCE**: The Presbyterian Church in America recognizes that the Body of Christ on earth consists of many parts and that Churches other than our own are Christian Churches, bearing a faithful testimony to the saving Gospel of Jesus Christ and the visible fellowship which is the fruit of that testimony. With all such churches, subsumed under and defined by the commonly accepted meaning of the term Evangelical, this Church desires to be in correspondence.

(b) **CHURCHES IN FRATERNAL RELATION**: Within the fellowship of Christian Churches, there are some specially defined by doctrine and polity similar to those of the Presbyterian Church in America. Of such are those denominations adhering by conviction and public subscription to one or more of the historic Reformed confessions, viz., the Westminster Confession of Faith, The Belgic Confession, the Canons of Dort, the Heidelberg Catechism, the Westminster Larger and Shorter Catechisms; and practising historic Presbyterian polity, viz., government by representatives of the people according to the Scriptural pattern of the eldership, with parity among ministers and ordained laymen. Among such, moreover there is the plain and unequivocal acceptance of the Old and New Testaments as the inerrant Word of God, written, the only infallible rule of faith and practice.

With such Churches, the Presbyterian Church in America wishes to enter the possibilities and potentials of fraternal relations, such a connection to include:

1. Appointing of delegates to each other's supreme judicatories as a token of mutual friendship and interest in the Lord.

2. Keeping each other informed of our progress in the Kingdom through an exchange of the acts of our General Assemblies (or Synods).

3. Seeking through consultation and advice, encouragement and assistance in witness and service, the solution of spiritual and ecclesiastical problems.

4. Cooperating, as much as possible, in programs of mutual interest.

To carry out these objectives, the General Assembly shall elect a Committee on Interchurch Relations to function under the administrative oversight of the Permanent Committee on Administration. This Committee will seek to become informed of all contact made by agencies of the Presbyterian Church in America with corresponding agencies of other denominations and will offer its services to such agencies in the development of such contacts.

The Committee, further, will be responsible for the development of fraternal relations wherever these may be desired, sought or authorized by the General Assembly, and will nominate to the Assembly

<a id="ga02-p78"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=78 printed_page=null -->

fraternal delegates to those churches with which the General Assembly desires to establish such relations.

2. That the following statement constitutes the policy of General Assembly in the area of functional relations with other Christian bodies:

From time to time may authorize functional relations with cooperative evangelical organizations existing to perform specific tasks related to the total interests of the Church. Membership in such bodies, however, shall be only by vote of the Assembly.

The General Assembly further authorizes contacts and consultations within the wider Christian community where these, in the judgment of the Committee on Interchurch Relations, may extend the witness of this Church to the advantage of the cause of Jesus Christ; except that no decisions or commitments may be made in the name of the Presbyterian Church in America without express authorization of the Assembly.

3. That the General Assembly implement this policy as follows:

a. That the General Assembly authorize the establishment of fraternal relations with the following Churches, if the way be clear:

- The Associate Reformed Presbyterian Church
- The Christian Reformed Church
- The Orthodox Presbyterian Church
- The Reformed Presbyterian Church of North America
- The Reformed Presbyterian Church Evangelical Synod

b. That the membership of the Committee on Interchurch Relations be set at 3 ministers and 3 ruling elders, established in classes, with the Stated Clerk of the General Assembly as member ex officio. The Committee suggests that the new class proposed to the Assembly by the Nominating Committee be added to the present membership in order to increase the total to the above recommended number: this class to be designated Class of 1977, and the others designated Class of 1976 and Class of 1975, respectively.

c. That the Assembly ratify the decision of the Committee on Interchurch Relations to participate in a plenary session of all such committees of those Churches named in 3 a, above and authorize such participation in a meeting proposed for October 25-26, in Pittsburgh, Pa.

B. 1. That the communication from the Presbyterian Church in Australia be answered as follows:

That General Assembly authorize the Committee on Interchurch Relations to enter into correspondence with the Presbyterian Church in Australia with a view to establishing possible overseas contact with that Church.

2. That communications from non-church related organizations be answered as follows:

a. That requests for speaking time by representatives of groups not of the church be answered in the negative, but that representatives of such groups be introduced at such time that other distinguished guests are introduced to the Assembly.

b. That the request from the Lord's Day Alliance that the Presbyterian Church in America send an observer to their meeting, October 17, 1974, in Nashville, Tennessee, be answered in the affirmative, and that the Interchurch Relations Committee be directed to name an observer to that meeting.

Respectfully submitted,

John W. Stodghill, Chairman
E. C. Case, Clerk

# 2-102 Report of the Committee of Commissioners on Christian Education and Publications

The Rev. Billy G. Combs, Chairman of the Committee of Commissioners on Christian Education and Publication presented the following report, which was adopted as amended:

## REPORT OF THE COMMITTEE OF COMMISSIONERS ON CHRISTIAN EDUCATION AND PUBLICATIONS

### I. ITEMS REFERRED AND CONSIDERED

- A. Minutes of the Permanent Committee for Christian Education and Publications;
- B. Report of the Permanent Committee for Christian Education and Publications; (Appendix J. p. 149)
- C. Item 1-82 from the First Assembly Minutes, p. 42.

### II. STATEMENTS OF THE ISSUES DISCUSSED

- A. Cooperative effort with Great Commission Publications;
- B. Responsibility of the Permanent Committee for C. E. and Publications;
- C. The proposed Budget for the Permanent Committee for C. E. and Publications;
- D. Denominational magazine;
- E. Reassignment of 1-82, p. 42.
- F. Authority of Permanent Committee for C. E. and Publications to price and sell materials it provides;
- G. Recommendation of list of study materials;
- H. Nellois Bible Camp and Conference Grounds.

### III. AUDIT

The financial report as submitted was approved. No adult is available at this time.

### IV. RECOMMENDATIONS

1. That the Assembly express its thanks to the living God for His manifold blessings, bestowed upon the NPC in the first months of her existence; for the generous financial support given by members and member churches; for the revival of love for Christ and His Word which is evidenced on every hand; for the effectiveness of the ministry of the permanent committees in spite of many obstacles both human and satanic;
2. That the Assembly endorse the “Introduction” to this report as setting forth a Biblical and Reformed interpretation of the Great Commission of Jesus Christ and as a renewed denominational commitment to the whole task of the whole church: Evangelism, Church, Growth, and Education;
3. That the Assembly reaffirm the job description given to the Committee for Christian Education and Publications by the First General Assembly and encourage the Committee in the pursuit of its rightful goals as outlined in the Minutes of the First General Assembly, 1-77, pp. 56-57;
4. That the Assembly encourage local churches and presbyteries to train their officers, leaders, and teachers, using local or General Assembly staff instructors as the Lord leads and enables.
5. That the Rev. Paul G. Settle be elected to the Office of Coordinator for Christian Education and Publications for the year 1975, and that the present office and program staff of the Committee be continued;
6. That the recommended budget for 1975, as printed on page , be approved. Action on this recommendation was postponed until the report of the Committee on Administration is heard.
7. That a Committee be authorized to publish a denominational magazine or newspaper to include editorial comment, articles of general and particular interest, news of the denomination and the world of religion; (10-1) This recommendation was tabled by the Assembly
8. That the Women in the Church of the NPC be commended for their generous contribution of more than $18,000.00 through their first annual Love Gift offering;
9. That the Assembly approve the Production of Radio Programs by the

<a id="ga02-p80"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=80 printed_page=null -->

Mission to U. S. Committee as the object for the 1975 Love Gift of the WIC;

10. That Presbyteries or combinations of Presbyteries be encouraged to conduct family conferences during the year 1975.

11. That the Committee for Christian Education and Publications of the Presbyterian Church in America enter upon a Joint Venture in Publications with the Christian Education Committee of the Orthodox Presbyterian Church, such venture to be based upon the principles of equal control of editorial policy and a share of financial support, with a view to making the Joint Venture the publishing arm of the two denominations.

12. That the “Suggestions for Adult Study Classes and/or Groups” be received as information and recommended to Sessions for their use in devising curriculum, with the understanding that the recommendation does not imply endorsement of everything in the books, nor of any other works by these authors.

13. That Item 1-82 from the Minutes of the First General Assembly be recommitted to the Permanent Committee for Christian Education and Publications. The Permanent Committee has not completed its action on this item.

14. That the Minutes of the Permanent Committee for Christian Education and Publications be approved.

15. That the Permanent Committee for Christian Education and Publications be commended by the General Assembly for diligent and faithful work in its behalf.

Billy G. Combs, Chairman

## 2-104 Report of the Committee of Commissioners on Mission to the United States

The Rev. Erskine L. Jackson resumed the chair as Moderator.

Dr. Palmer Robertson, Chairman of the Committee of Commissioners on Mission to the United States presented the following report, which was adopted:

### REPORT OF THE COMMITTEE OF COMMISSIONERS ON MISSION TO THE UNITED STATES

I. The Committee of Commissioners on Mission to the United States considered the following items referred to it:

<a id="ga02-p81"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=81 printed_page=null -->

Minutes of the Permanent Committee for meetings December 4, 1973, January 18, 1974, May 10, 1974 and June 28-29, 1974.

Report of the Permanent Committee and Supplementary Report of the Committee on Mission to the United States, (Appendix K, p. 157)

II. Your Committee Recommends:

A. That the minutes of the meetings December 4, 1973, January 18, 1974, March 1-2, 1974, May 10, 1974 and June 28-29, 1974 be approved, but recommends that all future minutes be signed by the Chairman and Clerk of the Committee. (15-0)

B. That the narrative report of the Committee on Mission to United States be approved and that the following recommendations be adopted:

1. That the General Assembly express its thanks to the sovereign God for the prayer and financial support which individuals, churches, and Presbyteries have given to the Committee on Mission to the United States since the First General Assembly and for the work which He has permitted this Committee to begin in 1974.

2. That the General Assembly adopt as its official position the part of this report entitled "Introduction" thereby affirming that there are many valid reasons from a Reformed point of view for actively engaging in home mission work.

3. That the General Assembly reaffirm the position of the First General Assembly that no work of this Committee be carried on in cooperation with those denominations which are a part of the National or World Councils of Churches.

4. That the General Assembly encourage all pastors and churches who have families leaving their area and moving into an area where there is a church or mission work of this denomination to encourage those families to affiliate with the church or mission church in the area where they are moving.

5. That the General Assembly now hear and act upon the nomination to be made by this Committee of the Reverend Mr. Larry Mills to serve as Coordinator for the General Assembly's Committee on Mission to the United States.

6. That the General Assembly call to the attention of all Presbyteries the need for financially assisting mission work which is begun outside the bounds of any existing Presbytery.

7. That the General Assembly approve a Day of Prayer for home mission work.

8. That General Assembly adopt as its policy that the Committee on Mission to U. S. continue taking advantage of the many opportunities for the establishment of new churches, with the constant thought in mind of firming up and substantiating what already has been done in 1974 by the establishment of more Presbyteries; and that these objectives be commended to the churches for prayer. (16-0)

9. That the General Assembly receive as information the pamphlet published by MUS entitled "I will Build My Church (Jesus) a brief and practical guide to beginning Reformed churches", and requests that it be commended to the churches. (16-0)

10. That the Book of Church Order (#8-3) be amended by inserting the words "organizing pastors" after the word "pastors" and before the word "teachers".

11. That the Church, which is authorized to call and appoint Teaching Elders to labour as Pastors (BCO #8-3), authorize the Committee on MUS to call Teaching Elders to be organizing pastors in areas not within the jurisdiction of an existing PCA Presbytery, provided the call is approved by the Teaching Elder's Presbytery. (BCO #22-1)

12. That the General Assembly authorize the Committee on MUS to establish a "Building Club" with the following purpose, membership, program and goal:

PURPOSE

To provide a means of helping the infant church begin to build the first unit of its church building.

<a id="ga02-p82"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=82 printed_page=null -->

**MEMBERSHIP**
Those who will pledge $10.00 per appeal, to be used completely for a specific church building program.

**PROGRAM**

- **a)** The assistance will be used only on MUS and Presbytery-approved programs.
- **b)** An appeal for help will be limited to a maximum of three a year, none to be less than three months apart.
- **c)** The assistance will be used only for the actual construction program, and only for the first building program of a church.
- **d)** Each member will receive detailed information about each proposal, and will receive progress reports.

**GOAL**
At least 5,000 members, 1974-75.

13. The Committee recommends that the General Assembly receive as information the following communication from the MUS Committee: “MUS brings to the attention of the PCA the availability of the Palmer Home, Columbus, Mississippi, for the care of orphans and dependents from broken homes.” (12-0)

III. The Committee notes that it received a financial Statement of the Permanent Committee through June 30, 1974 by way of the Committee’s minutes.

James T. McElrath, Clerk
Palmer Robertson, Chairman

The Rev. John Reeves, Chairman of the Committee of Commissioners on Review and Control of Presbyteries presented the following report, which was adopted as amended:

2-106 Report of the Committee of Commissioners on Administration

Ruling Elder James Abernathy, Chairman of the Committee of Commissioners on Administration, presented the following report, which was adopted:

**REPORT OF THE COMMITTEE OF COMMISSIONERS ON ADMINISTRATION**

I. The Committee of Commissioners on Administration was duly convened by Ruling Elder Jimmy Abernathy, Carolina Presbytery, Stanley, N. C. Mr. Jimmy Abernathy was elected to be Chairman. Teaching Elder B. I. Anderson was elected to be Secretary. Committee opened by prayer.

II. The Committee of Commissioners on Administration was made up of the following persons:

Ruling Elder, Jimmy Abernathy — Chairman
Teaching Elder, B. I. Anderson — Secretary
Members of the Committee were: R. H. Venable, C. E. Boyce, William H. Bell, Jr., Dale Umbreit, Allen Fleece, William Rose, Charles Olim, F. W. Payne, George Stafford, L. L. Langford, J. B. Holloway, Morse Up de Graff, D. A. Dunkerley, Walter Hattent.

III. Teaching Elder Gordon Reed, member of the Permanent Committee on Administration and advisor to the Committee moved that:

A. The committee on Administration recommend that the General Assembly accept the invitation of the Second Presbyterian Church of Greenville, South Carolina for the meeting of the General Assembly in 1976.

B. The time for the meeting of the General Assembly in 1976 be during the third week of September. Motion carried. We so move.

IV. Recommendations of the Committee on Administration's report given in the Appendix E Pages 130-134. The Committee recommends the Assembly approvete the following:

1. That the report of the trustees be heard. This report previously heard. See p. 49.

2. That we hear the following report from Rev. E. C. Cooley, Chairman of the Subcommittee on Insurance. See page 143. This Report previously heard by the Assembly p. 52.

3. That our present Stated Clerk, the Rev. Morton Smith, be employed through the 1975 General Assembly.

4. That the Committee on Administration be empowered to hire a provisional Stated Clerk if the need should arise between assemblies.

5. That our present consultant, Dr. Dan Moore, be employed as business consultant to June 1, 1975 and from that time as Business Administrator.

6. That the General Assembly recommend October 20th through November 17, 1974 as a season for special stewardship emphasis in the local congregation.

7. That the General Assembly accept the invitation of the First Presbyterian Church, Jackson, Mississippi. That the Third General Assembly of the National Presbyterian Church be held in Jackson, Mississippi the week of September 8, 1975.

8. That the responsibilities of the Insurance Subcommittee be placed in the hands of the trustees for the insurance and annuity fund after the 1975 General Assembly. Until then, the Insurance Subcommittee will continue to evaluate our major medical insurance and other insurance needs.

9. That the Trustees of the Insurance and Annuity Fund be authorized and directed to report directly to the General Assembly.

10. That the General Assembly instruct all Committees to report monthly, in a uniform manner, financial information to the Committee on Administration.

11. That the Assembly accept with gratitude the generous gift of $100,000 under the following conditions:

<a id="ga02-p85"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=85 printed_page=null -->

(1) The donor has requested that the money be used for some special project or projects which in the opinion of the Committee on Administration will help undergird the work and program of the Presbyterian Church in America.

(2) Pending the decision of the Committee on Administration as to the purpose for which the money will be used, the funds shall be invested in a Certificate of Deposit, U.S. Treasury bills or such other securities as the Committee on Administration considers proper. Interest received may either be used for current operating expenses of the four Committees or it may be added to the corpus of the funds.

(3) If the Committee on Administration has not allocated the funds as provided in (1) above within 3 years from the date of receipt, the donor shall have the right to order the money distributed among the four Committees of the Church in such proportions as he sees fit.

(4) The money is not to be used for the current operating expenses of the Church's four committees.

12. That the Assembly instruct the Committee in consultation with the other Permanent Committees to recommend a worthy project for the gift mentioned in recommendation 11 and report back to the 1975 General Assembly.

13. That the General Assembly direct the Stated Clerks of Presbyteries to report all changes in their rolls to the Stated Clerk of the General Assembly within one week after such changes have been made.

14. That the report of the Sub-committee on Interchurch Relations be heard. See page 146. This report previously heard by the Assembly, p. 74.

15. That the report of the Sub-committee on Judicial Business be heard. See page 147-148. This report previously heard by the Assembly, p. 71.

16. That the General Assembly approve the Recommendation that all non-designated General Assembly benevolent money be distributed according to the percentages adopted in the 1975 budget.

17. That an item be added to the budget for Committee on Administration for operation of moderator's office of $1,000.00.

18. That all travel expenses incurred by the moderator on denominational business be paid by the denomination, and that such expenses incurred at the request of permanent committees, churches, presbyterys or other agencies be borne by that agency.

19. That the cost of promoting the Christmas Gift for ministerial relief be paid out of the ministerial relief fund.

20. That the responsibility for preparing and distributing stewardship materials for use in the local churches be placed in the hands of the Committee of Christian Education and Publications.

VI. Committee of Commissioners on Administration recommend General Assembly approve work of the Permanent Committee on Administration.

VII. Recommend that the General Assembly approve the following "In light of the expanding geographical growth of the Presbyterian Church in America that the General Assembly instruct the Permanent Committee on Administration to give serious consideration and make recommendation as to the most convenient dates and locations of the 1977 and subsequent General Assembly meetings.

VIII. Consideration of the Assembly Budget

It was determined that the Assembly would first approve of individually additions to the budget due to actions of the Second Assembly, and then treat the budgets of the individual committees as a whole.

1. The budget of the Committee on Mission to the World was increased by $20,000 to provide for additional personnel involved in preparing the manual. See paragraph 2-88, item II, B, 9, page 68.

2. An additional item of $4,000 was provided for the Ad Interim Committee to Study the Question of the Number of Officers of the Church, to be added to the budget of the Committee on Administration.

3. An additional item of $2,000 was provided for the Subcommittee on Interchurch Relations, to be added to the Budget of the Committee on Administration.

<a id="ga02-p86"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=86 printed_page=null -->

4. An addition of $25,200 was added to the budget of the Committee for Christian Education and Publications.

5. The total budgets for the four Permanent Committees was set as follows:

|  Committee on Administration | $ 122,000  |
| --- | --- |
|  Committee for Christian Education and Publications | 467,200  |
|  Committee on Mission to the United States | 453,000  |
|  Committee on Mission to the World | 810,000  |
|  Total | $1,852,000  |

The Committee for Christian Education and Publications was authorized to rearrange its budget within the total approved.

The budgets of the four Permanent Committees were adopted as a whole, with the above indicated totals.

The Report of the Committee of Commissioners on Administration as a whole was adopted.

Ruling Elder Jimmy Abernathy, Chairman

2-107 Scholarship Fund

The General Assembly approved the establishment of a student scholarship fund, to be designated as the recipient of any memorial funds given for scholarships.

2-108 Report of the Thanks Committee

The following report of the Thanks Committee was approved as amended:

COMMITTEE ON THANKS

Whereas, The Second General Assembly of the Presbyterian Church in America has met by the gracious providence of God and under the headship of the Lord Jesus Christ;

Therefore, Be It Resolved that this Assembly express its gratitude to our heavenly Father for the evident guidance and blessing of the Holy Spirit in our deliberations; for the maintenance of the unity of the Spirit in the bond of peace; and for every report of the growth and progress of the work of the gospel throughout our church.

Moreover, Be It Resolved that we sincerely thank;

1. The First Presbyterian Church of Macon, Georgia, together with the Pastor, the Rev. James M. Baird, Session, Deacons, Committees, Hosts, Hostesses and Staff for their thorough preparation for the meeting of this Assembly; the use of their historic and most adequate facilities; the generous provision for all our needs; and warm hospitality throughout the sessions.

2. The Rev. Henry Hope and the Vineville Presbyterian Church of Macon for their service and cooperation in all phases of the hosting of this Assembly.

3. The Mulberry Street United Methodist Church and the Pastor, Dr. C. W. Hancock, whose hospitality we enjoyed during our noon-days meals in the spacious church facilities.

4. Dr. Dan Moore, who has given over-all supervision to the operation of the Assembly, and his Assembly staff, who have provided us with the pages of necessary reports, and many other services.

5. The Committee on Arrangements for the planning of the Lord's Supper, the morning worship services, and the lectures presented by Dr. Francis Schaeffer.

6. Dr. Schaeffer for his profound insights into God's truth, his strong encouragements, and his wise counsel for our lives and that of our church.

7. Mrs. Edith Schaeffer for her messages under the sponsorship of the Women in the Church of the First Presbyterian Church of Macon, of the First Presbyterian Church of Jackson, Mississippi, and of the Briarwood Church of Birmingham, Alabama.

8. Retiring Moderator, D. Jack Williamfson for his ministry of the Word and his service to our Church.

<a id="ga02-p87"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=87 printed_page=null -->

9. The Moderator of this Assembly, the Rev. Erskine Jackson, for his wise and patient direction of our deliberations.

10. The efficient work of the Stated Clerk, Dr. Morton Smith, and the Recording Clerks, John Spencer and James Kemper, and the temporary clerks.

11. Ruling Elder Ligon Duncan, who true to his word given at the First General Assembly has provided all the signers of the Message to all Churches with beautiful reproductions of the Message to all Churches and the signatures on parchment.

Respectfully submitted
Adrian DeYoung, Chairman
David Jussley
L. M. Young
