# Appendix A

## RULES FOR ASSEMBLY OPERATIONS

### As Adopted by the General Assembly

#### I. Organization of a General Assembly's Meeting

1-1 The Assembly shall be opened with a sermon by the retiring Moderator. The Lord's Supper shall be celebrated after the opening sermon.

1-2 The Stated Clerk shall present a report on the enrollment of Commissioners, and declare if a quorum is present. If it is present, then the Assembly shall be declared to be properly constituted for the transaction of business.

1-3 The first order of business shall be the election of a Moderator. There shall be only one nominating speech not to exceed five minutes for each nominee. No seconding speeches shall be permitted.

1-4 If more than one Commissioner is nominated, election shall be by ballot, on ballots provided by the Stated Clerk. Tellers appointed by the Stated Clerk shall gather and count the ballots, and report the tabulation to the Stated Clerk. If no nominee receives a majority of the votes cast, a second ballot shall be called on the two nominees who receive the highest number of votes on the first ballot. The Moderator shall declare an election when a nominee receives a majority of the votes cast by the commissioners present and voting.

1-5 As soon as a Moderator shall have been declared elected he shall assume his constitutional duties as Moderator.

#### II. The Moderator

2-1 The Moderator shall preside at all sessions of the Assembly except when he may temporarily invite another Commissioner to act as the presiding officer.

2-2 The Moderator shall call the succeeding Assembly to order and preside over its sessions until a successor has been elected. Ordinarily he shall preach a retiring Moderator's sermon. If the Moderator is unable to act the Stated Clerk shall call the Assembly to order and preside over its sessions until a Moderator has been elected.

#### III. The Stated Clerk

3-1 The Stated Clerk shall be elected in connection with the annual report of the Committee on Administration, which shall present a nomination. It is understood that further nominations are in order. A new Stated Clerk shall assume office at the end of the Assembly meeting.

3-2 The Stated Clerk shall perform the duties assigned by the Book of Church Order and by the Standing Rules of the General Assembly, and such other duties as are assigned by action of the Assembly. The Stated Clerk shall administer these duties under supervision of the Committee on Administration.

3-3 The Stated Clerk shall prepare and distribute, with the cooperation of the Committee for Christian Education and Publications, a Handbook for Commissioners prior to the meeting of the Assembly to all commissioners. This Handbook shall contain a proposed docket, overtures, reports of permanent committees, reports of ad interim committees and of special committees, and any other information regarding the Assembly that may be useful to the commissioners. The Handbook shall be mailed so as to reach commissioners one month prior to the convening of the Assembly. Items received too late for inclusion in the Handbook shall be mailed to commissioners in the form of a supplement, if possible, or be distributed to them at the time of registration.

3-4 The Stated Clerk shall assemble the items of business to come before the Assembly and refer each item to the proper committee. If the Clerk has question regarding reference, he is to consult with the Committee on Judicial Business before making reference.

3-5 The Stated Clerk shall keep the Minutes of the General Assembly. He shall publish them annually with statistical reports of the Church and reports of the agencies of the Assembly, and give certified extracts therefrom when the business of the Assembly requires. He shall prepare and supervise the printing of the Minutes in cooperation with the Committee on Christian Education and Publications. The costs shall be borne by the Committee on Administration.

<a id="ga02-p92"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=92 printed_page=null -->

3-6 The Stated Clerk shall have the privilege of the floor in all matters pertaining to his office, shall have the privilege of the floor to present necessary information on business before the meeting concerning the work and report of any committee on which he serves, and at such times when the Moderator, the coordinators, chairmen of Assembly committees (or their designated representatives), or any commissioner may request that he clarify matters before the court.

3-7 The Stated Clerk shall be an ex officio member of the Committee on Interchurch Relations, and shall serve as a member of or an advisory member of any such other committees as the General Assembly may direct.

3-8 The Stated Clerk shall be the parliamentarian of the General Assembly.

IV The Assembly Arrangements

4-1 A brief worship service shall begin each morning session.

4-2 The first order of the day, except the opening day, at the beginning of the business session, and during the day as may be necessary, shall be the presentation of a docket listing the business which is to be considered that day.

V Communications and Overtures

5-1 A communication to the General Assembly is formal correspondence received by the Stated Clerk from other churches, from interchurch agencies to which this Church may be related, from committees of this Church on matters which could not be included in regular reports, and from organized bodies outside the Church proper having business with the General Assembly.

5-2 Ordinarily, communications from individuals shall not be received by the General Assembly, unless they originate with persons who have no other access to the Assembly. If the Assembly desires to receive and consider any such communications, other than as information, the Stated Clerk shall recommend reference to the proper Assembly Committee. Letters, telegrams, or telephone calls from communicants or congregations of the Presbyterian Church in America are not proper communications, and are not to be received by the Assembly.

5-3 The Stated Clerk shall recommend to the Assembly reference for all proper communications.

5-4 An overture ordinarily is the request of a presbytery for action by the General Assembly upon a specific matter.

5-5 Upon receipt the Stated Clerk shall refer to the Permanent Committee on Judicial Business all overtures requesting amendment of the Book of Church Order or interpretation thereof by the General Assembly. All other overtures shall be referred by the Clerk to the appropriate Committee for Commissioners. All overtures shall be printed in the Handbook with reference for consideration indicated.

5-6 All overtures requiring reference to the Committee on Judicial Business shall be delivered by July 1 to the Stated Clerk in order to be referred to the Committee. No overture requiring reference to the Permanent Committee on Judicial Business received after July 1 by the Stated Clerk shall be referred or considered by the General Assembly convening in that year.

5-7 All other overtures shall be delivered to the Stated Clerk by June 1 in order to be included in the Handbook for the next meeting of the General Assembly. Overtures received after the Handbook is printed, and at least one (1) month (31 days) prior to the opening of the General Assembly shall be reported to the Assembly by the Stated Clerk, together with reference. No overtures received by the Stated Clerk less than one month prior to the opening of the meeting of the General Assembly shall be referred to or considered by the General Assembly convening in that year.

5-8 No overture will be considered by the General Assembly until it first has been presented to a presbytery. If approved by the presbytery, it will come before the Assembly as the overture of that court. An overture requested by an individual communicant, a teaching elder, or a session, but rejected by the presbytery, may be presented to the Assembly, provided the fact that it was rejected by the presbytery is clearly stated with the overture.

<a id="ga02-p93"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=93 printed_page=null -->

## VI Reports to the General Assembly

6-1 The Board of Directors, the permanent committees, ad interim committees, and all other agencies of the Assembly shall make annual reports, which shall be transmitted to the Stated Clerk by June 1. These reports shall be referred to the proper Committee of Commissioners by the Clerk.

## VII New Business

7-1 Any matter presented in any form which has not been received by the Stated Clerk prior to the opening of the General Assembly shall be treated as new business.

7-2 New business must be presented to the Assembly before the close of the second day of business.

7-3 All new business presented by members of the court must be in written form in triplicate, and if received shall be referred to the proper Committee of Commissioners.

7-4 The Committee on Judicial Business shall be available as a reference committee, to assist the Clerk in referring all new business coming to the Assembly.

7-5 The appropriate committee shall receive and consider all such references, deliberate and report to the Assembly in compliance with the directions of these Rules.

7-6 The Committee on Judicial Business shall serve as a Constitutional Committee. All matters introduced as new business, if received, and touching on constitutional matters, including requested rulings by the Moderator on questions of order involving constitutional questions, shall be referred in writing to the Committee on Judicial Business for consideration.

7-7 The Committee on Judicial Business shall consider each such constitutional matter referred to it, and make recommendation directly to the Assembly.

## VIII Committees of Commissioners

8-1 All business shall ordinarily come to the floor of the Assembly for final action through Committees of Commissioners, except reports of Ad Interim Committees, which shall report directly to the Assembly. The following Committees of Commissioners shall handle the matters indicated:

|  Committees | Reports of | Overtures, resolutions or communications  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  1. Administration | Permanent Committee | Touching Administrative matters  |
|  2. Bills and Overtures |  | Of general nature  |
|  3. Board of Directors | Board of Directors | Touching the corporation  |
|  4. Christian Education and Publications | Permanent Committee | Touching Christian Education and Publications  |
|  5. Insurance and Annuities | Sub-committee | Touching insurance and annuities  |
|  6. Interchurch Relations | Sub-committee | Touching comity, cooperation, relations to other churches.  |
|  7. Judicial Business | Permanent Committee | Touching Constitution  |
|  8. Mission to the United States | Permanent Committee | Touching home missions  |
|  9. Mission to the World | Permanent Committee | Touching world missions  |
|  10. Review and control of Presbyteries | Presbytery Minutes |   |

8-2 Committees of Commissioners for the Second General Assembly shall be named as follows: Following the opening session of the Assembly each Presbytery shall meet and elect one of their members to each of the Committees of Commissioners according to the following formula: Odd numbered presbyteries in the following listing shall elect teaching elders to the odd numbered committees listed above, and ruling elders to the even numbered committees.

<a id="ga02-p94"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=94 printed_page=null -->

Even numbered presbyteries shall elect teaching elders to the even numbered committees, and ruling elders to the odd numbered committees.

|  1. Calvary | 11. North Georgia  |
| --- | --- |
|  2. Carolina | 12. Pacific  |
|  3. Central Georgia | 13. Southern Florida  |
|  4. Covenant | 14. Tennessee Valley  |
|  5. Evangel | 15. Texas  |
|  6. Grace | 16. Vanguard  |
|  7. Gulf Coast | 17. Warrior  |
|  8. Mid Atlantic | 18. Western Carolina  |
|  9. Mississippi Valley | 19. Westminster  |
|  10. New River |   |

In the event that a Presbytery does not have sufficient Teaching Elders, Ruling Elders may be named to the Committees to which they have been assigned Teaching Elders at the discretion of the Presbytery. In the event that a Presbytery is not able to supply members for all of the Committees, the Presbytery may select the Committees to which they wish to send representatives.

No commissioner serving on a Permanent Committee or Sub-Committee or the staffs thereof shall be eligible to serve on the Committees of Commissioners.

For Assemblies subsequent to the Second Assembly, each Presbytery shall prior to the meeting of the Assembly elect one of its commissioners to each of the Committees of Commissioners, dividing them as to ruling and teaching elders by a formula established by the Assembly. In the event that a duly elected commissioner of a Presbytery is unable to attend the Assembly, his alternate shall take his place on the Committee. No Commissioner serving on a particular Permanent Committee or Sub-Committee shall be eligible to serve on the Committee of Commissioners treating that Permanent Committee's report.

8-3 The Conveners of the Committees shall be designated by the Board of Directors.

8-4 The Committees on Commissioners shall proceed as follows:

(1) At the proper time each committee shall assemble in its assigned room, elect a chairman and a secretary, review material in hand, appoint sub-committees as may be necessary, and begin its work.

(2) Each committee shall be available to reconvene to consider additional references that may come from the floor of the Assembly.

(3) A committee with a heavy work load of business requiring extended conference with parties not members of the committee may create subcommittees as needed.

(4) Meetings of a Committee of Commissioners shall ordinarily be open to the public as nonparticipating visitors, to the extent made possible by the physical facilities of the available meeting room. The Committee may go into executive session under Robert's Rules of Order when the Committee determines, and must be in executive session when it adopts finally the report to the General Assembly. The Chairman and members of the Permanent Committee, and the Coordinator shall meet for consultation with the Committee reviewing their work. The Committee of Commissioners may invite other persons for consultative purposes, when this is felt necessary to the Committee's performance of its business.

8-5 The report of the Committee of Commissioners shall be brief and concise. It shall include the following:

(1) A list of all items referred to and considered by the Committee.

(2) A statement of the issues discussed.

(3) A report of all recommendations contained in an agency or committee report under consideration. (If any of the recommendations contained in a report were not approved, this shall be reported with reasons. New recommendations may be added, with words of explanation. Amendments to original recommendations shall be reported and explained.)

(4) A statement of the division of the vote on every official recommendation made to or by the Committee.

<a id="ga02-p95"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=95 printed_page=null -->

(5) Reference to overtures by number with brief statement of content and recommended answer.

(6) Reference to communications by number with brief statement of content and recommended answer.

(7) Only such portions of narrative sections of the printed reports as are necessary to make the report of the Committee of Commissioners intelligible.

(8) A note that the audit of the reporting Committee has been received and that the Committee is taking any necessary action on any recommendation of its audits.

8-6 The Chairman of the Permanent Committee or his designated representative shall be granted the privilege of the floor of the Assembly by the Chairman of the Committee of Commissioners to present the report of the Permanent Committee to the Assembly. No report printed in the Handbook shall be read in full to the Assembly. The Chairman of the Committee of Commissioners shall present the recommendations of the Committee of Commissioners to the Assembly. The Chairman of the Permanent Committee or his designated representative shall have the privilege of defending the position of the Permanent Committee on any recommendations in which the Committee of Commissioners differ from the Permanent Committee's report.

8-7 Minutes of the Permanent Committee shall be submitted to the Committee of Commissioners for review.

8-8 Informational presentation of some special aspects of the work reported by a Committee of Commissioners shall be limited to five minutes.

8-9 Any recommendation affecting the Budget of the Assembly or the coordination of the program of the church shall be referred to the Committee of Commissioners on Administration.

8-10 The completed report of a Committee of Commissioners shall contain the full text of the report and shall be handled as follows:

(1) Typed, double spaced, original and two carbon copies, by Assembly stenographers.

(2) Proofread and signed by the chairman of the committee; and then delivered to the Stated Clerk when duplicated copies are available for the commissioners.

(3) Docketed by the Program Committee (Moderator. Stated Clerk) for consideration by the Assembly.

(4) Presented to the Assembly by the chairman or his designate, by reading through the entire text of the report from the original typed copy. Any change ordered by the Assembly shall be noted and included by the chairman with the assistance of the Stated Clerk on the original copy.

(5) The report, as adopted by the Assembly, shall be filed with the Recording Clerk for the permanent record.

8-11 No partial report of a Committee of Commissioners shall be presented without the consent of the Assembly.

## IX Parliamentary Procedure

9-1 Except as otherwise specifically provided in these Rules, REVISED ROBERTS RULES OF ORDER shall be the standard in parliamentary procedure.

9-2 The entire report of each Committee of Commissioners, including narrative, shall be read before any comment. When a minority of a Committee wishes to present a minority report, the member reporting for the minority shall have the privilege of presenting the minority report and moving it as a substitute for the portion of the majority report affected.

9-3 Each recommendation in each report must be read, considered and acted upon separately.

(1) The chairman moves the adoption.

(2) Motion to adopt is seconded from the floor.

(3) The Moderator asks: Is there objection or question?

(4) Hearing no objection or question, the Moderator states: It is adopted. (The above procedure is known as the “Short Form of Voting.”)

9-4 Procedure in debating a question:

(1) The chairman or his designate may answer questions concerning the report addressed to him through the Moderator.

<a id="ga02-p96"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=96 printed_page=null -->

(2) The chairman shall have an opportunity to make the final statement in debate.

(3) No commissioner may speak on the same question more than once until all desiring to speak have done so.

(4) When any main motion has been debated for 15 minutes the Moderator shall inquire of the court whether it wishes to place some definite limit upon further debate.

(5) Debate shall be free and open, with equal time being given to proponents and opponents in so far as possible.

9-5 Special Provisions

(1) The assistants to the Stated Clerk shall have the privilege of the floor when requested by the Moderator to render some specific service to the court.

(2) All motions shall be presented in writing and read before being voted upon.

X Amendment or Suspension of Rules

The Rules of the General Assembly may be amended or suspended only by a two thirds vote of the total enrollment of commissioners. A motion to amend is debatable. A motion to suspend is not debatable.

<a id="ga02-p95"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=97 printed_page=95 -->

# Appendix B

## MINUTES OF THE BOARD OF DIRECTORS OF THE NATIONAL PRESBYTERIAN CHURCH

April 15, 16, 1974
Montgomery, Alabama

1-1 The Board of Directors of the National Presbyterian Church met on the call of the Moderator at the First Presbyterian Church, Montgomery, Alabama, April 15-16, 1974.

1-2 The meeting was convened at 7:00 P.M., April 15 by the Moderator, Mr. W. Jack Williamson, who opened the meeting with a devotional. After the devotion a season of prayer was held, in which a number participated.

1-3 Present were the following Board members:

W. Jack Williamson, Moderator; Morton H. Smith, Clerk; Donald B. Patterson, Cecil Williamson, Harry Miller, Robert C. Cannada, Gordon Reed, Bill Joseph, John Spencer, Charles Dunahoo, Bob Ostenson, M. B. Swayze, Jules Vroon, Joseph Everett, Jr.

Also present were: Paul Settle, Larry Mills, John Kyle, David White, and Dan Moore.

1-4 A report of the activities of each of the Assembly Committees was presented by the respective Chairmen and Coordinators.

1-5 Mr. Cannada discussed the basic concept of the Corporation and the Board of Directors, as set forth in the By-laws.

1-6 Affiliation Resolutions

The question of whether it was advisable for formal resolutions to be adopted by congregations documenting their desire to become affiliated with and the conditions, if any, under which they will become so affiliated with Presbyteries and the affiliation of Presbyteries with the National Presbyterian Church was discussed, and it was agreed that this should be done. A proposed form of a Presbytery resolution was presented for consideration and later action.

1-7 The Board was recessed with prayer led by Cecil Williamson until the following morning at 8:30 A.M.

1-8 The Board reconvened at 8:30 A.M. on April 16, with a devotional led by the Moderator, followed by a season of prayer with a number participating.

1-9 Affiliation Resolutions

On motion made, seconded and unanimously adopted, it was resolved (1) that the Board of Directors recommend to Presbyteries that have already affiliated with or plan to affiliate with the National Presbyterian Church, that such affiliation be reflected by a resolution duly adopted by each such presbytery and that such resolution be submitted to and acted upon by the General Assembly of the National Presbyterian Church, and (2) that this Board of Directors also recommend to any congregation that is already affiliated with or that plans to affili-

<a id="ga02-p98"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=98 printed_page=null -->

ate with a presbytery, which presbytery is affiliated with or plans to affiliate with the National Presbyterian Church, that such affiliation be reflected by a resolution duly adopted by such congregations (either by action of the congregation or by the session if so authorized), and that such resolution be submitted to and acted upon by such presbytery; (3) that the Clerk be authorized and directed to prepare a suggested form of such resolutions, and after approval by the Moderator, that appropriate forms, together with a letter of explanation be sent to such presbyteries and congregations; (4) that such proposed resolutions and explanatory letter be sent in sufficient time to permit such congregations as desire to do so to have the presbytery receive and act upon such resolution prior to the next meeting of the General Assembly for submission to the next meeting of the General Assembly.

## 1-10 State Qualifications

On motion made, seconded and adopted, it was resolved that the Board of Directors authorize its officers to qualify the National Presbyterian Church (A Corporation) to do business in Alabama, Georgia and Mississippi, where Assembly Committees are based.

## 1-11 Address Change

On motion made, seconded and adopted it was resolved that the Board of Directors authorize the officers to change the official address of the Corporation to the office of the Business Manager, Plaza Office Building, Cross Country Plaza, Suite 206, Macon Road, Columbus, Georgia 31906.

## 1-12 By-Laws Amended

On motion made, seconded and adopted, the following amendments were made to the By-Laws, all of which are subject to ratification by the next General Assembly:

**Article II, Section 3** is hereby amended to read as follows:

Special meetings of the members, for any purposes, may be fixed at the annual General Assembly, or as prescribed in the Book of Church Order. No business shall be transacted at such special meeting except as stated in the notice thereof delivered to the members.

**Article II, Section 4** is amended to read as follows:

Written or printed notice, stating the place, date and hour of all special meetings called by the Board or Directors shall be given to all members not less than twenty (20) days nor more than ninety (90) days prior to the date of the meeting.

## 1-13 Other Changes Authorized

On motion made, seconded and unanimously carried, the Reverend Charles Dunahoo, Chairman of the Constitutional Documents Committee, was authorized to draft additional changes to the By-Laws that he deemed necessary or desirable to bring the By-Laws into conformity with the Book of Church Order, and supply such suggested changes to the Clerk for submission to the next meeting of the Board of Directors.

## 1-14 Temporary Committee Member Approved

Upon motion made, seconded and adopted, it was resolved that the

<a id="ga02-p99"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=99 printed_page=null -->

request of the Chairman of the Committee on Mission to the World be granted to the extent that such Committee be authorized to select a 1-15 The Board was recessed for lunch with prayer led by the Reverperson to act in the place of the Reverend Arnie Maves, who has resigned, until the next General Assembly. end John Kyle.

1-16 The Board was reconvened at 1:30 P.M.

1-17 By-Laws Amended

On motion made, seconded and adopted, the following amendments to the By-Laws were made, all which are subject to ratification by the next General Assembly:

Article III, Section 6 is hereby amended to read as follows:

Annual meetings of the Board of Directors shall be held each year immediately prior to the annual meeting of the General Assembly and at the same place. Notice shall be required to be given of the time and place of the annual meeting of the Board of Directors.

Article III, Section 7 is hereby amended to read as follows:

The Board of Directors, by resolution adopted by a majority of the full Board of Directors, may designate the place, date and time for regular meetings of the Board of Directors. Written or printed notice of such resolution should be given to all directors within a reasonable time after the adoption thereof. Notice of the time, place or purpose of such regular meetings of the Board of Directors shall be required to be given.

1-18 Monthly Reports

On motion made, seconded and unanimously adopted it was resolved that each of the Permanent Committees, except the Judicial Business Committee, should furnish to the Business Manager a monthly report showing at least the following information: the amount of money received, the amount disbursed and the amount in the bank.

1-19 Previous Acts Ratified

On motion made, seconded and unanimously adopted, it was resolved that the Board of Directors ratifies and approves all actions of all Permanent Committees, the Moderator and the Stated Clerk taken in behalf of, and in the name of the National Presbyterian Church up to this date.

1-20 Committee Authorizations

On motion duly made, seconded and unanimously carried, it was resolved that each Permanent Committee, except the Judicial Business Committee, be authorized to act for and in the name of the National Presbyterian Church in all activities necessary and desirable to the carrying out of assignments made by the General Assembly to the said committee, except for the buying or selling of any real property or the receiving of any real property to which any conditions are attached. Any borrowing by each Committee shall be limited to a maximum total of $50,000 under this authorization, unless express approval of the Board of Directors is obtained for any such excess.

In order to have the proper resolutions available for the committees the following resolutions were adopted:

## Resolution Authorizing Committees to Open or Continue Bank Accounts And Authorizing Withdrawals Therefrom

At a meeting of the Board of Directors of the National Presbyterian Church held at the First Presbyterian Church in the City of Montgomery, Alabama on April 16, 1974, pursuant to due notice, at which a quorum of the Board was present, on motion, duly seconded, the following resolutions unanimously adopted:

RESOLVED, That the following Permanent Committees of the National Presbyterian Church (A Corporation): The Committee on Administration; The Committee on Christian Education and Publications; The Committee on Mission to the United States and The Committee on Mission to the World; may upon a proper resolution duly adopted by the said committee, open (or continue) a bank account (or bank accounts) in a suitable bank, chosen by the said committee, in the name of this Corporation, or in the name of the said Committee, which is a constitutionally appointed committee of this corporation, that all monies, checks or other funds of the Corporation and its Committees may be deposited in said bank account (s), and that until otherwise notified in writing the said bank(s) is (are) hereby authorized to make payments from the funds of the Corporation on deposit with it, upon and according to the check of this Corporation through its Committee signed by the persons designated in the resolution of the said Committee; that said bank is authorized to receive for deposit or collection any items purporting to be endorsed in the corporate name of this Corporation or of the Committee of this Corporation; and that all such checks, drafts, notes or other negotiable papers endorsed or signed by this Corporation as aforesaid, including checks drawn to cash or bearer or to the individual order of any officer or employee of the Corporation, shall be honored and paid by said Bank without inquiry as to whether the same be drawn or required for the Corporation's business or benefit, and all such payments shall be charged to the Corporation's account; it is further resolved that any and all acts and things done pursuant to the authority of this resolution by the said Bank or by the officers of this Corporation be and the same are hereby fully ratified and approved. It is further resolved that this resolution shall continue in full force and effect until written notice of revocation, duly signed in the name of the Corporation by properly designated officers thereof and duly sealed, shall have been received by the said Bank.

## Resolution Authorizing Committees to Borrow Money and Sign Notes Not to Exceed a Maximum Total of $50,000

At a meeting of the Board of Directors of the National Presbyterian Church held at the First Presbyterian Church in the City of Montgomery, Alabama, on April 16, 1974, pursuant to due notice, at which a quorum of the Board was present, on motion, duly seconded, the following resolutions were unanimously adopted:

RESOLVED, that the following Permanent Committees of the National Presbyterian Church (A Corporation): The Committee on Administration; The Committee on Christian Education and Publications; The Committee on Mission to the United States and The Committee on

<a id="ga02-p101"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=101 printed_page=null -->

Mission to the World; be hereby authorized, upon proper resolution duly adopted by the said Committee, in the name of and for the account of this Corporation, or in the name of and for the account of the said Committee, which is a constitutionally appointed Committee of this Corporation, and on such terms as the said Committee may deem proper, to borrow from a bank or other lending agency as designated by the said Committee any sum or sums of money, not to exceed a maximum total of $50,000; to sign, execute and endorse such documents as may be necessary or required by said Bank or lending institution to evidence such indebtedness; to discount or rediscount with said Bank or lending institution and of the bills receivable held by this Corporation through the said Committee; to apply for and obtain from said Bank or lending institution, letters of credit, and to sign and execute agreements to secure said Bank or lending institution in connection therewith; to pledge and/or mortgage any moneys on deposit or any moneys otherwise in possession of said Bank or lending institution, and/or any bonds, stocks, bills receivable or other property of this Corporation to secure the payment of the indebtedness, liability or obligation of this Corporation to said Bank or lending institution, whether due or to become due and whether existing or hereafter incurred, howsoever arising; to withdraw and/or substitute any property of this Corporation held at any time by said Bank or lending institution, and to sign and execute trust receipts for the withdrawal of same when required; and generally to do and perform any and all instruments necessary or required by the said Bank or lending institution for its protection in its dealings with this Corporation.

RESOLVED, that the said Bank or lending institution be furnished with a certified copy of these resolutions and be hereby authorized to deal with the Committee or its duly appointed representatives hereinabove named under said authority unless and until it be expressly notified in writing to the contrary by this Corporation, and shall in writing acknowledge receipt of such notification; and said Bank shall at all times be protected in recognizing as such officers the persons duly certified by the Committees named in a certificate signed by any officer of this Corporation.

## Resolution Authorizing Committees to Open or Continue An Account with a Brokerage Firm

At a meeting of the Board of Directors of the National Presbyterian Church held at the First Presbyterian Church in the City of Montgomery, Alabama, on April 16, 1974, pursuant to due notice, at which a quorum of the Board was present, on motion, duly seconded, the following resolution was unanimously adopted:

RESOLVED, That the following Permanent Committees of the National Presbyterian Church (A Corporation): The Committee on Administration; The Committee on Christian Education and Publications; The Committee on Mission to the United States, and The Committee on Mission to the World; are hereby authorized and empowered to open and maintain an account with a Brokerage Firm as chosen by the said Committee, for the sale of stocks, bonds or securities, on exchanges of which the brokers are members or otherwise, and that any of the per-

<a id="ga02-p102"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=102 printed_page=null -->

sons designated by the said committee be, and he hereby is, authorized to give written or verbal instructions by telephone, or telegraph, or otherwise, to the brokers to sell stocks, bonds, or securities, either for immediate or future delivery, and he shall at all times have authority in every way to bind and obligate this corporation for the carrying out of any such contract, arrangement or transaction which shall, for or on behalf of this corporation, be entered into or made with or through the brokers; and the said brokers are authorized to receive from said officer(s) or from any other officer or employee of this corporation; stocks, bonds, or other security for the account of this corporation with said brokers; said brokers are further authorized to accept instructions from any officer named or any such committee as to the delivery of stocks, bonds, and other securities held in said account to be sold at the discretion of said officer; and the sale of any such stocks, bonds, or securities, sold as directed by him, shall be deemed as sold by this corporation; any such officer shall have the fullest authority at all times with reference to any such sale deemed by him to be proper to make or enter into for or on behalf of this corporation with the brokers or others as may be set forth in the authorization of such committee. That this resolution shall be and remain in full force and effect until written notice of the revocation hereof shall be delivered to the brokers. The officer(s) herein referred to are those designated by the above named Committees of this Corporation through a duly and properly adopted resolution.

## 1-21 Real Property

On motion made, seconded and unanimously adopted, it was resolved that any purchase or disposition of real property or the receiving of any property, real or personal, to which any condition is attached, must be approved by this Board of Directors.

## 1-22 Executive Committee

On motion made, seconded and unanimously carried, it is resolved that the Board of Directors does hereby establish an Executive Committee made up of the Moderator, Clerk and the Chairmen of the Permanent Committees, except the Judicial Business Committee, which Executive Committee shall be authorized to act upon any recommendation of a Permanent Committee that is administrative in character and such action shall constitute the action of the Board of Directors. The Executive Committee shall speak only through its Minutes, and the Minutes shall be submitted to the Board of Directors for ratification.

## 1-23 Policy on Conditional Gifts

On motion made, seconded and unanimously adopted, it is resolved that the Board of Directors establish as a matter of policy that before any conditional gifts are received in behalf of the National Presbyterian Church, the conditions shall be put into writing and submitted to the Board of Directors for approval. It was further resolved that as a matter of policy the Board of Directors does not favor receiving gifts that have conditions attached thereto, unless such conditions can be changed or removed by a three-fourths vote of the General Assembly by those present and voting.

<a id="ga02-p103"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=103 printed_page=null -->

## 1-24 Bonding and Insurance

On motion duly made, seconded and unanimously adopted, it was resolved that this Board of Directors does hereby request that the Chairmen and Coordinators of the Permanent Committees, except the Committee on Judicial Business, investigate the possibility of covering all treasurers under one blanket bond, having insurance policies covering all property of the National Presbyterian Church and other similar matters.

## 1-25 Legal Counsel

On motion duly made, seconded and unanimously adopted, it was resolved that the action of the Committee on Administration in employing the Honorable Owen Page, an attorney of Savannah, Georgia, be and the same is hereby approved with the understanding that Mr. Page’s legal services for which the National Presbyterian Church will be financially responsible shall be limited to the following:

1. Advice and consultation with the attorney representing a congregation or a proposed congregation; and
2. For rendering a “clearinghouse” service to all interested congregations and their attorneys consisting of the furnishing of copies of any briefs, court decisions, legal memoranda, or other documents dealing in any way with the legal issues involved in the ownership of property by congregations and their efforts to withdraw from other denominations, together with a list showing the names and addresses of all attorneys representing any congregations that have affiliated with or have indicated a desire to affiliate with any Presbytery affiliated with or which shall have indicated a desire to affiliate with the National Presbyterian Church.

## 1-26 Court Cases

On motion duly made, seconded and unanimously adopted, it was resolved that the National Presbyterian Church shall not as a denomination or through its attorney, take part in or enter its appearance in any court case involving any congregation without the express approval of and authorization by the Board of Directors.

## 1-27 Amicus Curiae Authorized

The Board of Directors recessed for a short period of time, during which recess the Executive Committee, with exception of Gordon Reed and Morton Smith discussed the possibility of having Mr. Owen Page file an amicus curiae brief in the United States Supreme Court in the case involving the Hillcrest Church of Seattle, Washington. The conclusion was reached by the Executive Committee that such authorization should be given and upon the reconvening of the Board of Directors this recommendation was reported to the Board. The Board then gave specific authorization that this be done. The Moderator was charged with the responsibility of notifying Mr. Page and with making the necessary financial arrangements with Mr. Page, and reporting them to the Committee on Administration.

## 1-28 Legal Defense Funds

It was suggested that any and all gifts made to any Permanent Committee of the National Presbyterian Church designated for use in connection with any legal problems in which the National Presbyterian Church, any Presbytery affiliated therewith or any congregation

<a id="ga02-p104"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=104 printed_page=null -->

affiliated therewith, shall, subject to the approval of the donor, be
turned over to the Committee on Administration to be used by this
Committee as authorized and directed by the Board of Directors.

1-39 Executive Committee Actions Approved

The following Minutes of the Executive Committee were admitted to record, and the actions of the Executive Committee reported in these Minutes were approved by the Board:

Action of the Executive Committee of the Board of Directors of the National Presbyterian Church, May 9, 1974

After consultation by phone with the Moderator, the Stated Clerk contacted all the members of the Executive Committee, except the Rev. Cecil Williamson, whom he was unable to reach. All agreed to the following actions:

1. The approval of the Action of the Moderator in hiring Ken Ryskamp to prepare a legal brief on the question of whether or not the name of the denomination is endangered by the threatened lawsuit by a congregation with the same name in Washington, D.C.

2. The approval of the action of the Stated Clerk in asking that Presbyteries supply to the Assembly's Nominating Committee nominees on the same basis as prescribed for naming the Nominating Committee itself, namely, one Ruling and one Teaching Elder for each two thousand communicant members or fraction thereof, but not to exceed three Ruling Elders and three Teaching Elders from each Presbytery. (Assembly Minutes 1-53)

3. The approval of the accompanying resolutions as suggested forms to be used by Presbyteries and Congregations for documenting their affiliation with the National Presbyterian Church. The Stated Clerk was authorized to send these to each Presbytery, with a letter requesting presbytery action prior to the Second General Assembly. (Board Minutes 1-30)

According to the Minutes of the Board of Directors (1-22) "the Minutes of the Executive Committee shall be submitted to the Board of Directors for ratification."

Morton H. Smith, Clerk

The matter of the Coordinator's monthly reports was discussed, and it was agreed that the Business Manager should prepare a simplified uniform report form for all to use.

Bob Cannada and Jack Williamson presented a diagram of the organizational structure of the Church. The question of the proper function of the Board of Directors was discussed.

<a id="ga02-p106"></a>

1-47 By Law Committee Appointed

Upon motion made and seconded, and adopted by a majority vote, the Moderator was asked to appoint a Committee to draw up the necessary changes in the By Laws to provide for the Board to act in an advisory capacity regarding Permanent Committee business, and to serve as a decision making body regarding legal and business matters.

1-48 Rules for Assembly Operation

The Committee on Rules for Assembly Operation, namely, W. Jack Williamson, Robert C. Cannada, Larry C. Mills, Donald B. Patterson and Morton H. Smith presented Proposed Rules for Assembly Operations, which were approved as amended. (See attached copy.) These rules are to be presented to the Assembly for Assembly action.

1-49 Assembly Docket

The Stated Clerk presented the docket as recommended by the Assembly Arrangements Committee. Upon motion made, seconded and passed, the hour for proposed adjournment of the Assembly was set at 4 P.M., Friday. The inspirational programs at the Assembly are to be limited to one hour, and the Assembly is to continue business for at least one hour each evening, except Wednesday, when the afternoon session will be extended by one hour, and the evening devoted to a message by Dr. Francis Schaeffer, and a reception for the Moderator. Informational programs of the Permanent Committees may be given as part of the Committee reports.

The Clerk was directed to prepare a new docket in accord with these amendments. (See attached copy.)

1-50 The meeting was recessed for lunch at 12:30 and reconvened at 1:30 P.M.

1-51 Corporate Seal Approved

It was moved, seconded and unanimously adopted that the seal prepared by Mr. Cannada, and hereby impressed on these Minutes, be hereby approved as the official seal of the Incorporation to be impressed upon the By Laws, and used on any official documents calling for such a seal hereafter.

1-52 By Law Amendment

It was moved and seconded and unanimously approved that the By Laws, Article IV, Section 1 be amended to read as follows:

The officers of the corporation shall be the Moderator, the Clerk, the Treasurer, and such Assistant Secretaries as may be designated by the Board of Directors. The officers, with the exception of the Treasurer, shall be elected by the members of the corporation as set forth in these By-laws. The Treasurer, who shall also serve as Business Administrator, shall be selected by the Board of Directors to serve for such term and under such terms and conditions as may be designated by the Board of Directors. The Treasurer need not be a Ruling Elder or Minister in the National Presbyterian Church.

MINUTES OF THE
BOARD OF DIRECTORS OF THE
national presbyterian church
September 16, 1974
Macon, Georgia
1-61 The Board of Directors of the National Presbyterian Church met
i nits annual meeting prior to the second General Assembly at the macon
Hilton on September 16, 1974.
1-62 The meeting was convened at 7 :30 P.M. by the Moderator, Mr. W.
Jack Williamson. The meeting was opened with a season of prayer.
1-63 Present were the follow ing:
Board members: W. Jack Williamson, Moderator; Morton H. Smith,
Clerk; Robert Cannada; E. C. Cooley; Charles Dunahoo; Joseph Everett,
J r.; William Joseph; Harry N. Miller; Robert J. Ostenson; Donald B.
Patterson; Gordon Reed; John Spencer; M. B. Swayze; Cecil Williamson
Also present w ere: Ken K eyes; larry mills; Dan Moore; Paul
Settle; Aiken Taylor and Ken Ryskamp
1-64 discussion of designated gifts
the board discussed the matter of designated gifts. Mr. Keyes
was invited to speak to this m atter. A fter the discussion Mr. Keyes
was excused.
1-65 Policy on Conditional Gifts Rescinded
On motion, made, seconded and adopted the policy on conditional
gifts (Board Minutes, paragraphs 1-23, (see p. 100) was rescinded.
1-66 committee appointed to study the matter of gifts
On motion, made, seconded and adopted, the Moderator was asked
to appoint a committee to study the question of gifts to the Assembly,
and to report back to the Board during this Assembly. The Moderator
appointed the following committee: John Spencer, Chairman; E. C.
Cooley; M. B. Swayze.
1-67 discussion of the name
Ken Ryskamp reported on the problem regarding the name of the
denomination. after a full discussion of them atter, Major General
Reginald C. Harmon of the National Presbyterian Church of Washington, D.C., was invited into the meeting to present the position of that

<a id="ga02-p109"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=109 printed_page=null -->

congregation regarding this matter. After a full presentation, General Harmon was excused.

1-68 Decision to Change the Name

It was moved, seconded and unanimously adopted that the Moderator be asked to appoint a committee to propose the change of the name of the Church to the Assembly in the opening session of the Assembly, and that the vote on the question of whether to change the name or not be docketed for the opening session. Gordon Reed and Morton Smith were named to this committee.

1-69 New Name Proposed

It was moved, seconded and approved that the Board recommends to the General Assembly the name “American Presbyterian Church.”

1-70 Time for Name Selection

It was moved, seconded and adopted that the selection of the name be docketed for 7:00 P.M. Tuesday evening.

1-71 Mr. Ryskamp to Present the Matter of the Name to the Assembly

It was moved, seconded and unanimously approved that Mr. Ryskamp be asked to present the matter regarding the name of the Church to the Assembly as a part of the Moderator’s report.

1-72 Revised By Laws Approved

It was moved, seconded and adopted that the attached By Laws be adopted as amended. (See Appendix D, pp. 126-129).

1-73 Resolution on the Name Change

Whereas, the First General Assembly of the National President Church did in good faith adopt the name “National Presbyterian Church,” and

Whereas, since the First General Assembly, it has come to the attention of the Board of Directors of the National Presbyterian Church that there is a congregation of the United Presbyterian Church in the United States of America in the nation’s capitol called by the name “National Presbyterian Church,” which congregation derives a portion of its support from across the nation and claims a nationwide ministry, and thus fears that our use of the same name will cause confusion in their support base, and

Whereas, representatives of the Washington congregation feel so strongly about this matter that they indicate they would resort to the civil courts, if necessary, to settle this issue, and

Whereas, our Lord eaches that “If any man will sue thee at the law, and take away thy coat, let him have thy cloak also. And whosoever shall compel thee to go a mile, go with him twain. Give to him that asketh thee, and from him that would borrow of thee turn not away” (Mt. 5:40-42),

Therefore, be it Resolved, that the Board of Directors of the National Presbyterian Church recommends to the Second General Assembly of the National Presbyterian Church that it change the name of the Church, out of obedience to her Lord, and in love for our brethren in Christ of the National Presbyterian Church and Center of Washington, D. C.

1-74 Adjournment

Upon motion, the meeting was adjourned, being closed with prayer.

W. Jack Williamson, Moderator
Morton H. Smith, Clerk

supplement to the minutes of the board of directors
Report of Committee appointed to study question of gifts to the
Assembly.
The Committee to study the question of gifts to the Assembly rec
om mends to the board that it adopt the following as the policy of the
denomination regarding gifts to the church:
it is resolved that the board of directors establish as a matter of
policy that before any conditional gifts are received in behalf of the
National Presbyterian Church, the conditions shall be put into w riting
and submitted to the Board of Directors for approval. it is further
resolved that as a matter of policy the board of directors doe snot
favor receiving gifts that have any conditions attached thereto, unless
after ten (10) years the General Assembly may upon recommendation
of the Board of Directors remove such conditions by a 2 /3 vote of reg
istered commissioners.
John Spencer
Chairman

<a id="ga02-p112"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=112 printed_page=null -->

the right to withdraw from said Assembly at any time under conditions and in accordance with such rules as may be prescribed by the Presbytery. The Presbytery reserves to itself the right of the ownership of all property of every sort, nature or description now owned or hereafter acquired. This is not to be construed as a claim by the Presbytery upon the properties of its constituent congregations, since the properties of congregations under the National Presbyterian Church may not be claimed by the higher courts, except as voluntarily given by the congregation to the said higher court.

Done on the 18th day of July, 1974, in Stated Meeting of the Presbytery being met at Hopewell Church, Rock Hill, S. C.

Be it further Resolved that pursuant to the above Resolution, the Presbytery of the Gulf Coast does hereby request formal recognition of it by the Second General Assembly of the National Presbyterian Church as a member of the Presbytery of the National Presbyterian Church (A Corporation), with all the rights and obligations belonging to member presbyteries as set forth in the Book of Church Order of the National Presbyterian Church. The Presbytery of the Gulf Coast reserves to itself the right to withdraw from said Assembly at any time under conditions and in accordance with such rules as may be prescribed by the Presbytery. The Presbytery reserves to itself the right of the ownership of all property of every sort, nature or description now owned or hereafter acquired. This is not to be construed as a claim by the Presbytery upon the properties of its constituent congregations, since the properties of congregations under the National Presbyterian Church may not be claimed by the higher courts, except as voluntarily given by the congregation to the said higher court.

Done on this Fourth day of June, 1974, in the Stated Meeting of the Presbytery being met at the Warrington Presbyterian Church of Warrington, Florida.

Subscribed and attested by:

M. Timothy Elder, Moderator
James W. Thrashey, Stated Clerk

Be it Resolved that the **Presbytery of Westminster** which is composed of the following Churches and Ministers, who all concur with and subscribe to the Constitution of the National Presbyterian Church (A Corporation), namely, the Westminster Confession of Faith, the Larger and Shorter Catechism, and the Book of Church Order as the basis for church unity, does here declare its commitment to the National Presbyterian Church as that branch of the Church of Christ to which it adheres

of Westminster does hereby request formal recognition of it by the Second General Assembly of the National Presbyterian Church as a member Presbytery of
the National Presbyterian Church (A Corporation), with all the rights and obligations belonging to member presbyteries as set forth in the Book of Church Order of the National Presbyterian Church . The Presbytery of Westminster reserves to itself the right to withdraw from said Assembly at any time under
conditions and in accordance with such rules as may be prescribed by the Presbytery. The Presbytery reserves to itself the right of ownership of all property of every sort, nature or description now owned or hereafter acquired. This
is not to be construed as a claim by the Presbytery upon the properties of its
constituent congregations, since the properties of congregations under the National Presbyterian Church may not be claimed by the higher courts, except
as voluntarily given by the congregation to the said higher court.

# Appendix D

## REPORT OF THE SPECIAL COMMITTEE ON CORPORATION BY LAWS

By action of the Board of Directors taken on June 18, 1974, (1-47, 1-56) the following Committee was appointed to prepare a revision of the By Laws: W. Jack Williamson, Chairman, Robert C. Cannada, Larry C. Mills, Donald B. Patterson, and Morton H. Smith. The Committee met at the Jackson, Mississippi, Airport on August 19, 1974, with Gordon Reed also in attendance. The following By Laws were drawn up and approved for submission to the Board of Directors at its annual meeting on September 16, 1974, at Macon, Georgia, at 7:30 P.M.

## BY-LAWS OF NATIONAL PRESBYTERIAN CHURCH (A CORPORATION)

### ARTICLE I NAME AND LOCATION.

**Section 1.** The name of this corporation shall be National Presbyterian Church (A Corporation).

**Section 2.** The registered office in the State of Delaware is to be located at 229 South State Street, in the City of Dover, County of Kent. The registered agent in charge thereof is The Prentice-Hall Corporation System, Inc., at 229 South State Street, Dover, Delaware. The official business address of the Corporation is the office of the Business Administrator.

Other offices for transaction of business shall be located at such places as the General Assembly or its Permanent Committees shall designate.

### ARTICLE II. MEMBERS AND MEETINGS OF THE CORPORATION

**Section 1.** The members of the corporation shall be those duly ordained Teaching Elders (Ministers) enrolled in a Presbytery affiliated with the National Presbyterian Church and those Ruling Elders representing local congregations, which congregations are affiliated with Presbyteries affiliated with the National Presbyterian Church, who have been designated or commissioned to attend the annual General Assembly of the National Presbyterian Church. Such Teaching Elders and Ruling Elders shall be designated or commissioned by Presbyteries or Congregations in accordance with rules and regulations prescribed by the Book of Church Order (15-2) (See Article VI.). Such individuals shall be the members of the corporation until the next annual meeting of the General Assembly of the National Presbyterian Church, at which time the members of the corporation shall be those individuals designated or commissioned as hereinabove set forth to attend such annual General Assembly.

**Section 2.** The annual meeting of the corporation shall be at such time and such place as designated by the General Assembly, and ordinarily will be held during the month of September. Each General Assembly shall have the power to designate the time and place for more than one annual General Assembly, and shall also have the power to authorize the Committee on Administration to designate the time and place of the next General Assembly.

**Section 3.** Special meetings of the General Assembly may be called in accordance with the Book of Church Order (15-3).

**Section 4.** A quorum for the transaction of business at any meeting of the General Assembly shall be that prescribed in the Book of Church Order (15-5).

**Section 5.** The Moderator shall call all meetings to order and shall preside until his successor has been selected and takes office. If the Moderator is unable to act, the Stated Clerk shall call the Assembly to order and preside over its sessions until a Moderator has been elected.

**Section 6.** Proxies shall not be allowed at General Assembly meetings.

### ARTICLE III. OFFICERS.

**Section 1.** The officers of the corporation shall be the Moderator, the Clerk,

<a id="ga02-p129"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=129 printed_page=null -->

the Business Administrator-treasurer, and such assistant clerks and treasurers as may be deemed desirable by the Committee on Administration. The officers, with exception of the assistant clerks or assistant treasurers, shall be elected by the General Assembly as set forth in the Book of Church Order and the Rules for Assembly Operation. In the event that the Stated Clerk or the Business Administrator are unable to act, the Committee on Administration shall be authorized to appoint a provisional Clerk or a provisional Business Administrator to serve until a regular Clerk or Business Administrator may be elected by the next General Assembly.

**Section 2.** The Moderator shall have such duties and responsibilities as set forth in the Book of Church Order and the Rules of Assembly Operation. The Moderator, unless specifically authorized by the General Assembly, shall have no authority to and shall not be expected to perform any functions for the corporation other than those specifically set forth in these By-Laws or those set forth in the Book of Church Order, and the Rules for Assembly Operation.

**Section 3.** The Clerk shall have such duties and responsibilities as set forth in the Book of Church Order and Rules of Assembly Operation. He shall be immediately responsible to the Committee on Administration. The Clerk shall prepare and forward all notices required by law or by these By-Laws, and shall have general charge of the corporate books and records. He shall sign such instruments as may be required, and perform the duties incident to the office of Clerk, and such duties as may be assigned by the Moderator, the Committee on Administration, the members of the corporation in General Assembly.

**Section 4.** The Business Administrator-treasurer shall by the custodian of the funds and securities belonging to the corporation, and not otherwise designated to one of the three program committees. He shall receive deposit and disburse such funds as directed by the General Assembly, including any provisions set forth in the Book of Church Order. He shall keep an accurate account of the finances of the corporation, not only of these funds in the custody, but by means of monthly reports from the other committees of their funds also, on a uniform form, which he shall provide. He shall prepare or have prepared such reports of the financial condition of the corporation as be required, and, in general, perform all of the duties incident to the office of Business Administrator-treasurer. He shall be bonded in an amount to be determined by the Committee on Administration.

**ARTICLE IV. PERMANENT COMMITTEES.**

**Section 1.** The affairs of the corporation shall be conducted primarily through Permanent Committees, to wit: Committee on Administration; Committee for Christian Education and Publications; Committee on Mission to the United States; Committee on Mission to the World. The Committee of Administration, shall be composed of six Teaching Elders and six Ruling Elders elected as prescribed by the General Assembly, plus the Moderator of the General Assembly, the immediate past Moderator,* the Stater Clerk and the Chairman of the other three Permanent Committees. The other Committees shall consist of six Teaching Elders and six Ruling Elders, elected as prescribed by the General Assembly.

**Section 2.** The power and authority of the Permanent Committees shall be those set forth in these By-Laws or by direction of the General Assembly.

**Section 3.** The Permanent Committees shall, unless specifically directed otherwise by the General Assembly, be authorized to operate from separate locations with separate offices and separate staffs. The budget for each Permanent Committee, including specifically the compensation to be paid the chief administrative officer of each Permanent Committee, shall be submitted to the Committee on Administration, which shall consider the requests of each committee as it relates to the budget requests of other committees, to needs and to opportunities, and shall recommend an over all budget to the General Assembly, for its approval. All funds received by the corporation that are designated for the benefit of any particular Permanent Committee shall be disbursed by the Business Administrator to the proper committee. There shall be no equalization of funds so designated. Any funds received by the corporation not desig-

<a id="ga02-p130"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=130 printed_page=null -->

nated as being for the benefit of a particular Permanent Committee shall be distributed by the Business Administrator as directed by the General Assembly.

**Section 4.** Each Permanent Committee, by resolution adopted by a majority of its committee members, may designate the place, date and time for regular meetings of the committee, which should be held at least quarterly. Written or printed notice of such resolution should be given to all committee members within a reasonable time after the adoption thereof. Notice of the time, place or purpose of such regular meetings of the Permanent Committee shall not be required to be given.

**Section 5.** Special meetings of the Permanent Committees may be called at any time or place by the Chairman of the Committee, or by a majority of the committee members. Written notice stating the place, date and hour of such special meeting shall be delivered by the Chairman of the Committee to each committee member at least ten days prior to the date of such meeting, and such notice should specify the purpose of such special meeting. Attendance of a committee member at such a meeting will constitute a waiver of notice of such meeting. The act of the majority of the committee members present at a meeting at which a quorum is present shall be the act of the Committee.

**Section 6.** A majority of a Permanent Committee shall constitute a quorum.

**Section 7.** The Chairman and the Secretary of each Permanent Committee shall be elected annually at the first meeting of the Committee following the General Assembly. The incumbent Chairman and Secretary shall continue to serve until their successors have been elected and assume their duties. In the event that the Chairman is rotated off of a Committee, the Moderator of the General Assembly shall name a Convener of the Committee, who shall preside over the Committee until a Chairman is elected and assume his duties.

**Section 8.** In the event any administrative personnel employed by a Committee and approved by the General Assembly is unable to act, such Committee may employ a provisional replacement, who has been examined and approved by the Assembly's Theological Examining Committee, and who shall serve until the next General Assembly.

**Section 9.** The Individual Permanent Committees

**A. The Committee on Administration**

1. The business affairs of the corporation as distinguished from the ecclesiastical matters, and those not specifically assigned to one of the other Permanent Committees by these By-Laws or an act of the General Assembly, shall be managed by the Committee on Administration, which serves as the Board of Directors provided in the Charter of Incorporation, subject to such rules and regulations as may be prescribed by the General Assembly, including all applicable provisions of the Book of Church Order.

2. The Committee on Administration shall hold an annual meeting in conjunction with the annual General Assembly meeting, at a time and place to be determined by the Committee. Notice shall not be required to be given of the time or place of the annual meeting of the Committee, other than that which shall be included in the Commissioner's Handbook for the General Assembly.

**B. The Committee for Christian Education and Publications**

The affairs of the Church in the areas of Christian education and publications are assigned to the Committee for Christian Education and Publications, whose duties and authority shall be designated by the General Assembly.

**C. The Committee on Mission to the United States**

The affairs of the Church involved in its extension in the United States and Canada are assigned to the Committee on Mission to the United States, whose duties and authority shall be designated by the General Assembly.

**D. The Committee on Mission to the World**

The affairs of the Church in the area of world missions outside of the United States and Canada are assigned to the Committee on Mission to the World, whose duties and authority shall be designated by the General Assembly.

<a id="ga02-p131"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=131 printed_page=null -->

## ARTICLE V. FISCAL MATTERS.

**Section 1.** The fiscal year of the corporation shall be from January 1 through December 31 of each year. The General Assembly shall annually designate the auditors for the corporation on recommendation from the Committee on Administration, which auditing firm shall make an audit of the financial affairs of the corporation and of each Permanent Committee promptly following the close of each fiscal year. The expenses of such audit shall be prorated among the corporation and each Permanent Committee.

**Section 2.** All funds of the corporation shall be deposited from time to time to the credit of the corporation in such banks, savings and loan institutions, trust or other depositories as the Permanent Committees by resolution may select.

**Section 3.** All checks, drafts or other orders for the payment of money, notes or other evidences of indebtedness issued in the name of the corporation shall be signed by such officer or officers of the corporation as the Committee on Administration shall designate. All checks, drafts or other orders for the payment of money, notes or other evidences of indebtedness issued in the name of any of the Permanent Committees shall be signed by such representative of the Committee as the Committee by resolution shall designate.

## ARTICLE VI. ECCLESIASTICAL MATTERS.

**Section 1.** The ecclesiastical Constitution of the Church is composed of: the Westminster Confession of Faith, the Larger and Shorter Catechisms as adopted by the General Assembly of the National Presbyterian Church, and the Book of Church Order of the National Presbyterian Church. The provisions of the Constitution shall control over any provisions of these By-Laws that may be in conflict therewith.

## ARTICLE VII. AMENDMENTS TO THE BY-LAWS

These By-Laws may be amended by a majority vote at any annual or special meeting of the General Assembly.

*The General Assembly amended these By Laws by adding “the immediate past Moderator,” to the membership of the Committee on Administration, in Article IV, Section 1. (See 2-94, p. 70)*

<a id="ga02-p132"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=132 printed_page=null -->

## Appendix E

## REPORT OF THE COMMITTEE ON ADMINISTRATION

Our first year has been a time of discovery. What are the duties and responsibilities of this and other committees? Every case has been carefully considered because the first decisions set the precedents for future years.

We feel the need for the Assembly to clarify the role of the Committees in the area of stewardship in general. While we recognize that the Assembly has assigned to each committee the responsibility for raising its own budget yet there is more to stewardship than raising funds for a budget. Our people need to learn the joy of giving and the responsibility of stewardship as taught in the Word of God. A program could be developed to help the local church in its stewardship responsibilities. We believe that some committee could serve the Assembly in this role.

In 1974, by mutual consent, the four committees joined together in an effort to promote their budgets. This was coordinated by the Committee on Administration and was known as “the Kings Million” program. Many individual members of the denomination gave their time to this effort and deserve our thanks.

We would like to express our appreciation for the splendid cooperation the other committees have given us in presenting their budgets to the General Assembly. We have lived with the tension of the tremendous opportunities which are before the National Presbyterian Church at this time, but also a realistic appraisal of the income available for the work of the Assembly. We have all been aware of the difficulty of this task because of the limited time for accumulating information on income and expenditures. We hope that as experience is gained over a longer period of time this task will become less complicated.

In response to actions taken at the first General Assembly the Committee has procured bonds for employees of this Committee. We, together with the other committees, are in the process of arranging for an end of the year audit of all of the Assembly’s financial records by a Certified Public Accountant.

The First General Assembly placed in the hands of the Committee on Administration the responsibility for further study and action on a proposed gift of property in western North Carolina for a proposed conference center for the National Presbyterian Church. After a detailed study of the whole matter, the committee voted unanimously not to accept the generous offer. This decision was based upon matters relating to the suitability of the property for that purpose, and the conditions placed on the offer by the donor. In recent months a generous gift amounting to approximately $100,000 has been made to the National Presbyterian Church. We thank God for this gift and for the generous spirit of the donor who over the years has enthusiastically supported the things for which we stand. Recommendations concerning the use of this gift will appear below.

The Committee on Administration is grateful to God for the effective work and sincere dedication of our Stated Clerk and our Business Consultant and their staffs.

The Committee on Administration accepts the responsibility for our many mistakes and requests the continued prayers and forbearance of the Assembly as we learn and grow. For all of the advances and blessings we claim no credit but ascribe all glory to God the Father, God the Son, and God the Holy Spirit. Amen.

Rev. Gordon Reed, Chairman

See the following for the detailed budgets as submitted by each of the Permanent Committees.

Recommendations as adopted by the Assembly are found in 2-106

<a id="ga02-p133"></a>
