# Appendix F

## REPORT OF THE TRUSTEES OF THE ANNUITY FUND

The trustees have prepared an annuity program for the ministers of the denomination. It is as follows:

### The Official Plan of the Annuity Fund for Ministers of the National Presbyterian Church

#### SECTION 1. ELIGIBILITY PROVISIONS

##### Section 1.1 Eligibility for Membership

All ordained ministers of the National Presbyterian Church are eligible for membership in the Annuity Fund for Ministers. A member is a minister of the Church whose signed application has been received by the Trustees on a form to be supplied by the Trustees and on whose behalf dues payments to the fund have been made. Membership in the Fund may be effective with the date of ordination or later. A minister ordained in some other denomination becomes eligible for membership effective with the date of reception by a presbytery of the Church. Full time administrative personnel of the National Presbyterian Church may be members of this Annuity Fund with the approval of the Trustees.

##### Section 1.2 Eligibility for Current Protection

A currently protected member is a member of the Fund (a) who is currently an ordained minister of the Church or otherwise eligible, (b) who has made written application to the Fund and has had at least three months full dues payments made to the Fund on his behalf, (c) who has not previously entered upon an age retirement annuity and (d) whose current member and employer dues payments are not more than ninety days in arrears.

##### Section 1.3 Delayed Application for Membership

In the event an ordained minister of the Church delays application for participation in the Fund two years or more after becoming eligible, and if partially disabled or not insurable at standard rates for life insurance at the time of making a delayed application for membership in the Fund, the Trustees may limit the liability under the disability, survivor and death benefits provisions in such manner or amount as the Trustees deem commensurate with the risks involved.

##### Section 1.4 Transfers from Other Denominations

Any minister who transfers from some other denomination to the Church shall be subject at the time of making application for membership in the Fund, to the provision stated in Section 1.3 concerning partial disability and insurability.

#### SECTION 2. DUES STRUCTURE

##### Section 2.1 Dues Payments to the Fund

Dues payments to the Fund shall be made at the rate of 12% of the compensation basis of the member as defined in Section 2.5. The portion of such rate of payment which shall be considered as employer dues and member dues, respectively, shall be as follows:

(a) Employer dues, which may be paid by the employer or the member, shall equal 9% of the compensation basis of the member and shall be administered on a group basis to be applied toward providing age retirement, disability, survivor and death benefits. These dues are not refundable in the event of the cancellation of an account as outlined in Section 2.4. A portion of employer dues payments, if required, may be used to provide administrative expenses not otherwise provided.

(b) Member dues, which may be paid by the member or by the employer, shall equal 3% of the compensation basis of the member. In either case, member dues are to be credited to the member's individual account. The 3% member dues shall be applied toward providing an age retirement or disability annuity or, in the event of prior death, toward providing survivor benefits. However, if a member or the eligible survivors of the member receive less in annuity

<a id="ga02-p138"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=138 printed_page=null -->

and insurance benefits than the total member and employer dues payments actually made on behalf of the member, the balance, if any, shall be paid as outlined in the payment of death benefits under Section 6.3.

(c) Ordained ministers of the Church, who with the consent of the presbytery are not serving in a salaried relationship to any church or agency of the Church, are eligible to participate in the Fund. Such participation may be on a minimum compensation basis of $1,200 or on any larger amount not exceeding the actual salary. Dues payments for such minister may be received either from the member or from the employer. In either case, such dues shall be credited and administered as provided elsewhere in Section 2.1.

## Section 2.2. How Dues are Payable

Payment of the 12% dues shall be made to the Fund in monthly, quarterly, semi-annual or annual installments in advance. Each remittance should be made payable to the Annuity Fund for Ministers and shall include the full 12% dues for the period involved.

## Section 2.3 Return of Partial Payment of Dues

If the Fund does not have in its possession by the end of the second month of any fiscal year all the payments due the Fund on the member's account for the previous fiscal year, the Trustees retain the privilege of returning without interest all payments made for such year to the sources paying them and canceling participation for the entire year.

## Section 2.4 Refund of Member Dues upon Termination of Service

There can be no cancellation of membership and refund of member dues so long as the member is an ordained minister of the Church. A member ceasing to be an ordained minister of the Church who does not qualify for or elect the privileges of Section 8.2 or Section 8.3 shall receive a refund of the total of the member dues payments actually made on behalf of the member under Section 2.1 and the special dues credits provided under Section 9.1, together with interest as determined by the Trustees, but less the sum of any annuity payments received by the member. This refund shall cancel membership in the Fund and represent a complete discharge of all obligations of the Trustees to the member resulting from participation in the Fund.

## Section 2.5 Basis on Which Dues are Payable

The compensation basis shall be one of the following:

(a) The member's cash salary plus 20% of that cash salary for the free use of a manse, if manse is provided. If the member has more than one source of salary and has free use of manse owned by any one or more organizations paying the salary, the 20% should be added to the cash salary by each source.

(b) The member's cash salary plus the total rental allowance if the member does not have free use of the manse, but in lieu thereof is paid a rent allowance.

In determining the compensation basis on which dues are to be paid, there may be added to (a) or (b) above any other payments made to or for the member, such as manse utilities allowance, automobile allowance, etc.

## Section 2.6 Non-Payment of Dues During Membership

In the event dues payments to the Fund have not been made on behalf of a member (including a member who is receiving an age retirement or disability annuity) for any part of such member's period of membership, as defined later in this Section 2.6, the following benefits shall be adjusted:

(a) the $300 minimum surviving spouse annuity under Section 5.1.

(b) the children annuities under Section 5.2,

(c) the death benefits under Section 6.1 and Section 6.4 and

(d) the disability benefits (including the accrual of basic retirement credits) under Section 7.

The adjustment shall be in accordance with the ratio of the member and employer dues payments actually made on behalf of the member during such member's period of membership to the total member and employer dues payments which would have been made on behalf of the member had such dues been paid during the member's entire period of membership. The compensation basis upon which dues were paid in the twelve months immediately preceding any period of non-payment of dues shall be the assumed compensation basis for any such period.

<a id="ga02-p139"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=139 printed_page=null -->

The period of membership of a member shall be the entire period beginning on the date membership in the Fund is established and ending with the date of such member's death, disability retirement, or age retirement, whichever is applicable, and shall include any period during which no dues payments are made on behalf of the member, regardless of the reason.

## SECTION 3. HOW CREDITS ARE ACCUMULATED

### Section 3.1 Basic Retirement Credits

(a) The Basic Retirement Credits accumulated by each member are to be at the rate of 1½% of the compensation basis on which full dues payments have been made for that year under Section 2. The total basic retirement credits of a member at any time will be 1½% of the total compensation basis on which full dues have been paid from the date of entry into the Fund.

(b) Additional retirement credits shall be granted those eligible members who become members prior to the 1975 General Assembly, and who, upon entry into the Fund, had forfeited credits earned as participants in the annuity fund of another plan. The Additional retirement credits shall be granted on the compensation basis on which they were accumulated and forfeited. The maximum additional credits that may be accumulated are those earned and forfeited during the last five years of the member's participation in an annuity fund before entry into this Plan. These Additional retirement credits shall be restored at the rate of 10% per year beginning with the member's date of entry into the Plan.

### Section 3.2 Special Retirement Credits

Special retirement credits shall be those credits declared under the provisions of Section 9.1 as they apply to retirement credits.

### Section 3.3 Combined Retirement Credits

Combined retirement credits shall be the total of all basic retirement credits in addition to the total of all special retirement credits which have been added to a member's account.

## SECTION 4. AGE RETIREMENT BENEFITS

### Section 4.1 Age Retirement Annuity

(a) A member of the Fund shall be entitled to receive an age retirement annuity provided such member has attained age 65 and filed a signed retirement application form with the Trustees.

(b) The annual amount of the age retirement annuity shall be equal to the combined retirement credits in the member's account at the date the annuity begins. The age retirement annuity is payable to the member for life with 50% thereof continued at the death of the member to the surviving spouse under the provisions of 5.1. Special credits declared by the Trustees after the commencement of the annuity shall be credited to this annuity as set forth in Section 9.

(c) A member whose annuity commences after the attainment of age 65 shall receive an annuity based upon the total of his combined retirement credits at the time the annuity payments begin.

Such member shall continue to earn basic retirement credits following his 65th birthday for each full year or fraction thereof that full dues payments have been made to the Fund. The member is also eligible for any special retirement credits that may be declared by the Trustees between the date of the 65th birthday and the beginning of his age retirement annuity.

A member who elects at age 65 or thereafter to receive his age retirement annuity but continues his employment in some capacity with the Church may do so, but upon this election he shall accrue no further basic retirement credits in the Fund nor shall he pay dues to the Fund after the commencement of the age retirement annuity.

### Section 4.2 Early Age Retirement Options

A member of the Fund may elect and receive an early age retirement annuity at any time after attaining age 55 provided such member has requested and received retirement by act of the presbytery and filed a signed retirement

<a id="ga02-p140"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=140 printed_page=null -->

application form with the Trustees. The annual amount of the early age retirement annuity shall be equal to:

The combined retirement credits (see Section 3.3) in the member's account at the date the annuity begins but reduced to a percentage based on the age at early retirement as set forth in the following schedule:

|  Age of Retirement | % of Credits  |
| --- | --- |
|  65 | 100%  |
|  64 | 100  |
|  63 | 100  |
|  62 | 94  |
|  61 | 88  |
|  60 | 82  |
|  59 | 76  |
|  58 | 73  |
|  57 | 70  |
|  56 | 67  |
|  55 | 64  |

## Section 4.3 Joint and Survivor Age Retirement Options

(a) Before retirement on an age retirement or disability annuity, a member may elect one of the following options for an actuarially adjusted age retirement annuity payable to the member upon retirement after attaining age 65 and providing a larger surviving spouse annuity than under Section 5.1 to a spouse whose marriage to the member took place before the member made such election.

OPTION A — An actuarially adjusted annuity payable to the member for life. Upon the death of the member following retirement, an annuity equal to 75% of the adjusted age retirement annuity shall be paid to the surviving spouse. The 75% surviving spouse annuity shall terminate upon the death or remarriage of the spouse.

OPTION B — An actuarially adjusted annuity payable to the member as long as both the member and the spouse of the member survive. Upon the death of either the member or the spouse following the member's retirement, an annuity equal to 75% of the adjusted age retirement annuity shall be paid to the survivor. If the survivor is the member, the 75% member annuity shall terminate at the death of the member. If the survivor is the spouse, the 75% surviving spouse annuity shall terminate upon the death or remarriage of the spouse.

(b) The amount of the adjusted annuity payable under Option A or Option B shall be the actuarial equivalent, as determined by the Trustees, of the member's combined retirement credits (see Section 3.3). The election of either option will not alter the annuity to any minor child of the member.

The payment of a 75% surviving spouse annuity under either option shall be in lieu of any annuity otherwise payable to a surviving spouse after the member's retirement under the provisions of Section 5.1.

Either option may be elected by a member at the time up to one year before the effective date of the age retirement, annuity without submission of evidence of good health. A member desiring to elect either option less than one year before the effective date must submit evidence of good health satisfactory to the Trustees. The election of either option may be cancelled by a member at any time up to one year before the effective date of the age retirement annuity. Cancellation less than one year before the effective date will require the approval of the Trustees.

The election of either option shall have no effect if (i) a member or member's spouse dies before the member's retirement, or (ii) a member subsequently begins to receive either an early age retirement or a disability annuity before attaining age 65.

## SECTION 5. SURVIVOR BENEFITS

### Section 5.1 Surviving Spouse Annuity

A surviving spouse is one whose marriage to a deceased member of the

<a id="ga02-p141"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=141 printed_page=null -->

Fund has taken place before the member begins to receive an age retirement annuity (see Section 4). A surviving spouse of a member who at the time of death is receiving a disability annuity (see Section 7) is one whose marriage to the member took place before the member began to receive such disability annuity. Upon the death of a member before or after the member begins to receive an age retirement or disability annuity, the surviving spouse shall receive an annual surviving spouse annuity equal to one-half of the member's combined retirement credits (see Section 3.3) at date of death. A minimum of $300 per year will be payable if all dues payment to the Fund on behalf of a member have been made for every month of the member's period of membership (see Section 2.6). Any special credit declared by the Trustees after the surviving spouse annuity begins shall be added to this annuity as specified in Section 9.1.

The surviving spouse annuity shall terminate upon death or remarriage of the spouse.

## Section 5.2 Children Annuities

When a member dies before or after the member begins to receive an age retirement or disability annuity and if all dues payments to the Fund on behalf of the member have been made for every month of the member's period of membership (see Section 2.6), each of the children of the member shall receive an annual child annuity of $300, subject to maximum annuities payable to all the children of a member of $900 per year. Each child annuity shall be payable to the surviving parent or guardian on behalf of said child until the child reaches age eighteen. However, this annuity shall be continued thereafter up to age twenty-three if such child is in full-time attendance at some institution of learning. Any special credit declared by the Trustees after a child annuity begins shall be added to this annuity as specified in Section 9.1.

## SECTION 6. DEATH BENEFITS

### Section 6.1 Lump Sum Death Benefit upon Death of Currently Protected or Disabled Member

A currently protected member under Section 1.2 or a disabled member receiving a disability annuity whose death occurs prior to receiving an age annuity, and who at the time had made full dues payments to the Fund, shall have paid to his beneficiary in a lump sum an amount determined by his last twelve months dues compensation basis and age at the time of death, as follows:

- (a) All members up to age 36 — 3 times annual compensation
- (b) All members ages 36 to 55 — 1½ times annual compensation
- (c) All members ages 55 to 60 — 1 times annual compensation
- (d) All members ages 60 to 65 — ½ times annual compensation, but not less than $5,000
- (e) All members age 65 and above — $1,000

If a member's death occurs as the result of an accident, the lump sum amount to the member's beneficiary will be double the above scale.

The benefits to which a member is entitled under this Section 6.1 are subject to the contractual terms of the group life contract held by the Trustees, and with the exception of the payments to members age 65 and above, all benefit payments shall be made only after receipt of this benefit by the Fund from the insurance carrier with which the contract is written.

### Section 6.2 Lump Sum Death Benefit upon Death after Age Retirement

Upon the death of a member who has begun to receive an age retirement annuity, there shall be paid a lump sum death benefit in the amount of $500, but not in excess of the annual annuity payable to such deceased member.

### Section 6.3 To Whom Lump Sum Death Benefit is Payable

The lump sum death benefit shall be paid to the spouse of the member, if living. If there is no spouse living, the benefit shall be paid, at the option of the Trustees, to either: (a) any one of the following surviving relatives of the member: mother, father, child or children, or (b) the executor or administrator of the estate of the member. If there is no eligible person in either (a) or (b), the benefit shall be paid to any other person appearing to the Trustees to be equitably entitled thereto by reason of having incurred expenses for the

<a id="ga02-p142"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=142 printed_page=null -->

maintenance, medical attention, or burial of the member, or otherwise. Payment in accordance with this provision shall completely discharge the Fund's liability with respect to the benefit so paid.

## Section 6.4 Education Benefits

When a member dies before or after the member begins to receive an age retirement or disability annuity and if all dues payments to the Fund on behalf of the member have been made for every month of the member's period of membership (see Section 2.6), each of the children of the member shall receive an amount of $1,000 per year for each of the first four years of study beyond high school spent thereafter in full-time attendance at an institution of higher learning, subject to a maximum total benefit of $4,000 per child. The child of a deceased member is eligible to receive this benefit only prior to the attainment of age 25.

## SECTION 7. DISABILITY BENEFITS

### Section 7.1 When Granted

A disability annuity shall be granted to a currently protected member (see Section 1.2) of the Fund upon total disability occurring before such member reaches age 65. Total disability shall mean that the member is incapacitated because of sickness or injury to such an extent that such member is incapable of performing any type of work in keeping with the member's education, training and experience.

### Section 7.2 Certification as to Disability

Total disability must be certified by the medical authorities approved by the Trustees, which shall have the right to call for proof (at the member's expense) of continued disability from time to time, but not more than once a year.

### Section 7.3 Amount and Duration of the Disability Annuity

The disability annuity shall be payable to the member beginning on the 179th day of the period during which the member is totally disabled, or on the date the member ceases to receive any remuneration for services, whichever is later. If all dues payments to the Fund on behalf of the member have been made for every month of the member's period of membership (see Section 2.6), the annual amount of the disability annuity shall equal 60% of the member's compensation basis (excluding the portion of such basis in excess of $12,000) on which dues payments to the Fund were made on behalf of the member during the last twelve months of dues payments preceding the date such disability began, less any benefit for which the member becomes eligible as the result of such disability under OASDI (Social Security), Workmen's Compensation and Veteran's and other governmental disability benefit programs. Under the provisions of the preceding sentence, the annual amount of the disability annuity shall not be less than $600. In the event a member receiving a disability annuity becomes eligible to receive an increase in disability benefits from OASDI (Social Security), Workmen's Compensation, Veteran's and other governmental disability programs three months or more after the beginning of benefits from any such source, such increases shall not reduce the sum the member is receiving as a disability benefit from the Fund.

The disability annuity shall terminate on the earliest of (a) the first day on which the member is no longer totally disabled, (b) the date on which the member attains age 65 or (c) the date of the member's death.

The benefits provided by this Section 7.3 are subject to the provisions of the long term disability insurance contract provisions held by the Trustees and no payments shall be made by the Trustees under this Section other than those distributed to the Fund by the insurer of this contract.

### Section 7.4 Waiver of Dues and Accrual of Retirement Credits While Disabled

If all dues payments to the Fund on behalf of the member have been made for every month of the member's period of membership (see Section 2.6), the members and employer dues payments under Section 2 shall be waived during the period that a disability annuity is being paid to the member and the member shall continue to accrue basic retirement credits during such period of disability annuity payment as if such dues payments were made on the member's compensation basis (excluding the portion of such basis in excess of

<a id="ga02-p143"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=143 printed_page=null -->

$12,000) on which dues payments to the Fund were made on behalf of the member during the twelve-month period preceding the date such disability began. Any special credit declared by the Trustees after the member begins to accrue such basic retirement credits during disability shall be added to such credits as specified in Section 9.1. The dues waived shall not be credited to the member's account for any refund purpose under Section 2.1 or Section 2.4 of the plan.

## Section 7.5 Attainment of Age 65

When the member attains age 65, the disability annuity shall terminate and the member shall begin to receive an age retirement annuity equal to the member's combined retirement credits (see Section 3.3) at age 65. Any special credits declared by the Trustees after the beginning of the disability annuity will be included in these combined retirement credits and the age retirement annuity will be further increased by any special credits declared after such member attains age 65.

## SECTION 8. TERMINATION OF SERVICE

### Section 8.1 Member Who Remains an Ordained Minister

A member who remains an ordained minister of the Church but on whose behalf member and employer dues payments to the Fund are not being made shall continue to be a member of the Fund. Such member shall remain eligible to receive an age retirement benefit as provided in Section 4 and the spouse shall remain eligible to receive a surviving spouse annuity as provided in Section 5.1. However, such member is not a currently protected member (see Section 1.2).

### Section 8.2 Vesting of Credits after Two or More Years of Participation

(a) A member on whose behalf member and employer dues payments to the Fund or Annuity Fund of any other plan have been made for two or more years and who ceases to be an ordained minister of the Church or an eligible member of this plan may elect, in writing, a refund of member dues as set forth in Section 2.4. If the member elects not to take such refund but leaves such dues in the Fund, the member shall be entitled to receive an age retirement annuity as detailed in Section 4.1 and Section 4.2, provided such member has

(i) submitted a signed application on a form to be supplied by the Trustees and which has been received by the Trustees, and

(ii) submitted a statement signed by the member or the employer of the member giving date of retirement.

(b) In the event of the death of such member, either before or after retirement, the surviving spouse shall be entitled to receive a surviving spouse annuity as provided in Section 5.1, but without the minimum benefit indicated in that section.

(c) Disability benefits, children benefits and death benefits shall not apply to such member. The joint and survivor options shall not be available to such member. No other benefits of any kind, provided by the Church through the Trustees, shall be available to such member or the survivors of such member.

(d) The exercising of this vesting privilege by a member shall not be irrevocable. The member may, at any time prior to being granted an age retirement annuity, elect, in writing, to receive in a lump sum a refund of member dues as set forth in Section 2.4. Such refund shall cancel membership and represent a complete discharge of all obligations of the Trustees to the member resulting from participation in the Fund.

### Section 8.3 Comity Agreements

Any member transferring ministerial relationship from the Church to some other denomination with which the Fund has at that time a comity or similar agreement may elect, in writing, a refund of member dues as set forth in Section 2.4. If the member elects not to take such refund but leaves such dues in the Fund, the member shall be entitled to retain the combined retirement credits for the purpose of an age retirement benefit as provided in Section 4 and a surviving spouse annuity as provided in Section 5.1, but without the minimum benefit indicated in that section. Such member may be eligible for other benefits in accordance with specific provisions of a particular comity agreement.

### Section 8.4 Member Ineligible for or Not Electing Vesting or Comity Agreements

A member ceasing to be an ordained minister or administrative employee

<a id="ga02-p144"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=144 printed_page=null -->

of the Church who does not qualify for or elect the privileges of Section 8.2 or Section 8.3 shall receive a refund of member dues as set forth in Section 2.4.

## SECTION 9. GENERAL PROVISIONS

### Section 9.1 Special Credits

When, in the opinion of the Trustees and on the advice of its actuarial and financial consultants, the actuarial and financial condition of the Fund warrants the declaration of special credits, these credits will be declared by the Trustees for the endorsement of the General Assembly. The amount determined to be available for such credits shall be apportioned in the most equitable manner possible, as determined by the Trustees, to all members (non-retired and retired) of the Fund and their eligible survivors. In order to accomplish an equitable distribution, all annuities under Section 4 and Section 5 being paid on the effective date of the distribution will be increased by a percentage to be determined by the Trustees in accordance with the amount available for distribution. At the same time, special retirement credits based in an equal percentage shall be applied to the combined retirement credits (see Section 3.3) in the accounts of all non-retired members and in the accounts of all members receiving disability benefits. Special dues credits based on an equal percentage shall be applied to any dues refunded under Section 2.1(b) and Section 2.4.

### Section 9.2 Payment of Annuities

All annuities shall be paid in advance in monthly installments.

### Section 9.3 Incapacitated Annuitants

If any payee hereunder is, in the judgment of the Trustees, legally, physically or mentally incapable of personally receiving and receipting for any payments due hereunder, or is deceased, the Trustees may make payment thereof to such other person, persons or institution as, in its opinion, are then maintaining or have custody of such payee, until a guardian, committee or other legal representative of such payee shall be duly appointed and claim made by such appointee or, in the case of a deceased member or payee, to any person or persons appearing to the Trustees to be equitably entitled to the same. Such payment shall constitute a full discharge of the liability of the Trustees to the extent thereof.

### 9.4 Assignment of Benefits

The interest of members and all other persons entitled to benefits or payments under this Plan shall not be subject to anticipation, assignment, attachment or to voluntary or involuntary alienation.

## SECTION 10. ALTERATIONS OR AMENDMENTS

### Section 10.1 Right to Alter or Amend

The right is reserved by the Trustees to alter or amend the Plan as may be found to be to the advantage of the Church and the members of the Fund, subject to the approval of the General Assembly before such changes can become effective.

## SECTION 11. DEFINITIONS

1. Church: The National Presbyterian Church.
2. Employer: The particular church, agency or organization being served by a member of the Fund.
3. Trustees: Trustees for the Insurance and Annuity Fund.
4. Fund: Annuity Fund for Ministers.
5. Plan: The Official Plan of the Annuity Fund for Ministers.
6. Children: For the purposes of Section 5.1 and Section 6.4, minor children shall include legally adopted children as well as natural children of a member.

Recommendations as adopted by the Assembly found in 2-54

<a id="ga02-p143"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=145 printed_page=143 -->

# Appendix G

## REPORT OF SUBCOMMITTEE ON INSURANCE

### COMMITTEE ON ADMINISTRATION—NATIONAL PRESBYTERIAN CHURCH
REPORT TO THE 2ND GENERAL ASSEMBLY OF
THE NATIONAL PRESBYTERIAN CHURCH
SEPTEMBER 17-20, 1974

Dear Brethren

Your insurance Committee has held three meetings since our last General Assembly at the time of the preparation of this report, and possibly will have another meeting prior to the General Assembly, and a supplemental report. We can report the following accomplishments and would submit several recommendations.

The Insurance Committee met December 18, 1973 to consider and evaluate bids on our group life insurance and long-term disability insurance which was authorized by the first General Assembly. It was decided to accept the bid offered by the Mutual Benefit Life Insurance Company of New Jersey. We were offered the protection that we desired under very favorable rates and the group life insurance and long-term disability has been in force since January 1, 1974 on all ministers participating in the Annuity Plan and also on some other ministers and their families. It is the intention of the Insurance Committee in cooperation with the Trustees for the Insurance and Annuity Fund to follow the original intention in securing this group life insurance, that is to make it a part of the Annuity plan and thus the protection afforded will be provided only to those ministers who are in the Minister's Annuity Plan. A specific recommendation regarding this is included below.

The second meeting of the Insurance Committee was with the original meeting of the Trustees for the Insurance and the Annuity Fund. The responsibility for developing the Annuity Fund has been very ably handled by the Trustees of that fund, and the results of their work will be contained in their report.

The Insurance Committee met again May 30 to evaluate our health insurance coverage and to consider other insurance matters which we would recommend to the constituency of the National Presbyterian Church. We found as we evaluated the health insurance that we still have not had a full year's experience with the group life and major medical insurance carried by the Pacific Mutual Life Insurance Company. We will be in consultation with them and the results of our consultation will be included in our supplementary report.

Your Insurance Committee has studied the matter of relief funds and the needs of retired ministers. We have discovered that ministers and their families participate in the Ministerial Relief Program of the Presbyterian Church in the United States on the basis of their relationship to the Presbyterian Church in the United States when they retire. We will endeavor to follow the same policy and it is the goal of your Insurance Committee to provide assistance to retired ministers and personnel of the National Presbyterian Church at a level comparable to that in other churches. In the early stages of our life as a denomination we will have limited needs for relief funds. Therefore, the Insurance Committee is recommending below that we set aside a great portion of our income for Ministerial Relief into a reserve fund for future needs.

The committee has also investigated and evaluated supplementary insurance programs such as additional term life insurance and accidental protection. It is the opinion of your committee that our ministers and personnel need to realize that the life insurance involved in our group life and major medical insurance and that which is carried as a part of the Annuity program is term life insurance. We believe that a balanced program for a minister and his family should include some ordinary life insurance which can be purchased by ministers at favorable rates from a number of insurance companies.

Your Insurance Committee is happy to report that our Group Life and Major Medical Insurance Program is in force with 239 employees being insured. We have been in close consultation with the insurance carrier, Pacific Mutual Life Insurance Company, and are happy to report that some general improve-

<a id="ga02-p146"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=146 printed_page=null -->

ments in our coverage have been effected by the company, and a careful evaluation of the experience of the company with this policy is being made.

We have had the insurance in force since August 1, 1973. The company needs three months beyond the first full year to make a good evaluation of their experience, which would be November 1, 1974. They have agreed to continue our present premium structure until February 1, 1975. This will enable us to better evaluate the policy's performance, and we hope to be able to continue the same premium rates through 1975.

General liberalizations which are now in effect and give improved benefits to our employees and their families include:

1) An unlimited number of days in an Intensive Care Unit will be provided, for which the insurance pays up to 2½ times the room rate maximum.

2) Pregnancy Coverage is extended to provide that complicated pregnancies (Caesarian Section, etc.) will be covered under the regular benefits of the policy.

3) Intermediate Care provided in a hospital will be paid under the Intensive Care provisions.

We are happy to report that our Insurance Carrier will provide health insurance for persons over 65 years of age, both for persons who are under Medicare and those who do not qualify for Medicare protection. The coverage for persons who have Medicare Parts A and B will cost $8.00 per person per month. The protection will be coordinated with Medicare, and in most cases will pay 100% of covered medical costs. For persons not protected by Medicare above age 65, the premiums will be the same as for those under age 65.

We have evaluated the $52.00 a day limit on the hospital room rate, and believe that an increase in this protection to $62.00 a day would be advisable. This increased protection will increase the cost $1.00 a month for the employee, or $3.00 a month for the employee and his family. The cost with this increased coverage will then be:

For the employee only — $22.00 a month
For the employee and his family — $48.00 a month.

We are recommending that this increased coverage begin November 1, 1974.

Because the health insurance has not been in effect long enough to have a full evaluation of our experience, and thus a basis for the best possible premiums for 1975, we are asking the General Assembly to authorize the Insurance Committee to continue negotiations with Pacific Mutual and other companies if necessary to provide the same or better protection at the most favorable rates available.

Respectfully submitted,
E. C. Cooley

## SUPPLEMENTARY REPORT OF THE INSURANCE COMMITTEE TO THE SECOND GENERAL ASSEMBLY, MACON, GEORGIA,
September 17, 1974

Your Insurance Committee is happy to report that our Group Life and Major Medical Insurance Program is in force with 239 employees being insured. We have been in close consultation with the insurance carrier, Pacific Mutual Life Insurance Company, and are happy to report that some general improvements in our coverage have been effected by the company, and a careful evaluation of the experience of the company with this policy is being made.

We have had the insurance in force since August 1, 1973. The company needs three months beyond the first full year to make a good evaluation of their experience, which would be November 1, 1974. They have agreed to continue our present premium structure until February 1, 1975. This will enable us to better evaluate the policy's performance, and we hope to be able to continue the same premium rates through 1975.

General liberalizations which are now in effect and give improved benefits to our employees and their families include:

1) An unlimited number of days in an Intensive Care Unit will be provided, for which the insurance pays up to 2½ times the room rate maximum.

<a id="ga02-p147"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=147 printed_page=null -->

2) Pregnancy Coverage is extended to provide that complicated pregnancies (Caesarian Section, etc) will be covered under the regular benefits of the policy.

3) Intermediate care provided in a hospital will be paid under the Intensive Care provisions.

We are happy to report that our Insurance Carrier will provide health insurance for persons over 65 years of age, both for persons who are under Medicare and those who do not qualify for Medicare protection. The coverage for persons who have Medicare Parts A and B will cost $8.00 per person per month. The protection will be coordinated with Medicare, and in most cases will pay 100% of covered medical costs. For persons not protected by Medicare above age 65, the premiums will be the same as for those under age 65.

We have evaluated the $52.00 a day limit on the hospital room rate, and believe that an increase in this protection to $62.00 a day would be advisable. This increased protection will increase the cost $1.00 a month for the employee, or $3.00 a month for the employee and his family. The cost with this increased coverage will then be:

For the employee only — $22.00 a month
For the employee and his family — $48.00 a month.

We are recommending that this increased coverage begin November 1, 1974.

Because the health insurance has not been in effect long enough to have a full evaluation of our experience, and thus a basis for the best possible premiums for 1975, we are asking the General Assembly to authorize the Insurance Committee to continue negotiations with Pacific Mutual and other companies if necessary to provide the same or better protection at the most favorable rates available.

Recommendations as adopted by the Assembly are found in 2-63, p. 52.

Respectfully submitted,

E. C. Cooley

# Appendix H

## REPORT OF THE INTER-CHURCH RELATIONS COMMITTEE

To: The Second General Assembly of the National Presbyterian Church
From: The Committee on Interchurch Relations
Fathers and Brethren:

Your Committee on Interchurch Relations has sought to function since the first General Assembly under the instructions embodied in the resolution of the Assembly covering its work.

Pursuant to these instructions, contacts were established with inter-church relations committees of the Orthodox Presbyterian Church, the Reformed Presbyterian Church Evangelical Synod, the Reformed Presbyterian Church of North America, and the Christian Reformed Church. These contacts led to an informal meeting of representatives of all these Churches in Jackson, Miss., February 27, 1974. In the absence of authority to commit the National Presbyterian Church to any formal relationship to any denomination, the meeting explored possibilities of fellowship only. Those present decided to convene the full membership of all committees involved at the Reformed Presbyterian Seminary, Pittsburgh, Pa., on October 25-26 for further discussions.

A resolution of the first General Assembly instructed the committee to "place suitable notices in appropriate religious publications throughout the United States extending the right hand of fellowship to all Christians of the Presbyterian and Reformed tradition who believe in the Scriptures of the Old and New Testaments as the Word of God written."

The following notice was drawn up and offered as a paid advertisement to The Banner, The Covenanter Witness, The Presbyterian Guardian, The (Christian Reformed) Outlook, The Reformed Record, and The Mandate. Cost of the advertising was borne by private subscription at no expense to the NPC:

The National Presbyterian Church extends the right hand of fellowship to all Christians who believe the Bible to be the inspired and inerrant Word of God; and who are committed to the Reformed faith and the presbyterial order. We earnestly solicit your prayers and pledge our cooperation, in all giving praise and glory to god. — By order of the 1st General Assembly, Birmingham, Ala., Dec. 6, 1973. (The address of the chairman followed.)

It has been the judgment of the committee that the instructions given by the Assembly did not encompass the establishment of fraternal relations with any other body at this time. Consequently, the committee did not feel at liberty to appoint fraternal delegates to attend other denominational meetings, nor issue invitations to representatives of other denominations to attend the Second General Assembly as fraternal delegates. However, we did feel that it would not exceed our authority to invite representatives of those Churches named above to attend the Assembly as visitors, and this we have done. Expressions received from those Churches have been uniformly cordial and hopeful of closer contacts.

We note that the first General Assembly (1861) of the Presbyterian Church of the Confederate States of America solicited fraternal correspondence with several denominations mentioned by name, expressly affirming its conviction that God would have the new denomination "most earnestly endeavor to draw closer the bonds of Christian intercourse and communion between all churches of like faith and order . . ." In a subsequent action, the second Assembly declared:

The General Assembly need scarcely reassert its earnest desire to cultivate friendly relations with churches professing the same doctrines and practicing the same polity. The unity of God's people is not only a reality, it is of the highest importance that this unity should be manifested to the world.

Respectfully submitted:
John Clark
William E. Hill Jr.
Donald McInnis
G. Aiken Taylor, Chm.
Morton H. Smith, Ex Officio

Recommendations as adopted by the Assembly are found in 2-100, pp. 74-76.

<a id="ga02-p147"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=149 printed_page=147 -->

# Appendix I

## REPORT OF COMMITTEE ON JUDICIAL BUSINESS

The Committee on Judicial Business selected Mr. Robert C. Cannada of Jackson, Mississippi, as its Chairman. There have been no formal meetings of the Committee since the December meeting of the General Assembly since no matters were referred to the Committee that required Committee action. The individual members of the Committee have been available to individuals, congregations and Presbyteries for advice and consultation in any matters pertaining to the National Presbyterian Church and through its chairman has been responsible for the adoption by the Board of Directors of the National Presbyterian Church of the following resolution:

### Legal Counsel

On motion duly made, seconded and unanimously carried, it was resolved that the action of the Committee on Administration in employing the Honorable Owen Page, an attorney of Savannah, Georgia, be and the same is hereby approved with the understanding that Mr. Page's legal services for which the National Presbyterian Church will be financially responsible shall be limited to the following:

1. Advice and consultation with the attorney representing a congregation or a proposed congregation; and
2. For rendering a “clearing-house” service to all interested congregations and their attorneys consisting of the furnishing of copies of any briefs, court decisions, legal memoranda, or other documents dealing in any way with the legal issues involved in the ownership of property by congregations and their efforts to withdraw from other denominations, together with a list showing the names and addresses of all attorneys representing any congregations that have affiliated with or have indicated a desire to affiliate with any Presbytery affiliated with or which shall have indicated a desire to affiliate with the National Presbyterian Church.

### Court Cases

On motion duly made, seconded and unanimously adopted, it was resolved that the National Presbyterian Church shall not as a denomination or through its attorney, take part in or enter its appearance in any court case involving any congregation without the express approval of and authorization by the Board of Directors.

### Legal Defense Funds

It was suggested that any and all gifts made to any Permanent Committee of the National Presbyterian Church designated for use in connection with any legal problems in which the National Presbyterian Church, any Presbytery affiliated therewith or any congregation affiliated therewith, shall, subject to the approval of the donor, be turned over to the Committee on Administration to be used by this Committee as authorized and directed by the Board of Directors.

Robert C. Cannada, Chairman

<a id="ga02-p150"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=150 printed_page=null -->

the Committee on Judicial Business has just been informed by the

National Presbyterian Church with respect to this particular m atter,
that the reappears to be a serious question concerning a conflict be
tween the use of the name National Presbyterian Church (a corpora
tion) by this denomination and the use of the name The National Presbyterian Church. Inc. by a local congregation in Washington, D. C. As a
result of this report the Committee on Judicial Business plans to submit
to the Directors of the National Presbyterian Church (a corporation)
at its scheduled meeting on September 16, 1974, the question of w hether
a recommendation should be made to the 1974 General Assembly to the
effect that the name of the denomination be changed. In addition, the
Committee on Judicial Business has requested the moderator to invite
the representatives of The National Presbyterian Church, Inc. to appear
before the meeting of the Directors of the National Presbyterian Church
(a corporation) at its September 16 meeting.

# Appendix J

## REPORT OF THE COMMITTEE FOR CHRISTIAN EDUCATION AND PUBLICATIONS TO THE SECOND GENERAL ASSEMBLY OF THE NATIONAL PRESBYTERIAN CHURCH

### INTRODUCTION

The National Presbyterian Church sincerely desires to order its ministry of the Word according to the principles set forth in the Great Commission of Jesus Christ.

In His Commission (Matthew 28: 18-20), our Lord clearly gives to His Church a three-fold mission: 1) To disciple men through fervent evangelism; 2) To unite newly discipled Christians with the visible Church; and 3) to teach people the whole counsel of God in order that they may in turn teach others, to the end that all the saints of God shall be equipped to do the work of the ministry.

Here we have Evangelism, Church-growth, and Education united into the one mission of the Church of Jesus Christ on earth. Your Committee for Christian Education and Publications believes that none of these elements may be omitted if the Church is to bear a vital testimony to God. Evangelism without education is fanaticism. Education without evangelism becomes dead orthodoxy. Either of these separated from the ministry of local churches is unscriptural and leads to discord and confusion within the body of believers.

The Church teaches because God has commanded her to do so. God is, God is personal. God has revealed Himself and has decreed that the objective, propositional truth of His revelation shall be the primary means by which men shall be identified and sanctified. The Church then, must communicate God's truth to men.

Both the message and the method have been given by God. The message is the whole counsel of God set forth in Holy Scripture, centering in the Person and Work of Jesus Christ. The method is by witnessing.

The Church witnesses by preaching and teaching the Truth. The Church "proclaims as a herald" God's revealed message. The Church "expounds the testimony of God," setting it forth in detail, explaining its meaning and significance for the Children of God.

Thus, the Church's mission is to witness to God by preaching and teaching the divinely revealed message given in Scripture.

The Committee for Christian Education and Publications has been charged with the glad responsibility of disciplining men according to the principles set forth in the Great Commission. The Committee understands its purpose as that of glorifying God through the exposition of the Word and its application to the whole of the life of the National Presbyterian Church.

Our purpose will be realized, God willing, as we faithfully pursue the following programs:

I. Curriculum Building
II. Publishing
III. Leadership Training
IV. Family and Service Ministries
V. Staff Enlistment and Training
VI. Cooperation with Sister Committees
VII. The Establishment of Adequate Office Facilities
VIII. Financial Undergirding

### I. CURRICULUM BUILDING

A. Joint Venture With Great Commission Publications

The First General Assembly instructed the Committee to "join with the Christian Education Committee of the Orthodox Presbyterian Church for the purpose of studying and recommending a joint administrative structure by means of which the two bodies may join resources and/or personnel for the development of curriculum materials suitable for use in the respective churches . . ." (Minutes, p. 58, =22).

<a id="ga02-p152"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=152 printed_page=null -->

Your Committee worked diligently with the sub-committee of the Orthodox Presbyterian Church's C. E. Committee in a study of the feasibility of such a project as outlined above. It became apparent that the goals and means of the two denominations' C. E. programs are eminently compatible. Theological views, commitment to the Great Commission, desire for a thoroughly Christian and Calvinistic curriculum — in these and every other area of thought and discussion the subcommittees found themselves in agreement. A professional evaluation and analysis of the project was made by the Main LaFrentz Company of Philadelphia to determine the validity of the program from a business standpoint.

The full C. E. Committees of the two denominations met in Atlanta early in May to study the results of the business analysis. After thorough discussion, your Committee recommends the establishment of the Joint Venture with the Christian Education Committee of the Orthodox Presbyterian Church, such venture to be based upon the principles of equal control of editorial policy and a share of financial support, with a view to making the Joint Venture the publishing arm of the two denominations.

B. Cooperative Efforts with Great Commission Publications

In cooperation with Great Commission Publications, your Committee is moving rapidly toward the development of a curriculum for adults. Writers are being secured to prepare a number of study guides, with teachers' helps, on such topics as the Cults, the Second Coming of Christ, Presbyterian Doctrine, the Ministry of the Holy Spirit, etc., etc. These are designed to be popular expositions of Christian truth for use in the Sunday School, Home Bible studies, Circles — wherever adults gather to study the Word of God.

Great Commission Publications is cooperating with the Christian Reformed Church in the production of a curriculum for pre-school children. Publication is slated for the Fall of 1974. Members of the Committee have observed at least one of the planning sessions for this new pre-school series. However, a complete evaluation will not be possible until late 1974.

The C. E. Staffs of the two denominations have worked closely together in various conferences, workshops, and committee meetings. Further close cooperation is intended to the end that the Christian Education resources and personnel of both denominations may increasingly share in joint efforts toward the effective exposition of the testimony of God.

C. Other Projects

1. Memory Work Notebook — The Memory Work Notebook, authorized by the First General Assembly, has been published and is available to individuals and churches at $1.00 per copy. Carefully graded for use with children and youth from age 3 to Senior High grade 12, the Notebook includes the full texts of Scripture references, the Child's Catechism, and the Westminster Shorter Catechism, plus hymns.

2. Family Devotional Booklet — Writers have been approached to compose sample daily devotionals, using the Child's Catechism as a thematic guide. The proposed booklet will include a devotional message for each day, an appropriate Scripture text, catechism reference, hymns, and prayer requests for the life of the NPC. It is hoped that publication will be in 1975.

3. The staff has thoroughly evaluated the pre-school curricula of several independent publishers, including David C. Cook, Gospel Light, and Scripture Press. Other curricula, books, and pieces of literature are being analyzed with the use of an evaluation instrument devised by the staff. It is hoped that this information may soon be made available to the churches.

4. The Committee and Staff are constantly evaluating the educational needs of the denomination and studying the possibilities of meeting those needs through sound, practical publications and programs. Large financial resources are necessary, however. Printing, writing, editing and publishing costs are staggering. The cost of paper alone has increased several times since January 1, 1974. If the Committee is to publish a full curriculum, either by itself, or in cooperation with another publisher, it must receive substantially better financial support in 1975 than it received in the first half of 1974.

<a id="ga02-p153"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=153 printed_page=null -->

## II. PUBLICATIONS

### A. Current Publications Available

1. BOOK OF CHURCH ORDER OF THE NPC ($1.25 each)
2. MINUTES of the First General Assembly — includes the full texts of the Westminster Confession of Faith, the Larger and Shorter Catechisms, the Book of Church Order, and the Statistics. ($3.00 each)
3. MEMORY WORK NOTEBOOK ($1.00)
4. “Continuing . . .” — monthly newsletter
5. “The NPC Ministers Through . . .” leaflet describing the work and budgetary needs of the four permanent committees
6. “The NPC Is . . .” — leaflet giving an introduction to the NPC
7. “Your C. E. Team” — leaflet introducing the staff and ministry of the C. E. Committee
8. WIC MANUAL for Local Churches ($ .75 each)
9. WIC MANUAL for Women in Presbytery ($ .25 each)
10. PHILIPPIANS — Circle or Home Bible Study Booklet ($ .50 each)
11. I PETER — Circle or Home Bible Study Booklet ($ .50 each)
12. ADDRESSES DELIVERED TO THE FIRST GENERAL ASSEMBLY ($1.00 each)
13. THE WESTMINSTER CONFESSION OF FAITH ($ .20 each)
14. “In Partnership with God” — Keyes — stewardship tract
15. MINUTES of the Advisory Convention ($ .50 each)
16. Certificates and Forms:
- Dismission and Reception of Members (local church) ($ .05 each)
- Membership (local church) ($ .05 each)
- Ordination of Ruling Elder/Deacon (local church) ($ .05 each)
- Dismissal of a Candidate (presbytery) ($ .05 each)
- Licensure (presbytery) ($ .05 each)
- Call to a Particular Ministry (presbytery, church) ($ .05 each)
- Dismission and Reception of a Minister (presbytery) ($ .05 each)
- Application for Membership (local church) ($ .05 each)
17. Church Offering Envelopes
18. Church Pledge Cards
19. Certificate for Memorization of Shorter Catechism (self-adhesive label for flyleaf of Bible)
20. Church Financial Record Forms
21. A WOMAN LOOKS AT THE CONFESSION — Patterson — Circle Study
22. THE SERMON ON THE MOUNT — Reed — Circle or Home Bible Study
23. WESTMINSTER CONFESSION OF FAITH (NPC) — Fall, 1974
24. WESTMINSTER SHORTER CATECHISM (personal size), Fall, 1974
25. BOOK OF CHURCH ORDER (second edition), Fall, 1974.

## III. LEADERSHIP TRAINING

The Committee recognizes that one of the greatest needs in the new denomination is thoroughly trained leadership, especially among the officers, church school workers and others who provide educational leadership in the churches.

Because of this, the C. E. staff has been encouraged to provide workshops and conference programs for local churches and presbyteries across the denomination. By June 1, the staff had trained more than 500 teachers and leaders in 14 churches and 6 presbyteries. Included with many of these training programs has been a complete evaluation of the total C. E. program of the local church, covering the use of space and equipment, personnel, curriculum materials, organization, etc., etc. Both lay and ministerial response has been enthusiastic, with many churches and presbyteries requesting “repeat performances” within the year. Workshops and/or “mini-conferences” have been scheduled for the Fall of this year in churches and presbyteries in Mississippi, Alabama, South Carolina, North Carolina, Tennessee, and Georgia.

## IV. FAMILY AND SERVICE MINISTRIES

### A. The Women in the Church

The First General Assembly approved and set in motion an effective and orderly program for women, which has resulted in eleven presbytery-wide or-

<a id="ga02-p154"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=154 printed_page=null -->

ganizations for fellowship and training. Attendance at the organizational meetings has been unusually high, with a splendid degree of enthusiasm and appreciation expressed.

Following the Suggested Manual, Women in the Church groups have been established in almost every congregation in the denomination. Bible study, fellowship, and service are emphasized as the women, under the Session, strive to fashion a program that is truly Biblical.

The WIC advisory Subcommittee has worked closely with the Committee for Christian Education and has submitted all its plans and proposals to this Committee for action. A workshop was held in Montgomery for the presidents of the presbyterial organizations. During this time the Scriptural role of Women in the Church was stressed and emphasis was given to the functions of Service and Support within the life of the local church. The WIC Consultant has traveled to a number of presbyteries and local churches to assist with the organization of new groups along Assembly-approved guidelines.

The first annual Women's Love Gift, received in February and designated to the work of the four permanent committees, totaled approximately $18,000.00.

Two additional study guides for the use of women in circles are proposed for the Fall: "A Woman Looks at the Confession", by Mrs. D. G. Patterson, and "The Sermon on the Mount," by the Rev. Gordon Reed.

B. Men of Covenant

Local churches and presbyteries have organized Men of Covenant groups, but structure and program are still indefinite. Your Committee, working closely with Men in Action through its Coordinator, is considering a men's program that will be inspirational, practical, and a positive force for the enlistment and training of men for Christian service.

A pilot program in a church in South Florida is providing valuable insights into the needs and opportunities for an effective men's ministry. Continuing evaluation and analysis will lead to published material in the late Fall or early Winter, the Lord willing.

C. Family Ministries

The Committee is studying the feasibility of annual family conferences in the NPC which will at once bring together the denomination's constituency and provide individualized activities for men, women, and youth, but in a "family together" setting.

With this concept in mind, the Committee delayed plans for annual men's, women's and youth assemblies in 1974-1975.

### V. STAFF ENLISTMENT AND TRAINING

The activities of the Committee have been hampered by limited staff and facilities, but the situation improved radically in June with the addition of a third secretary and a move into new and larger quarters.

The new secretary brings to four the number of secretaries and clerical assistants who are serving the Coordinator, the Assistant to the Coordinator, the WIC Consultant (part time), and two DCE Consultants.

All staff members are encouraged to continue to increase their skills and experience through inservice training and study programs. Every staff member attended at least one training conference or seminar in the first half of 1974.

VI. OFFICE FACILITIES AND EQUIPMENT

Until June 6, the C. E. offices were housed in small, inadequately equipped quarters in downtown Montgomery, Alabama. On that date, a move was made to a new office building on the outskirts of the city. The first floor of the building was designed principally for the C. E. offices and provides space for five staff offices, a secretarial "pool" office, a conference room, bulk and inventory storage rooms, an equipment room, a small kitchen and lounge, and rest rooms.

The new space enables the staff to truly organize the office for the first time. Proper storage for inventory and records is available, plus ample room for staff functions.

<a id="ga02-p155"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=2 pdf_page=155 printed_page=null -->

## VII. COOPERATION WITH DENOMINATION COMMITTEES

The Committee is eager to cooperate fully with the other permanent Committees and the Board of Directors of the NPC.

Representatives have met twice with the Board of Directors and with representatives of the other committees on several occasions to assist in the important function of coordinating the total ministry of the denomination.

This Committee is providing a mailing service for all the Committees, which involves the compilation of a complete mailing list and the procurement of the necessary machines and personnel to expedite direct mailing service to as many members of the denomination as possible. By June 1, the mailing list included almost 10,000 names, consisting mainly of ministers, clerks of Session, elders and deacons.

Perhaps the greatest contribution to date is the publication of the denomination’s monthly newsletter, *Continuing*. The C. E. staff has performed all the functions of publication for the newsletter — gathering of news, writing, editing, lay-outs, printing and mailing — in the office. Copies have been sent in quantity packages (about 1/3 of the membership of a congregation) to every NPC church. A new smaller format, adopted in June, makes it possible for the newsletter to be inserted in the weekly bulletins of churches.

## VIII. FINANCIAL FOUNDATIONS

Unfortunately, though many churches have given generously to support the work of the denomination, all the Committees have been forced to curtail some of their activities due to insufficient funds.

The C. E. Committee is no exception. Due to a lack of funds, certain projects have been delayed, the hiring of some personnel has been postponed, and various pieces of equipment and some furnishings have not been purchased. As of June 1, funds have been received in sufficient quantity to keep the Committee solvent, but the total amount received represents only about one-half the amount needed to do the work approved by the First General Assembly.

Though the Committee is sincerely grateful to God for the many individuals and churches which have faithfully and generously contributed to the ministry of Christian Education, it cannot but urge greater commitment in the future. We are confident that God is going to use the NPC as an instrument of revival and renewal of the Christian faith. But this means that every individual and every church must examine his relationship to the living Lord and and to his denomination, and re-evaluate his priorities for the stewardship of money.

## IX. SUGGESTIONS FOR ADULT STUDY CLASSES AND/OR GROUPS

The Committee’s recommendation of these books does not imply endorsement of everything in the books, nor of any other works by these authors.

- **InterVarsity Press (IVP) 130 North Wells, Chicago, IL 60606**

- 25 basic studies
- **BASIC CHRISTIANITY — John Scott**
- Comes with study guide and excellent text.

- Old Testament character studies geared for 19 weeks of study.
- **GOD’S FRIEND — Alan Stibbs**
- Studies in the life of Abraham.
- **HOW TO GIVE AWAY YOUR FAITH — Paul Little**
- A Biblical, relevant, practical, and realistic book, with emphasis given to instructing the student how to share his faith. 9 chapters (could easily be made into 13 lessons.) Study guide available.
- **DISCUSSIONS ON THE LIFE OF JESUS CHRIST — 12 Studies.**
- For students who want to know more about the person and work of Jesus Christ.
- **DISCOVERING THE GOSPEL OF MARK**
- 16 Studies on the Gospel of Mark.
- **ACTS “YOUNG CHRISTIANS IN A HOSTILE WORLD”**
- 25 Brief Studies. As with all IVP study guides, these give brief comments, plus good discussion questions. Use this for student text; a good commentary on Acts for the teacher.

PHILIPPIANS J— J. Patterson

Circle Bible studies.

A WOMAN LOOKS AT THE CONFESSION — J. Patterson

A challenging doctrinal study of the rich heritage in the Reformed faith. For circles, but suitable for any group. This with Williamson will be excellent for studies in the Westminster Confession of Faith.
